Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Ensuring Textual Accuracy: Al-Aqta'i's Approach to Manuscripts
Description of the author's textual correction methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Aqta'i's method for correcting errors in manuscript copies and explain the importance of textual criticism in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
A reliable commentary depends on a correct text; al-Aqta'i corrected errors from multiple manuscripts.

This lesson focuses on al-Aqta'i's role as a textual critic. In the conclusion of his commentary, he mentions that he found errors in many copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and corrected them according to the Hanafi madhhab. This reflects the high standard of accuracy expected in the Hanafi tradition. The lesson also notes that the commentary was praised by later scholars like al-Kawthari as 'the best of commentaries.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Al-Aqta'i found errors in most manuscript copies of the Mukhtasar he consulted.
These errors were attributed to copyists (nasikh).
2
State his correction method
He corrected all errors according to what the Hanafi madhhab requires (ما يقتضيه مذهب أصحابنا).
This means he did not just rely on any manuscript, but on the established rulings of the school.
3
Appreciate the scholarly impact
By ensuring a correct text, al-Aqta'i made his commentary a reliable source for later scholars.
Al-Kawthari's praise confirms its value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
وفيما يلي نص مقدمة شرحه الكبير، حيث قال: ... ذكرتُم ـ وفقنا الله وإياكم إلى الصالح والرشاد ـ حاجتكم إلى شرح المختصر الذي عَمِله شيخنا أبو الحسين أحمـد بـن محمـد بـن جعفر القدوري شرحاً لا يخرج عن حد الاختصار، وأنكم رأيـتـم مـا كنتُ ابتدأت به من شرحه للشريف السعيد ضياء الشرف ذي المنصبين أبي الحسين عبد الله بن المطهر بن الحسين بن داود، الناصر لدين الله سبحانه وتعالى، فوجدتموه في غاية الاختصار.
وسألتُم أن أبسط القول فيه بعض البسط، وأذكر في كل مسألة من مسائل الكتاب ما يُعتمد عليه، وبه يُستخرج الجواب عن أخواتها من المسائل، وأن ألحق في كل موضع ما يُحتاج إليه من المسائل الظاهرة التي لا يُستغنى عن معرفتها، وما يكون فيه إيضاح لغيرها، قدراً لا يطول به الكتاب، ويعتدل به أوله وآخره، وأن أقتصر من ذكر اختلاف الناس على ما جرت به العادة بذكره في وقتنا.
فأجبتكم إلى ذلك، مستعيناً بالله عز وجل في جميع ما أقصده، وراغباً إليه جلت عظمته في التوفيق والعصمة في كـل مـا آتي وأذَرُ، وأن يجعل ما أتوخاه من ذلك له خالصاً، وأن ينفع الناظر فيه به ، وهو عزّ اسمه ولي الإجابة بمنه وكرمه). اهـ
ويقع هذا الشرح في مجلدين، في نحو ٣٠٠ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٣ سطراً، حسب نسخة الظاهرية بدمشق، التي تم نسخها سنة ٨٤٧هـ.
وتوجد من هذا الشرح نسخ عديدة، ينظر لهـا الفهرس الشامل للتراث العربي الإسلامي المخطوط (١).
وقد سجل الكتاب لتحقيقه في رسائل جامعية في جامعة الإمام محمد بن سعود في الرياض، وتمت مناقشة الرسالة الأولى منه، بتحقيق الأخ الكريم الأستاذ إبراهيم أكبر، ونال بها درجة الماجستير بمرتبة الامتياز مع التوصية بالطبع.
وقد قال العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله عن هذا الشرح «بأنه أحسن شروح المختصر » (٢).
وقد توسع الأقطع في هذا الشرح في ذكر الأدلة، كما أكثر من التفريع على المسائل، مع ذكره لخلاف الإمام مالك والشافعي، ومناقشة الأدلة، مع الأخذ والرد.
كما اهتم المؤلف بذكر فوارق نُسَخ مختصر القدوري التي وقـف عليها، وبين الصواب منها ، كما صرح بهذا في خاتمة شرحه، فقال: «وقد وجدتُ في أكثر نسخ الأصل خللاً في بعض المسائل، وهـو من الناسخ، وقد أصلحت جميع ذلك على ما يقتضيه مذهب أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى». اهـ
وممن كان يحفظ شرح الأقطع هذا، مـا ذكـره القرشي في الجواهر المضية، في ترجمة محمد بن يحيى بـن مـسـلـم القاضي خيري.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Below is the text of the introduction to his large commentary, where he said: ... You mentioned – may Allah guide us and you to righteousness and good conduct – your need for a commentary on the Mukhtasar compiled by our Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Quduri, a commentary that does not exceed the limits of conciseness, and that you saw what I had initially begun of his commentary for the noble and happy Diya' al-Sharaf, holder of two positions, Abu al-Husayn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn ibn Dawud, the supporter of the religion of Allah, and you found it extremely concise. And you asked that I expand the discussion somewhat, and mention in each issue of the book's issues what is relied upon, and by which the answer to similar issues can be derived, and that I append in each place the apparent issues that are needed and whose knowledge cannot be dispensed with, and what clarifies others, to an extent that does not lengthen the book, and makes its beginning and end balanced, and that I restrict the mention of disagreement among people to what is customary to mention in our time. So I responded to you, seeking help from Allah in all that I intend, and desiring His success and protection in all that I do and leave, and that He make what I aim for sincere to Him, and benefit the reader thereby. And He is worthy of response by His favor and generosity. End quote. This commentary is in two volumes, about 300 folios, each page 23 lines, according to the Zahiriyya copy in Damascus, copied in 847 AH. There are many copies of this commentary; see the Comprehensive Index of Arabic Islamic Manuscripts (1). The book has been registered for academic theses at Imam Muhammad ibn Sa'ud University in Riyadh, and the first thesis was discussed, edited by the brother Professor Ibrahim Akbar, who obtained a master's degree with distinction and recommendation for publication. The scholar al-Kawthari said about this commentary: 'It is the best of the commentaries on the Mukhtasar.' Al-Aqta'i expanded in this commentary in citing evidences, and abundantly branched out issues, while mentioning the disagreement of Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, and discussing evidences with give and take. The author also paid attention to mentioning the differences among copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri that he came across, and clarified the correct among them, as he stated in the conclusion of his commentary: 'And I found in most copies of the original errors in some issues, and that is from the copyist, and I corrected all of that according to the requirements of the madhhab of our companions, may Allah have mercy on them.' End quote. Among those who memorized this commentary of al-Aqta'i, as mentioned by al-Qurashi in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, in the biography of Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Muslim al-Qadi Khayri.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is front matter from a modern study on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, specifically introducing the large commentary by Izz al-Din al-Aqta'i. It opens with the chapter heading 'Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and then provides the text of the author's own introduction to his expanded commentary. In that introduction, al-Aqta'i explains that his readers requested a commentary that, while expanding on the original concise work, remains focused and practical. He commits to mentioning the relied-upon position in each issue, enabling the derivation of rulings for similar cases, and to include necessary apparent issues without making the book too long. He also limits mention of scholarly disagreement to what is customary. He then describes the physical description of the manuscript (two volumes, ~300 folios, 23 lines per page) and notes that it was copied in 847 AH. The passage goes on to quote later scholars, such as al-Kawthari, praising this commentary as the best. It highlights the commentary's features: extensive citation of evidence, branching out of issues, engagement with Maliki and Shafi'i positions, and critical correction of discrepancies in manuscript copies of the Mukhtasar. Finally, it mentions that the commentary was memorized by some, as recorded in biographical works.

Key Terms
النسخة (al-Nuskha): Manuscript copy of a work.
الناسخ (al-Nasikh): Copyist; the person who manually copied the manuscript.
الإصلاح (al-Islah): Correction; al-Aqta'i corrected errors according to the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How did al-Aqta'i correct errors in manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) By selecting the oldest manuscript
B) By following the majority of manuscripts
C) By applying the requirements of the Hanafi madhhab
D) By relying on his personal opinion

Key Takeaway
Al-Aqta'i's textual criticism shows the Hanafi emphasis on accurate transmission and conformity to madhhab principles.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Biographical Sketches of Hanafi Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical description of two Hanafi commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two major Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, state their authors and key characteristics, and explain their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Aqta's commentary and Ibn Qutlubugha's Taqrib al-Gharib are essential tools for understanding and verifying Hanafi fiqh rulings.

This lesson introduces you to two important Hanafi commentaries that build upon the foundational Mukhtasar al-Quduri. You will learn about the works of Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Aqta' and the later contribution of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, both of which serve different but complementary purposes in the study of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the works
Locate the two primary works discussed: Sharh al-Aqta' (the larger commentary) and its abridgment al-Muqni', and Taqrib al-Gharib (a commentary on obscure hadiths found in Sharh al-Aqta').
2
Note the authors and dates
Observe that Sharh al-Aqta' is by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), a direct student of al-Quduri, while Taqrib al-Gharib is by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), a later Hanafi scholar.
The gap of four centuries between the two works shows the enduring value of al-Aqta's commentary.
3
Recognize the methodology
Al-Aqta's commentary is known for expanding proofs (adilla), deriving subsidiary rulings (tafri'), discussing differences with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, and correcting manuscript variants of the Mukhtasar.
Al-Kawthari praised it as 'the best of the commentaries on the Mukhtasar'.
4
Understand the purpose of each work
Al-Muqni' is a concise version of al-Aqta's larger commentary, intended for learners who needed a more accessible reference. Taqrib al-Gharib specifically explains the obscure hadiths cited in Sharh al-Aqta', showing the interconnection between fiqh and hadith.
Ibn Qutlubugha's work is a specialized tool for verifying hadith evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Appreciate the chain of transmission
The passage notes that Qadi al-Maragi (d. 563 AH) had memorized Sharh al-Aqta', indicating the work's centrality in early Hanafi education. This memorization anchor tradition underscores the importance of these texts.
This shows how later scholars preserved and transmitted the school's core commentaries.

الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري للتراث العربي الإسلامي المخطوط (۱).
وقد سجل الكتاب لتحقيقه في رسائل جامعية في جامعة الإمام محمد بن سعود في الرياض، وتمت مناقشة الرسالة الأولى منه، بتحقيق الأخ الكريم الأستاذ إبراهيم أكبر، ونال بها درجة الماجستير بمرتبة الامتياز مع التوصية بالطبع.
وقد قال العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله عن هذا الشرح «بأنه أحسن شروح المختصر » (٢).
وقد توسع الأقطع في هذا الشرح في ذكر الأدلة، كما أكثر من التفريع على المسائل، مع ذكره لخلاف الإمام مالك والشافعي، ومناقشة الأدلة، مع الأخذ والرد.
كما اهتم المؤلف بذكر فوارق نُسَخ مختصر القدوري التي وقف عليها، وبين الصواب منها ، كما صرح بهذا في خاتمة شرحه، فقال: «وقد وجدتُ في أكثر نسخ الأصل خللاً في بعض المسائل، وهو من الناسخ، وقد أصلحت جميع ذلك على ما يقتضيه مذهب أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى». اهـ
وممن كان يحفظ شرح الأقطع هذا، ما ذكره القرشي في الجواهر المضية، في ترجمة محمد بن يحيى بن مسلم القاضي المراغي، المتوفى سنة ٥٦٣ هـ ، قال : كان من محافيظه كتاب الأقطع في شرح القدوري. اهـ
المقنع شرح مختصر القدوري (الشرح الصغير). للأقطع : أحمد بن محمد تلميذ القدوري، المتوفى سنة ٤٧٤هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد وجد عنوان هذا الشرح بهذا الاسم: (المقنع): على صفحة العنوان في النسخ الخطية له.
ومن هذا الشرح المختصر نسخة في مركز البحث العلمي بمكة المكرمة، برقم ٢٦٣ ، في (۱۷۳) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (٢١) سطراً، وتاريخ نسخها سنة ٩٦٦هـ ، مصوّرة عن النسخة الأزهرية بالقاهرة، برقم ٢١٤٧.
وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه ما يلي: «الحمد لله حق حمده، فقد كثُرت رغبة المتعلمين في معرفة هذا المختصر في الفقه الذي جَمَعـه أبو الحسين القدوري، لصغر حجمه، وعظم فائدته، فأشرتُ في كل مسألة إلى نكتة لطيفة ...... الخ»
تقريب الغريب، وهو شرح لغريب أحاديث شرح الأقطع.
للإمام العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا المتوفى سنة ٨٧٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri from the Manuscript Arab-Islamic Heritage (1).
The book has been registered for editing in university theses at Imam Muhammad bin Saud University in Riyadh, and the first thesis was discussed, edited by the noble brother Professor Ibrahim Akbar, who earned a Master's degree with distinction and a recommendation for publication.
Al-Allama al-Kawthari, may Allah have mercy on him, said about this commentary: 'It is the best of the commentaries on the Mukhtasar.' (2)
Al-Aqta' expanded in this commentary in mentioning proofs, and he extensively branched out into subsidiary issues, mentioning the differences of Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, discussing proofs, with give and take.
The author also paid attention to noting the textual variants of Mukhtasar al-Quduri that he came across, and clarified the correct version, as he stated in the conclusion of his commentary: 'I found errors in most copies of the original in some issues, due to the copyist, and I corrected all of that according to what the school of our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, requires.' End quote.
Among those who memorized this commentary of al-Aqta' was what al-Qurashi mentioned in al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, in the biography of Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Muslim al-Qadi al-Maragh, who died in 563 AH. He said: 'Among his memorized works was the book of al-Aqta' on the commentary of al-Quduri.' End quote.
Al-Muqni': A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the small commentary). By al-Aqta': Ahmad ibn Muhammad, student of al-Quduri, died in 474 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
The title of this commentary is found as (al-Muqni') on the title page of its manuscript copies.
A copy of this abridged commentary is in the Center for Scientific Research in Mecca, number 263, in 173 folios, with 21 lines per page, copied in 966 AH, photographed from the Azhar copy in Cairo, number 2147.
In its author's introduction it includes: 'Praise be to Allah, the praise He deserves. The desire of learners to know this abridged work on fiqh compiled by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, due to its small size and great benefit, has increased. So I have pointed out in each issue a subtle point... etc.'
Taqrib al-Gharib: A commentary on the obscure hadiths of Sharh al-Aqta'.
By al-Imam al-Allama Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, died in 879 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical section from the introduction of a book on Hanafi fiqh, discussing the commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It begins by noting that the book (likely al-Aqta's commentary) has been edited as a master's thesis at Imam Muhammad bin Saud University, with commendation. Al-Kawthari praised it as the best commentary on the Mukhtasar. The passage describes al-Aqta's methodology: he expanded on proofs, extensively derived subsidiary rulings (tafri'), mentioned the differences of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, and discussed proofs with critical analysis. He also carefully noted manuscript variants and corrected errors according to the Hanafi school. The passage quotes al-Qurashi's al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, stating that Qadi al-Maragi (d. 563 AH) had memorized al-Aqta's work. Then it introduces al-Muqni', a concise commentary by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), a student of al-Quduri. The title al-Muqni' is found on manuscript title pages. One manuscript is described: 173 folios, 21 lines per page, copied in 966 AH, from the Azhar library. The author's preface is quoted, emphasizing the benefit of the Mukhtasar and his aim to add subtle points. Finally, it mentions Taqrib al-Gharib by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), a commentary on the obscure hadiths in al-Aqta's Sharh. This passage gives biographical context for the Hanafi tradition of commentary writing.

Key Terms
شرح الأقطع (Sharh al-Aqta'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), known for its extensive proofs and critical discussion of differences with other schools.
المقنع (al-Muqni'): A concise commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by the same author, al-Aqta', also titled 'al-Sharh al-Saghir' (the small commentary).
تقريب الغريب (Taqrib al-Gharib): A commentary by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH) explaining the obscure hadiths found in Sharh al-Aqta'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which scholar praised al-Aqta's commentary as 'the best of the commentaries on the Mukhtasar'?
A) Al-Qurashi
B) Al-Kawthari
C) Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
D) Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Maragi

Key Takeaway
Al-Aqta's detailed commentary and its abridgment, along with Ibn Qutlubugha's specialized hadith work, form a layered system of Hanafi fiqh study rooted in the Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Identifying the Author of Mushkilat al-Quduri
Correcting authorship and quoting the preface of a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct author of Mushkilat al-Quduri and explain the evidence for this correction using biographical sources.

Core Idea
The author of Mushkilat al-Quduri is Ahmad al-Razi, not Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari.

This lesson examines a common mistake in attributing the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. We will learn how the editor corrects this error using manuscript evidence and biographical works, and then read the author's own preface to understand the purpose of the work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two authors mentioned
The passage contrasts two names: Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari and Ahmad al-Razi. Note which one is the correct author and why the other is mistakenly attributed.
The editor explicitly states the attribution to al-Kardari is an addition from an unrelated biography.
2
Understand the correction
The editor supports al-Baghdadi's view in Hadiyyat al-'Arifin and notes that the name of the father dropped from Taj al-Tarajim.
This shows the importance of consulting multiple sources for authorship verification.
3
Analyze the preface
Read al-Razi's preface: he wrote the book at the request of a dear friend to explain difficult points of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, praising its conciseness and usefulness.
The preface reveals the purpose and the intended readership of the commentary.
4
Note the manuscript evidence
The text lists several manuscript copies in Istanbul libraries under various titles, confirming the work's circulation.
Different titles (e.g., Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri) refer to the same commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣٧٠
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
وقوله : «شمس الأئمة الكردري، المتوفى سنة ٦٤٢هـ : فهذه زيادة من متعلقات ترجمة محمد بن عبد الستار بن محمد العمادي شمس الأئمة الكردري، المتوفى سنة ٦٤٢هـ، كما هو في تاج التراجم، وغيره ، وليس لها صلة بترجمة الرازي هذا
وما ذكره البغدادي في هدية العارفين هو الصواب ؛ لموافقته لما جاء في مقدمة الكتاب (مخطوط)، وقد سقط اسم الأب: (محمد) من تاج التراجم وكشف الظنون، والله أعلم.
وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه (۲):
«قال أحمد بن محمد بن المظفر بن المختار الرازي: أما بعد: قد سألني من كان مني بمكان من المحبة، وكان أعزّ علي من سائر الأحبة، بل كان بمنزلة رأسي من جسدي، وروحي من بدني، أن أشرح له مشكلات كتاب (المختصر)، المنسوب إلى الفقيه أبي أحمد بن محمد القدوري البغدادي رحمه الله ، فقد كثر فيه خَلْطُ المتكلّفين وخبطهم ، وعَزَبَ عن بعض معانيه فهمهم وضبطهم. وهو ـ أي مختصر القدوري - كتاب طَنَّـت به الآفاق، وتناقله الرفاق، واحتاج إليه الحاضر والبادي كما يحتاج إلى الزلال الصادي)، وأكب على دراسته المحتدي والمبتدي، والب ـ أي لزم وأقام ـ على قراءته المقتدى والمقتدي ؛ لما فيه من حسن الإيجاز، ولطف الإعجاز وجودة المعاني ومتانة المباني، وكثرة المسائل المحتاج إليها، والألفاظ الفصيحة المتفق عليها، وكونه مباركاً على طالبيه، ميموناً على قارئيه وضابطيه والناس أعقل من أن يمدحوا ما لم يروا عنده آثار إحسان. فامتثلتُ لحكم الذي ملك عنان قوادي، وألقيتُ إليه زمام طوعي وانقيادي، وأوضحت من ذلك ما أهمله الشارحون في كتبهم، وأغفله المصنفون في تصانيفهم، لا يصعب على مقتبس ومستوضح، ولا ينغلق على كل مستفتح، موصياً لهم بصالح الدعاء، وستر عيب وحسن إغضاء، والله ولي التوفيق». اهـ
وللكتاب نُسَخ عديدة، بعناوين مختلفة متقاربة، في مكتبات اسطنبول ، ففي مكتبة جار الله نسخة برقم باسم : : مشكلات القدوري، كتبت سنة ٨٣٨هـ. في (٢٤٥) ورقة،
وفي مكتبة لاله لي (١١٦٠ ، في (۱۲۱) ورقة باسم شرح مشكلات القدوري، وفي جورلولي علي باشا ۲۱۱، في (۳۱۹) ورقة
باسم: شرح مختصر القدوري.
(1) أي العطشان والصادي من الصدى وهو العطش. (مختار الصحاح). (٢) ينظر معجم المخطوطات الموجودة في مكتبات استانبول وأناطولي ٢١١/١ .(٦٢٨)
370
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
And his statement: “Shams al-A’immah al-Kardari, died 642 AH”: this is an addition from the biography of Muhammad ibn ‘Abd al-Sattar ibn Muhammad al-‘Imadi Shams al-A’immah al-Kardari, died 642 AH, as in Taj al-Tarajim and others, and it has no connection to the biography of al-Razi.
What al-Baghdadi mentioned in Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin is correct because it agrees with what came in the introduction of the manuscript, and the name of the father (Muhammad) has dropped from Taj al-Tarajim and Kashf al-Zunun, and Allah knows best.
And it came in the introduction of its author:
“Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn al-Mukhtar al-Razi said: To proceed: One who held a place of love with me, and was dearer to me than all other beloved ones, nay, was like my head to my body and my soul to my body, asked me to explain for him the difficult passages of the book (al-Mukhtasar), attributed to the jurist Abu Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him. For the confused and mistaken interpretations of the pretentious have increased in it, and their understanding and grasp have failed to reach some of its meanings. And it—i.e. Mukhtasar al-Quduri—is a book that has resounded through the horizons, been passed from hand to hand by companions, and been needed by the settled and the nomad just as one needs cool sweet water. The beginner and the advanced have applied themselves to studying it, and the leader and follower have devoted themselves to reading it; because of its good conciseness, subtle eloquence, quality of meanings, firmness of structure, abundance of needed issues, eloquent agreed-upon expressions, and its being blessed for its seekers, fortunate for its readers and memorizers. And people are too intelligent to praise what they have not seen signs of goodness in. So I complied with the command of the one who held the reins of my heart, and I surrendered to him the reins of my obedience and submission, and I clarified from that what the commentators had neglected in their books and what the authors had omitted in their works—nothing difficult for a student or inquirer, nor obscure for any beginner—advising them for righteous prayer, covering of faults, and good overlooking. And Allah is the Grantor of success.” End.
And the book has many copies, with different but similar titles, in the libraries of Istanbul. In the Jarallah Library there is a copy numbered as “Mushkilat al-Quduri”, written in 838 AH, in 245 folios.
And in the Laleli Library (1160, in 121 folios) with the title “Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri”, and in Görülöli Ali Pasha (211, in 319 folios) with the title “Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri”.
(1) i.e., the thirsty, and al-sadi is from al-sada meaning thirst. (Mukhtar al-Sihah). (2) See Mu’jam al-Makhtutat al-Mawjudah fi Maktabat Istanbul wa Anatolia 1/211 (628).
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a biographical correction and a preface excerpt from the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The text begins by correcting a common mistake: the author of the commentary known as ‘Mushkilat al-Quduri’ is Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar al-Razi, not Shams al-A’immah al-Kardari. The editor notes that the attribution to al-Kardari is an addition from the biography of Muhammad ibn ‘Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari and is unrelated to al-Razi. He supports the correct view of al-Baghdadi in Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin, noting that the name of the father (Muhammad) dropped out in some sources. Then the author, al-Razi, states in his preface that he wrote the book at the request of a dear friend to explain the difficult points of al-Quduri’s Mukhtasar. He praises the Mukhtasar for its conciseness, eloquence, and usefulness. The author emphasizes that he has clarified matters that other commentators neglected. Finally, the text lists several manuscript copies in Istanbul libraries under various titles.

Key Terms
شمس الأئمة الكردري (Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari): A title attributed to Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Imadi, mistakenly thought to be the author of Mushkilat al-Quduri.
مشكلات القدوري (Mushkilat al-Quduri): The title of the commentary by Ahmad al-Razi on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining its difficult points.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Abu Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a core Hanafi text.
تاج التراجم (Taj al-Tarajim): A biographical work by the Hanafi scholar Ibn al-Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar al-Razi

D) Al-Baghdadi

Key Takeaway
The correct author of Mushkilat al-Quduri is Ahmad al-Razi, and the attribution to Shams al-A'immah al-Kardari is an error based on a weak transmission.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Its Commentaries
Front-matter description of Mukhtasar al-Quduri's merits and its commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain why this text is considered foundational in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study; its many commentaries testify to its authority.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by al-Maydani praises the conciseness and utility of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and lists several of its commentaries and manuscripts. Understanding the reception of this text helps us appreciate the tradition of Hanafi scholarship and the importance of authoritative texts in legal study.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the praise
Identify the qualities attributed to Mukhtasar al-Quduri: conciseness, eloquence, sound meanings, abundance of needed issues, and blessedness for students.
These qualities explain why the text became a primary reference.
2
List the commentaries
Note the three manuscripts: 'Mushkilat al-Quduri' (Jarallah Library), 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri' (Lale Li Library), and 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' (Gururli Ali Pasha). Also note the named commentary 'Multamas al-Ikhwan' by al-Ghaznawi.
The variety of titles indicates the text’s widespread study.
3
Assess the evidence of authority
Understand that the existence of multiple copies and commentaries, especially those cited by later authorities like al-Zayla'i, establishes the text's authoritative status in the Hanafi school.
This demonstrates how a text gains traction through scholarly consensus.

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
الصادي)، وأكب على دراسته المحتدي والمبتدي، والب ـ أي لــزم وأقام ـ على قراءته المقتدى والمقتدي ؛ لما فيه من حسن الإيجاز، ولطف الإعجاز وجودة المعاني ومتانة المباني، وكثرة المسائل المحتاج إليها، والألفاظ الفصيحة المتفق عليها، وكونه مباركاً على طالبيه، ميموناً على قارئيه وضابطيه والناس أعقل من أن يمدحوا ما لم يروا عنده آثار إحسان. فامتثلتُ لحكم الذي مَلَك عِنان قوادي، وألقيتُ إليه زمام طوعي وانقيادي، وأوضحت من ذلك ما أهمله الشارحون في كتبهم، وأغفله المصنفون في تصانيفهم، لا يصعب على مقتبس ومستوضح، ولا ينغلق على كل مستفتح، موصياً لهم بصالح الدعاء، وستر عيب وحسن إغضاء، والله ولي التوفيق». اهـ
وللكتاب نُسَخ عديدة، بعناوين مختلفة متقاربة، في مكتبات اسطنبول، ففي مكتبة جار الله نسخة برقم باسم : : مشكلات القدوري، كتبت سنة ٨٣٨هـ. في (٢٤٥) ورقة، وفي مكتبة لاله لي (١١٦٠)، في (١٢١) ورقة باسم شرح مشكلات القدوري، وفي جورلولي علي باشا ٢١١، في (٣١٩) ورقة باسم: شرح مختصر القدوري.
وأنبه هنا إلى أني صورت نسخة من مخطوطة كتب على صفحة عنوانها: (المشكلات من شرح المختصر)، وليس عليها ذكر اسم مؤلفها، وحين ذكرها أصحاب الفهرس الشامل، ذكروا أنها لمؤلف مجهول. وبمطالعتي لها لم يظهر أي شيء يفيد عن مؤلفها. وهي مصورة من المكتبة الأزهرية بالقاهرة ٢٢٥٣١، تقع في (٨٠) ورقة، كتبت سنة ٨٧٧هـ. وهي حاشية مختصرة على مواضع عديدة من المختصر، تنتهي بآخر تعليقة منها على كتاب الجهاد والسير من مختصر القدوري، ثم كتب: (تمت هذه المشكلات). اهـ
مُلْتَمَسُ الإخوان ومُبْتَغَى الأحباب والخـلان (شرح مختصر القدوري). لأبي المعالي عبد الرب بن منصور الغزنوي، المتوفى في حدود سنة ٥٠٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. ويقع الكتاب في مجلدين، ونقل عنه أئمة المذهب، كالزيلعي في تبيين الحقائق، والعلامة قاسم في تصحيح القدوري، وغيرهما.
Third Chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. ...the thirsty one, and both the beginner and the advanced devoted themselves to studying it—indeed, they remained constant in reading it, the one who is followed and the one who follows—because of its excellent conciseness, graceful inimitability, sound meanings, solid structure, abundance of needed issues, eloquent agreed-upon words, and its blessedness for its students, auspiciousness for its readers and memorizers. People are too intelligent to praise something without seeing signs of excellence in it. So I complied with the command of the One who held the reins of my heart, and I surrendered to Him the reins of my obedience and submission, and I clarified from that what the commentators neglected in their books and what authors omitted in their compositions; it is not difficult for an inquirer or a seeker of clarification, nor is it closed to any beginner, while I recommend them to offer righteous prayers, to conceal faults, and to practice gracious overlooking. And Allah is the Granter of success. End. The book has many copies with different but similar titles in the libraries of Istanbul: In the Jarallah Library, a copy numbered as 'Mushkilat al-Quduri,' written in 838 AH, 245 folios; in the Lale Li Library (1160), 121 folios, titled 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri'; in Gururli Ali Pasha 211, 319 folios, titled 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri.' I note here that I photographed a manuscript whose title page says: 'al-Mushkilat min Sharh al-Mukhtasar'; it does not mention its author's name, and when mentioned by the compilers of the comprehensive index, they said it is by an unknown author. Upon examining it, nothing appeared to indicate its author. It is a photograph from the Azhar Library in Cairo (22531), consisting of 80 folios, written in 877 AH. It is a brief gloss on many places of the Mukhtasar, ending with the last annotation on the Book of Jihad and Siyar from Mukhtasar al-Quduri, then it says: 'Tammath hadhihi al-Mushkilat' (Completed these problematic points). End. 'Multamas al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Abbab wa al-Khillan' (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri) by Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb ibn Mansur al-Ghaznawi, who died around 500 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The book is in two volumes. Imams of the madhhab have transmitted from him, such as al-Zayla'i in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Allama Qasim in Tashih al-Quduri, and others.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section from the book 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It is part of the third chapter discussing the commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The text begins with praise for Mukhtasar al-Quduri, highlighting its conciseness, eloquence, and usefulness for both beginners and advanced students. The author then mentions that he has clarified matters that other commentators neglected, complying with divine command. He describes multiple manuscript copies of the book in Istanbul libraries: one in Jarallah Library titled 'Mushkilat al-Quduri' from 838 AH, one in Lale Li Library titled 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri', and one in Gururli Ali Pasha titled 'Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. He also notes that he photographed a manuscript from the Azhar Library titled 'al-Mushkilat min Sharh al-Mukhtasar', written in 877 AH, by an unknown author—a brief gloss on various parts of the Mukhtasar. Finally, he introduces a commentary titled 'Multamas al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Abbab wa al-Khillan' by Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb ibn Mansur al-Ghaznawi (d. ca. 500 AH), consisting of two volumes, which was used by later Hanafi scholars like al-Zayla'i and al-Allama Qasim.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied for its conciseness and comprehensiveness.
المشكلات (al-Mushkilat): A gloss or commentary by an unknown author that addresses problematic points in Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
ملتمس الإخوان (Multamas al-Ikhwan): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb al-Ghaznawi, meaning 'The Request of the Brethren'.

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Commentarial Tradition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Bibliographic description of two Hanafi commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the manuscript evidence for al-Ghaznawi's commentary and explain how Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' expands upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab was transmitted through commentaries that refined and preserved the rulings of the matn.

This lesson introduces two important commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh. You will learn how scholars built upon the matn, adding proofs, organization, and clarification. Understanding the commentarial tradition is essential for navigating the sources of Hanafi fiqh and for appreciating the scholarly chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary text
Recognize Mukhtasar al-Quduri as the base matn. Note its author (al-Quduri, d. 428 AH) and its status in the Hanafi school as a standard work for beginners.
The matn is concise and focuses on rulings without extensive proofs.
2
Analyze al-Ghaznawi's commentary
Examine the passage's manuscript discussion: the Fatih and Yeni Jami copies are misattributed (they are actually 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by al-Isbijabi); the correct copy is Murad Mulla no. 909. Note the commentary's title 'Multamis al-Ikhwan' and its relation to an earlier commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi.
This demonstrates the importance of manuscript verification in Islamic studies.
3
Examine Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'
Identify the author 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi (d. 537 AH) and his method: he uses Mukhtasar al-Quduri as a framework but adds proofs, additional rulings, and improved organization.
Al-Samarqandi explicitly states that his work is built upon al-Quduri.
4
Understand the purpose of commentaries
Reflect on the quotes: al-Ghaznawi wrote for his brothers' request; al-Samarqandi describes the matn as guiding the beginner in most incidents. Commentaries serve to make the matn accessible, expand its rulings, and integrate later scholarly contributions.
This reflects the pedagogical function of sharh in the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
وقد ذكر له أصحاب الفهرس الشامل (1) ثلاث نسخ في تركيا : نسخة فاتح، برقم ١٧٧٥، ونسخة مراد ملا، برقم ٩٠٩، ونسخة يني جامع، برقم ٤٦٦ .
والواقع أن نسخة فاتح، ونسخة يني جامع هما نسختان من كتاب «زاد الفقهاء» شرح القدوري للإسبيجابي، ولذا تضاف هاتان النسختان إلى نسخ «زاد الفقهاء».
وأما نسخة مراد ملا ،۹۰۹ ، فهي الصحيحة النسبة، وأنهـا شـرح الغزنوي، وهي نسخة كاملة في (۲۷۹) ورقة وفي كل صفحة (۳۳) سطراً، كتبت في سنة ٥٤٦هـ.
وقد جاء على طرة الكتاب ما يلي:
كتاب ملتمس الإخوان ومبتغى الأحباب والخلان، وهـو شـرح مختصر القدوري شرحه الشيخ الإمام أبو المعالي عبد الرب بن منصور بن إسماعيل بن إبراهيم الغزنوي».
وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه:
إني لما وفقني الله تعالى بفضله ورحمته ومنه ورأفته أن لخصتُ شرح مختصر الكرخي، المصنف من جهة الشيخ أبي الحسين أحمد ابن محمد بن جعفر البغدادي القدوري قدس الله روحهما، ورضي أئمة الهدى، وأنفقتُ أكثر عمري على تلخيصه عنهما وعن جميع
وتنقيحه، وأرقــت مـا شـيبني في ترصيفه وتوشيحه، واستحــســن مجهودي كلِّ مَن وَقَفَ عليه من الفقهاء المحققين المميزين ... التمس إخواني ... أن أشرح لهم مختصر الشيخ أبي الحسين القدوري ... وسميت هذا الكتاب من بين سائر الأسامي ملتمس الإخوان ومبتغى الأحباب والخلان». اهـ (1).
تحفة الفقهاء (ضمن فيه مختصر القدوري مع زيادات، وأدلة، وحسن تنظيم وتنسيق).
لعلاء الدين السمرقندي محمد بن أ ن أحمد، المتوفى سنة ٥٣٧ هـ (2) ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد صرح صاحب تحفة الفقهاء بأنه بنى تحفتـه علـى مختصر القدوري، واعتمد عليه، فقد قال في المقدمة :
اعلم أن المختصر المنسوب إلى الشيخ أبي الحسين القدوري من الفقه جامع جُمَلاً (3) مستعملة، بحيث لا تراها مدى الدهر مهملة يهدي بها الرائض في أكثر الحوادث والنوازل
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The comprehensive index authors mentioned three copies in Turkey: Fatih copy no. 1775, Murad Mulla copy no. 909, and Yeni Jami copy no. 466. In fact, the Fatih and Yeni Jami copies are two copies of the book 'Zad al-Fuqaha'' - the commentary on al-Quduri by al-Isbijabi, so these two copies are added to the copies of 'Zad al-Fuqaha''. As for the Murad Mulla copy no. 909, it is correctly attributed, being the commentary of al-Ghaznawi, a complete copy in 279 folios with 33 lines per page, written in 546 AH. On its flyleaf was written: 'The book Multamis al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Ahbab wa al-Khillan, which is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by the Shaykh Imam Abu al-Ma'ali 'Abd al-Rabb ibn Mansur ibn Isma'il ibn Ibrahim al-Ghaznawi.' In its author's introduction: 'When Allah Almighty by His grace, mercy, favor and kindness enabled me to summarize the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, authored by Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Baghdadi al-Quduri (may Allah sanctify their souls and be pleased with the righteous imams), and I spent most of my life summarizing it from them and from all… and refining it, and I spent sleepless nights in arranging and embellishing it, and every discerning jurist who saw it praised my effort… my brothers asked me to explain to them the Mukhtasar of Shaykh Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri… and I named this book among all names Multamis al-Ikhwan wa Mubtagha al-Ahbab wa al-Khillan.' End quote.
Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (which includes Mukhtasar al-Quduri with additions, proofs, and good organization and arrangement) by 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi Muhammad ibn Ahmad, died 537 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The author of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' stated that he built his Tuhfa on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and relied upon it. He said in the introduction: 'Know that the Mukhtasar attributed to Shaykh Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri is a compendium of collected, well-used fiqh statements, such that you will not see them neglected over time; it guides the beginner in most incidents and calamities.'
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion of two important commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It first addresses the manuscript tradition of al-Ghaznawi's commentary, correcting a common error: the Fatih and Yeni Jami copies are not of al-Ghaznawi's work but rather of al-Isbijabi's 'Zad al-Fuqaha'. The only correct copy of al-Ghaznawi's commentary is the Murad Mulla copy. The passage then quotes the flyleaf and introduction of al-Ghaznawi's work, revealing its title 'Multamis al-Ikhwan' and that it was a summary of an earlier commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. The passage then introduces 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' by 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, noting that it is based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and includes additional material and proofs. A quote from al-Samarqandi's introduction praises the Mukhtasar as a comprehensive and constantly useful text for students of fiqh.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh text by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
تحفة الفقهاء (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'): A commentary by 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, including additions and proofs.
الرائض (al-ra'id): The beginner student who practices and familiarizes himself with fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the base text; al-Ghaznawi's 'Multamis al-Ikhwan' and al-Samarqandi's 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'' are two distinct commentaries that preserve and expand the Hanafi fiqh tradition.

Tuhfat al-Fuqaha': A Gift of Fiqh Expanding al-Quduri
Biographical and pedagogical introduction to a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' supplements Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify its key structural features.

Core Idea
Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' is a Hanafi commentary that supplements Mukhtasar al-Quduri with evidence, organization, and additional issues.

This passage introduces us to Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' by Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, a pivotal Hanafi work. It explicitly builds upon the renowned Mukhtasar al-Quduri, enhancing it with missing categories, clarifying difficult points with strong proofs, and arranging issues beautifully. Understanding this relationship helps you navigate the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and the commentary
The passage states that Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' is built on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Note that al-Samarqandi explicitly acknowledges al-Quduri's work as his foundation.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a concise Hanafi fiqh matn.
2
Extract the author's stated purpose
Read the author's introduction where he explains why he wrote: to include categories of issues left out, to clarify difficult points with strong evidence, and to organize the material beautifully.
Look for verbs like 'mention', 'clarify', 'classify'.
3
Analyze the intended audience
The author mentions two types of students: al-ra'id (beginner) and al-murtad (advanced practicing student). Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' serves both levels.
This shows the work's pedagogical scope.
4
List the key features highlighted
From the passage, note the features: inclusion of evidence (dalil), beautiful arrangement, detailed categorization, ease of memorization and understanding, and comprehensiveness.
These are the author's claimed merits.
5
Connect to later commentaries
The passage mentions that al-Samarqandi's student, Imam al-Kasani, affirmed these features. This work is used in later commentaries like Al-Lubab.
This shows the chain of transmission and reliance.

الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
تحفة الفقهاء (ضمن فيه مختصر القدوري مع زيادات، وأدلة، وحسن تنظيم وتنسيق).
لعلاء الدين السمرقندي محمد بن أحمد، المتوفى سنة ٥٣٧ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد صرح صاحب تحفة الفقهاء بأنه بنى تحفته على مختصر القدوري، واعتمد عليه، فقد قال في المقدمة :
اعلم أن المختصر المنسوب إلى الشيخ أبي الحسين القدوري رحمه الله، جامع جُمَلٍ من الفقه مستعملة، بحيث لا تراها مدى الدهر مهملة، يهدي بها الرائض في أكثر الحوادث والنوازل، ويرتقي بها المرتاض إلى أعلى المراقي والمنازل.
ولما عمت رغبة الفقهاء إلى هذا الكتاب، طلب مني بعض من الإخوان والأصحاب، أن أذكر فيه بعض ما ترك المصنف من أقسام المسائل، وأوضح المشكلات منه بقوي من الدلائل، ليكون ذريعة إلى تصنيف الفائدة بالتقسيم والتفصيل، ووسيلة بذكر الدليل إلى تخريج ذوي التحصيل.
فأسرعت في الإسعاف والإجابة، وجاء التوفيق من الله تعالى في الإتمام والإصابة، وطمعاً من فضله في العفو والغفران والإنابة، فهو الموفق للصواب والسداد والهادي إلى سبل الرشاد، وسميته: «تحفة الفقهاء»، إذ هي هديتي لهم، لتحقيق الصحبة والإخاء، عند رجوعهم إلى مواطن الآباء.
فليقبل هديتي هذه من شاء كسب العز والبهاء، وليذكرني بصالح الدعاء، في الحياة والممات، فهو غرضي ونيتي، والأعمال بالنيات، وقابل الأعمال عالم بالخفيات، وما توفيقي إلا بالله، عليه توكلت، وإليه أنيب). اهـ
ومن أهم مزايا تحفة الفقهاء، مع ضمه لمختصر القدوري، أنه يختص بترتيب وتقسيم جميل للمسائل، وتفصيل مفيد للغاية، للدارس والمدرس في تيسير سبيل الوصول إلى المطلوب على الطالبين، وتقريبه إلى أفهام المقتبسين من تيسير حفظه، وسرعة فهمه واستيعاب مضمونه، وسهولة ضبطه. كما صرح بهذا المؤلف، وأكده تلميذه الإمام الكاساني شارح 6
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (it includes Mukhtasar al-Quduri with additions, evidence, and good organization and arrangement). By Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi Muhammad ibn Ahmad, who died in the year 537 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The author of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' explicitly stated that he built his Tuhfah upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri and relied upon it. He said in the introduction: Know that the mukhtasar attributed to Shaykh Abi al-Husayn al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is a collection of commonly used sections of fiqh, such that you do not see them neglected throughout time. It guides the beginner (al-ra'id) in most incidents and events, and the advanced student (al-murtad) rises with it to the highest stations and ranks. When the desire of the jurists for this book became widespread, some of the brothers and companions asked me to mention in it some of the categories of issues that the author left out, and to clarify the problematic points with strong evidence, so that it might be a means to classify benefit through division and detail, and a means by mentioning evidence to train those of attainment. So I hastened to comply and respond, and success came from Allah Almighty in completion and correctness, hoping for His bounty in pardon, forgiveness, and repentance. He is the Granter of success to what is right and correct, and the Guide to the paths of righteousness. I named it 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (The Gift of the Jurists), for it is my gift to them, to achieve companionship and brotherhood when they return to their homelands. So let whoever desires to acquire honor and splendor accept this gift of mine, and remember me with a virtuous supplication in life and death. That is my aim and intention, and deeds are by intentions, and the Acceptor of deeds is Knower of hidden things. My success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely and to Him I turn. End. Among the most important features of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', in addition to its inclusion of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, is that it is distinguished by a beautiful arrangement and division of issues, and a highly beneficial detail for the student and teacher in facilitating the way to reach the desired goal for students, and bringing it closer to the understanding of learners through ease of memorization, quick comprehension, grasp of its content, and simplicity of mastery. As the author stated and his student Imam al-Kasani, the commentator, confirmed.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and introductory section from the work 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It presents the work 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' by Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, who is a Hanafi jurist (d. 537 AH). The commentator explains that al-Samarqandi explicitly based his book on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', a foundational Hanafi text. The author's own words from the introduction of 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' are quoted to show his purpose: to supplement the Mukhtasar with additional categories of issues not covered by Quduri, and to clarify difficult points with strong evidence (dalil). The work is named 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (Gift of the Jurists) as a gift to fellow scholars. The passage highlights the practical utility of the book: it is well-organized, detailed, and facilitates memorization and understanding for both students and teachers. Al-Samarqandi's student, Imam al-Kasani (author of 'Bada'i' al-Sana'i'), also praised the work. This passage sets the stage for the commentary that follows in 'Al-Lubab', which itself is a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' drawing from 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' and other sources.

Key Terms
تحفة الفقهاء (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'): A Hanafi fiqh work by Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi that expands Mukhtasar al-Quduri with additional sections, evidence, and better organization.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) summarizing key rulings without detailed evidence.
الرائض (al-ra'id): The beginner student of fiqh who is still learning and practicing the rulings.
المرتاض (al-murtad): An advanced student who has become proficient in fiqh through practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' is a Hanafi commentary that enriches Mukhtasar al-Quduri by adding evidence, filling gaps, and presenting the material in a well-organized manner.

The Unique Organization of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha
Describing the significance and organization of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the unique chapter arrangement of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha and its pedagogical advantages.

Core Idea
Tuhfat al-Fuqaha reorders Mukhtasar al-Quduri to facilitate learning and comprehension.

Imam al-Samarqandi's Tuhfat al-Fuqaha is not merely a commentary but a systematic reorganization of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. In this lesson, we explore why the author rearranged the chapters, placing marriage and divorce after sales, and how this structure benefits students of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
The author wrote Tuhfat al-Fuqaha to fill gaps left by al-Quduri and clarify difficult issues with strong evidence.
The work is a gift (tuhfa) to jurists.
2
Examine the chapter reordering
Unlike Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Tuhfat al-Fuqaha places marriage (nikah) and divorce (talaq) after sales (buyu'), then continues with other transactions.
This breaks from the traditional ibadat-muamalat sequence.
3
Analyze the claimed benefits
The author states that his arrangement facilitates memorization, quick comprehension, and ease of mastery for both student and teacher.
The student Imam al-Kasani affirmed this in Badai'i al-Sanai'i.

ولما عمت رغبة الفقهاء إلى هذا الكتاب، طلب مني بعض من الإخوان والأصحاب، أن أذكر فيه بعض ما ترك المصنف من أقسام المسائل، وأوضح المشكلات منه بقوي من الدلائل، ليكون ذريعة إلى تصنيف الفائدة بالتقسيم والتفصيل، ووسيلة بذكر الدليل إلى تخريج ذوي التحصيل.

وأما عن ترتيب أبوابه، فلم يلتزم صاحب التحفة ترتيب ونَسَقَ القدوري، فإنه أتى بكتاب النكاح والطلاق بعد البيوع، ثم أكمل أبواب المعاملات كالإجارة والشركة، وهكذا.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
And the aspiring ascends through them to the highest stations and ranks.
When the desire of the jurists for this book became widespread, some of my brethren and companions requested that I mention in it some of the categories of issues that the author left out, and clarify the problematic ones among them with strong proofs, so that it may be a means to classify benefit by division and detail, and a way by mentioning the evidence to stimulate those of accomplishment.
So I hastened to comply and respond, and success came from Allah Almighty in completion and correctness, and hoping for His favor in pardon, forgiveness, and repentance, for He is the granter of success to what is right and correct, and the guide to the paths of rectitude. And I named it 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (The Gift of the Jurists), for it is my gift to them, realizing companionship and brotherhood, when they return to the homelands of their fathers.
Let whoever desires to earn honor and splendor accept this gift of mine, and remember me with righteous supplication, in life and after death, for that is my aim and intention, and deeds are by intentions, and the Acceptor of deeds is Knower of hidden things. And my success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely, and to Him I turn in repentance.
Among the most important merits of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha, besides its inclusion of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, is that it is distinguished by a beautiful arrangement and division of issues, and a highly beneficial detail for the student and teacher in facilitating the way to reach the desired object, and making it accessible to the minds of those seeking knowledge, by facilitating its memorization, quick comprehension, grasping its content, and ease of mastery. As the author declared this, and his student Imam al-Kasani, the commentator of al-Tuhfa, affirmed it in the introduction to his book Badai'i al-Sanai'i, and that his teacher 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi devoted attention to arrangement and organization.
As for the order of its chapters, the author of al-Tuhfa did not adhere to the order and sequence of al-Quduri, for he placed the Book of Marriage and Divorce after Sales, then completed the chapters on transactions like Lease and Partnership, and so on.
Tuhfat al-Fuqaha is a published and circulated book, edited by Dr. Muhammad Zaki 'Abd al-Barr in three volumes, in a detailed and luminous edition. Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Kasani (d. 587 AH) explained Tuhfat al-Fuqaha in his famous great book 'Badai'i al-Sanai'i', which is also published, circulated, and well-known, in seven volumes.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Verifying Authorship of Commentaries: Sharh Mushkilat and Al-Lubab
Identifying authors via chronological reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate biographical claims about Hanafi commentary authorship using chronological reasoning.

Core Idea
Not every attribution in biographic encyclopedias is reliable – historical chronology filters authentic authorship.

When studying the Hanafi tradition, knowing which scholar wrote which commentary is essential for understanding the evolution of the school. This passage demonstrates how to critically examine authorship claims, correcting a common misattribution through careful date alignment. You will learn to apply similar scrutiny to other texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two commentaries and their claimed authors
First, note the two works discussed: 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri' and 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab'. Kashf al-Zunun attributes the first to Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 383 AH). The second is by al-Yazidi (d. after 559 AH).
Keep the death dates in mind.
2
Check the chronology of the base text and the claimed commentator
Al-Quduri was born in 362 AH. Abu al-Layth died around 383 AH. For Abu al-Layth to comment on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, al-Quduri must have completed it before his death. That would require al-Quduri to author a major work before age 21, which is historically improbable.
Chronological plausibility is key.
3
Assess the alternative attribution
The author suggests the commentary is actually by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi (d. 552 AH), a later Hanafi scholar. This is plausible because he lived after al-Quduri and is known for other commentaries.
The correct author must be after the base text's composition.
4
Characterize the second commentary
Al-Yazidi's Al-Lubab is described as a medium-length commentary that points to each issue concisely, directing readers to his fuller work al-Tahdhib for detailed proofs.
This shows the author's intent: a practical reference, not a comprehensive analysis.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
۱۰- شرح مشكلات القدوري
لمحمد بن أحمد السمرقندي، المتوفى سنة ٥٥٢هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
جاء في كشف الظنون: شرح مشكلات القدوري، للشيخ الإمام أبي الليث نصر بن محمد السمرقندي، وهو شرح مختصر. كذا قيل.
ولعله شرح أبي بكر علاء الدين محمد بن أحمد السمرقندي، المفسر، وصاحب ميزان الأصول، المتوفى سنة ٥٥٢ هـ. اهـ من كشف الظنون.
قلت: وفاة أبي الليث نصر بن محمد كانت سنة ٣٨٣هـ، وقيل ٣٧٥هـ، وقيل ٣٩٣هـ وولادة الإمام القدوري سنة ٣٦٢هـ، فيبعد جداً أن القدوري ألف مختصره قبل سن العشرين، وأن أبا الليث شرحه.
وعليه، فهذا الشرح هو لمحمد بن أحمد السمرقندي، المتوفى سنة ٥٥٢هـ.
ومن هذا الشرح نسخة في الظاهرية برقم ٩١٨٣، تقع في ٢٩٢ ورقة، وهي نسخة قديمة، وينظر الفهرس الشامل، فقد ذكر له عدة نسخ.

١١ - اللباب في شرح الكتاب (شرح مختصر القدوري).
لليزيدي الإمام شيخ الإسلام قاضي القضاة جمال الدين (جلال الدين) أبي سعد المطهر بن الحسين (الحسن) بن سعد اليزدي، ولم يُحدد مترجموه سنة وفاته، لكنها كانت بعد سنة ٥٥٩هـ. فقد ذكر صاحب كشف الظنون أن للمطهر هذا شرحاً على الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن سماه التهذيب، في مجلدين، فرغ من تأليفه سنة ٥٥٩هـ.
وقد ذكر اليزدي في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري (اللباب) أنه يشير إشارة لكل مسألة من مسائل مختصر القدوري بدون إطالة، ومن أراد الزيادة فليراجع: التهذيب شرح الجامع الصغير، ففيه غنى، حيث علل فيه للمسائل والأحكام باستيفاء.
وعلى هذا، فشرح اللباب شرح متوسط، يذكر فيه بعض الأدلة، دون استيفاء.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
10- Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri
By Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, who died in the year 552 AH, may God have mercy on him.
It is mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun: 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri, by the Shaykh al-Imam Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Samarqandi, and it is a brief commentary. Thus it was said.'
But perhaps it is the commentary of Abu Bakr 'Ala' al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, the exegete, author of Mizan al-Usul, who died in 552 AH. End quote from Kashf al-Zunun.
I say: The death of Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad was in 383 AH, or it is said 375 AH, or 393 AH, and the birth of Imam al-Quduri was in 362 AH. So it is extremely unlikely that al-Quduri authored his Mukhtasar before the age of twenty, and that Abu al-Layth commented on it.
Therefore, this commentary is by Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi, who died in 552 AH.
A copy of this commentary exists in al-Zahiriyya under number 9183, comprising 292 folios, and it is an old copy. See al-Fihris al-Shamil, for it mentions several copies.

11- Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri)
By al-Yazidi, the Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, Qadi al-Qudat Jamal al-Din (Jalal al-Din) Abu Sa'd al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn (al-Hasan) ibn Sa'd al-Yazidi. His biographers did not specify his year of death, but he died after 559 AH. The author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned that this al-Mutahhar has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, named al-Tahdhib, in two volumes, which he completed in 559 AH.
Al-Yazidi mentioned in the introduction to his commentary on al-Quduri (Al-Lubab) that he points to each issue of the issues of Mukhtasar al-Quduri without elaboration, and whoever wants more should consult al-Tahdhib: Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, for it is sufficient, as it provides reasons for the issues and rulings comprehensively.
Accordingly, Al-Lubab is a medium-length commentary; it mentions some proofs, but not exhaustively.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the third chapter of the book, which surveys commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author discusses two specific commentaries. First, 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri' — he clarifies a common error: although Kashf al-Zunun attributes it to Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, the author argues this is impossible due to historical chronology. Abu al-Layth died around 383 AH, while Imam al-Quduri was born in 362 AH. For al-Quduri to have written his Mukhtasar early enough for Abu al-Layth to comment on it, he would have had to produce it before age twenty, which is improbable. Therefore, the correct author is Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi (d. 552 AH), who also wrote a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir called al-Tahdhib. Second, 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' by al-Yazidi (d. after 559 AH). This is a medium-length commentary that provides brief references to each issue of the Mukhtasar, without exhaustive discussion of proofs; it serves as a concise guide, directing readers to his fuller commentary al-Tahdhib for detailed reasoning.

Key Terms
شرح مشكلات القدوري (Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri that addresses difficult or problematic points, attributed here to Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi.
اللباب في شرح الكتاب (Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab): A medium-length commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Yazidi, providing concise explanations without exhaustive detail.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it unlikely that Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi authored 'Sharh Mushkilat al-Quduri'?
A) Because Abu al-Layth died before al-Quduri was born.
B) Because al-Quduri would have had to write his Mukhtasar before age twenty for Abu al-Layth to comment on it.
C) Because Abu al-Layth was a Shafi'i scholar.
D) Because the manuscript is attributed to Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi.

Key Takeaway
Authorship claims in classical bibliographies must be tested against chronological plausibility; a commentator must have lived after the base text's composition by a reasonable interval.

Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Scholarly Tradition
Listing of commentaries on a Hanafi fiqh manual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three early commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and state their authors and approximate dates.

Core Idea
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri generated a rich commentarial tradition that shaped Hanafi fiqh study.

This passage from al-Maydani's al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri lists several earlier works that explain al-Quduri's concise manual. These commentaries show how later Hanafi scholars built upon the matn, producing verse and prose expositions. Understanding this tradition helps you appreciate the layered nature of Hanafi texts and the scholarly chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the core Hanafi fiqh manual being commented upon. Note its author and significance.
Al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) composed this concise work that became a standard matn.
2
Note the oldest manuscripts of al-Lubab
The author mentions manuscript copies of his own book to establish its textual history. Observe the dates and locations.
Oldest copies from 571 AH and 576 AH relate to the text itself.
3
Recognize each commentary
The passage lists three works: a poem (nazm), a prose commentary by al-Sarakhsi, and 'Zād al-Fuqahā' by al-Isbījābī. Identify author and death year for each.
Use the given death dates to place them chronologically.
4
Observe the scholarly chain
The author cites a contemporary scholar (Shaykh Muhammad Fatih Qaya) and a biographer (Qasim ibn Qutlubugha) to attest to the works.
This demonstrates how later scholars rely on earlier authorities.
5
Reflect on significance
Consider why multiple commentaries were written: to clarify, expand, or versify the matn. This indicates the matn's centrality in Hanafi education.
Each commentary serves a pedagogical purpose.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography from the book 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' listing several commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author begins by noting extant manuscript copies of the book itself, emphasizing its scholarly transmission. He then lists three works: a poetic versification (nazm) by Ibn al-Hakim al-Hakimi (d. 567 AH), a prose commentary by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi (d. 571 AH), and 'Zad al-Fuqaha'' by Baha' al-Din al-Isbījābī (d. 591 AH). Al-Isbījābī's commentary is praised by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha as 'beneficial'. This demonstrates the extensive scholarly activity around al-Quduri's Mukhtasar in the 6th-7th centuries AH.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise handbook of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied in the Hanafi madhhab.
اللباب في شرح القدوري (al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (the author of the present book), providing detailed exposition.
نَظم (nazm): A poetic versification of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, rendering the prose into verse for easier memorization.

The Role and Methodology of Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Commentary introduction and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and methodology of al-Isbijabi's Zad al-Fuqaha' and identify the key features that distinguish a Hanafi commentary focused on fatwa positions.

Core Idea
A commentary (sharh) on a matn is the essential bridge to the madhhab's relied-upon rulings.

This passage introduces the third chapter of al-Lubab, which catalogues commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It highlights Zad al-Fuqaha' by Baha' al-Din al-Isbijabi, a commentary that prioritizes proofs for the mufta bihi positions. Understanding the author's introduction gives us insight into the methodology of writing a beneficial commentary in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentary and its author
Locate the name of the commentary (Zad al-Fuqaha') and its author (al-Isbijabi). Note his death date and the appraisal by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.
The author is a Hanafi jurist from the 6th century AH.
2
Analyse the author's motivation
Read the introduction: al-Isbijabi explains that students of fiqh need a concise text (mukhtasar) to rely on. He chose Mukhtasar al-Quduri because it covers essential, applied fiqh and will not become neglected.
This reflects a pragmatic pedagogical concern.
3
Examine the declared methodology
Al-Isbijabi states he will limit his commentary to proofs (dalil) for the position that is the basis for fatwa in most issues. He will include some real incidents (waqiat) and new cases (nawazil), avoiding excessive brevity or length.
Focus on dalil and mufta bihi positions is a hallmark of this commentary.
4
Note the evidence of his methodology
The passage points out that al-Isbijabi uses phrases like 'this is the most correct' or 'upon it is the fatwa' throughout his commentary, which show his commitment to identifying the relied-upon view.
Such phrases guide the reader to the operative ruling.

Third Chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri By Radi al-Din Abu Mansur al-Sarakhsi Muhammad ibn Muhammad, died in the year 571 AH, author of al-Muhit al-Radawi, may Allah have mercy on him. Mentioned by the authors of al-Fihris al-Shamil, and that a copy of it exists in the Kabul Museum, written in the year 731 AH, in 190 folios. 14 - Zad al-Fuqaha' Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Imam Qadi Abu al-Ma'ali Baha' al-Din al-Isbijabi Muhammad ibn Ahmad, died in the year 591 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said about this commentary: 'He explained al-Quduri with a beneficial explanation.' And it is mentioned in the author's introduction: ... The Shaykh, the Qadi, the Imam, the most distinguished, the professor, Baha' al-Din, the beauty of Islam and the Muslims, the adornment of the Imams, the Mufti of the nation, the unique of the age, the magnificent of this composition... (and refers to Kashf al-Zunun 1632/2). (1) His biography in Taj al-Tarajim p. 248, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 188, Hadiyat al-'Arifin 91/2, and his death is recorded as 544 AH. (3) His biography in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 461/5. (4) Taj al-Tarajim p. 257. 154 Taj al-Tarajim p. 256, al-Jawahir 381 Third Chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri 381 Know that deeds have fallen short, and events and occupations have increased, and the senses have become weak, and memory has become weary, and the one desiring fiqh does not find a way without a summarised work (mukhtasar) that encompasses it, to be his provision for incidents that befall him. Therefore I considered the most correct in planning and the most obligatory in opinion, that I should explain the summarised book of fiqh attributed to the Shaykh, the Imam, the venerable Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him; because it includes a collection of applied fiqh, such that it will not be neglected for long periods. And I will limit myself in that to the proofs (dalil) based on what is the fatwa in most issues, and I will include with them a little of the incidents and new cases (nawazil) to complete the benefit and increase the return, and I will be cautious thereby against conciseness and prolixity, and I will seek the best path in between. So I sought help from Allah Almighty in completing it and sought His protection from error and slip therein, and I named it (Zad al-Fuqaha'), and it is beneficial for them when they return to the homes of their fathers. And Allah is the Grantor of success and rectitude, and the Guide to the path of goodness and guidance. End quote from the author's introduction. And it is pointed out here that the author al-Isbijabi declared that he limits himself in this explanation to the proofs based on what is the fatwa in most issues, and thus he says for example: 'This is the most correct, or: and upon it is the fatwa', or: 'Upon this narration our shuyukh relied', or: 'The correct is the apparent narration', or: 'The correct'.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a front matter excerpt from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, specifically the third chapter, which lists and describes various commentaries written on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam al-Quduri. The chapter begins by mentioning the commentary by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi (d. 571 AH), author of al-Muhit al-Radawi, noting that a manuscript exists in the Kabul Museum. Then it introduces the commentary entitled Zad al-Fuqaha' by Baha' al-Din al-Isbijabi (d. 591 AH), quoting a favorable appraisal by al-Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. The passage then cites al-Isbijabi's own introduction to his commentary, explaining his motivation: recognizing that seekers of fiqh need a concise text (mukhtasar) to rely on, he chose to explain al-Quduri's Mukhtasar because it contains essential, commonly applied fiqh. He states his methodology of focusing on proofs (dalil) for positions that are the basis for fatwa in most cases, adding some real incidents (waqi'at) and new cases (nawazil) to enrich the benefit, while avoiding excess brevity or length. The commentary is named Zad al-Fuqaha' (Provision for Jurists). Finally, the text of al-Lubab notes that al-Isbijabi emphasizes his reliance on the preferred positions for fatwa, evident in his frequent phrases like 'this is the most correct' or 'upon it is the fatwa'.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied as a foundational text.
زاد الفقهاء (Zad al-Fuqaha'): Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Isbijabi, focusing on proofs and fatwa positions.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary or exposition of a text, here referring to works that explain Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
دليل (Dalil): Proof or evidence, often a Quranic verse, hadith, or qiyas, used to support a ruling.
الفتوى (Fatwa): A legal opinion based on the school's relied-upon position.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Methodology of al-Isbabiji's 'Zad al-Fuqaha': Focus on Mufta Bihi Proofs
Author explaining his commentary methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Isbabiji's methodological principle in his commentary and explain how it serves the practical needs of a Hanafi jurist.

Core Idea
Al-Isbabiji's commentary provides only the proof for the fatwa position, not every opinion.

This lesson introduces you to the commentary 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by Ahmad ibn Yusuf al-Isbabiji, a concise yet complete explanation of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author explains his unique method: he limits himself to presenting the legal proofs (dala'il) for the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in most issues, rather than surveying all opinions. This approach makes the work practical for a jurist who needs the reasoning behind the operative ruling without getting lost in minor differences. Understanding this method helps you appreciate how later Hanafi scholars streamlined fiqh study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
Read the first paragraph where al-Isbabiji explains why he wrote the commentary. He notes people's weakness and the need for a concise work covering common issues.
2
Extract the core methodological statement
Find the sentence where he says 'I limit myself to the proofs according to what is relied upon for fatwa in most issues.' This is the key principle.
3
List the additional features he includes
Note that he adds a few incidents (waqi'at) and new cases (nawazil) to complete the benefit. He also aims to avoid both brevity and length.
4
Recognize the terminology he uses for the mufta bihi
The passage later gives examples of his phrasing: 'This is the most correct,' 'Upon it is the fatwa,' 'The correct is the statement of Abu Hanifa.' Identify these as indicators of the preferred ruling.
5
Understand the significance of this method in Hanafi learning
Reflect on why focusing on the mufta bihi proofs is helpful: it saves time, clarifies the operative ruling, and still gives the reasoning. This contrasts with commentaries that discuss every ikhtilaf without preference.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 381. [I am] Ahmad ibn Yusuf, attributed to Isbijab, may Allah have mercy on him. Know that [people's] actions have fallen short, events and occupations have multiplied, perception has weakened, and memory has declined. The one desiring fiqh has no choice but to have a Mukhtasar that contains it, to be his provision for the incidents that befall him. So I considered the most correct in planning and the most obligatory in opinion to be that I explain the Mukhtasar in fiqh attributed to the great Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri al-Baghdadi, may Allah have mercy on him; because it contains commonly used branches of fiqh that are not neglected throughout the ages. And I limit myself in that to the proofs according to what is relied upon for fatwa in most issues, and I add to them a small amount of incidents and new cases to complete the benefit and increase the return. By doing so, I avoid brevity and length, and I seek the best path in between. So I sought help from Allah Almighty in completing it and sought protection from Him from error and slip in it, and I named it 'Zad al-Fuqaha' (Provision for Jurists). It is beneficial for them when they return to their ancestral homes. Allah is the Giver of success to what is right and correct, and the Guide to the path of good and right guidance. End quote from the author's introduction. It is noted here that the author al-Isbabiji declared that he limits himself in this commentary to the proofs according to what is relied upon for fatwa in most issues. Hence, he says, for example: 'This is the most correct,' or 'Upon it is the fatwa,' or 'Upon this narration our mashayikh relied,' or 'The correct is Zahir al-Riwayah,' or 'The correct is the statement of Abu Hanifa.' And so on. He transmitted many of these quotations to establish the mufta bihi, as did 'Allamah Qasim in Tashih al-Quduri, attributing them to al-Isbabiji. The author also addresses in this commentary the differences among the imams of the madhhab, and the differences of the Shafi'is and Malikis, and he pays attention to mentioning transmitted proofs and rational explanations for the statements and narrations he presents. This is important for clarifying the source of the ruling from the evidence. He also pays attention to mentioning the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalala). It is a complete commentary, not a gloss, as he brings the full text of al-Quduri then explains it. In sum, it is a precious commentary of fine size, among the commentaries that one seeks to edit and publish before others. The book consists of 268 folios, each page 22 lines, as in the photograph of a copy in the Islamic University of Madinah. There are many copies; see al-Fihris al-Shamil (4/546). It is noted here that the compilers of al-Fihris al-Shamil mentioned copies of Multamis al-Ikhwan, a commentary on al-Quduri by al-Ghaznawi, and they mentioned two copies in Fatih Library, number 1775, consisting of 273 folios, written in 537 AH, as informed to me by dear brother Dr. Khalil Qutlay from Istanbul. They also mentioned a copy in Yeni Cami, number 466. These two copies are actually from the book 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by al-Isbabiji, not from Multamis al-Ikhwan, as previously noted.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction to the commentary 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by Ahmad ibn Yusuf al-Isbabiji (d. after 540 AH) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author opens by lamenting the difficulty of modern life and the lack of dedication to learning, then states his purpose: to write a commentary that is concise yet covers the most commonly needed fiqh issues. He explicitly declares that his method is to limit himself to presenting proofs (dalil) only for the position that is preferred for fatwa (al-mufta bihi) in most issues. This means he does not delve into all differences but focuses on what is operative. He also adds a small number of contemporary incidents (waqi'at) and new cases (nawazil) for completeness. He names his work 'Zad al-Fuqaha' (Provision for Jurists), indicating it is a practical reference. The passage then notes that his terminology includes phrases like 'this is the most correct' or 'upon it is the fatwa' to identify the preferred view. He also references the later scholar 'Allamah Qasim (Qasim al-Qunawi?) who used al-Isbabiji's work in his Tashih al-Quduri. Al-Isbabiji's commentary is praised as complete (not a gloss), including full text of al-Quduri, and covering inter-madhhab differences with proofs. Finally, manuscript details are given: 268 folios, 22 lines per page, with copies in Madinah and Istanbul, and a clarification that certain manuscripts attributed to al-Ghaznawi are actually by al-Isbabiji.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The famous Hanafi fiqh primer by Imam Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
زاد الفقهاء (Zad al-Fuqaha): Title of al-Isbabiji's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'Provision for Jurists'.
ما عليه الفتوى (ma 'alayhi al-fatwa): The relied-upon position for issuing legal verdicts; the preferred opinion in the madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the six core books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani.
الدلائل (al-dala'il): The legal proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, etc.) used to derive rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 'This is the view of Imam al-Shafi'i'

Key Takeaway
Al-Isbabiji's 'Zad al-Fuqaha' is a commentary that efficiently provides proofs only for the preferred fatwa positions, making it a practical tool for Hanafi jurists.

Introduction and Front Matter
