Understanding Commentaries and Manuscript Verification in Hanafi Fiqh
Front matter describing a commentary's methodology and manuscript correction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological features of al-Isbijabi's commentary and identify the manuscript correction regarding 'Zad al-Fuqaha'.

Core Idea
A reliable commentary clarifies the mufta bihi through textual evidence and rational justification, but only if the manuscript attribution is correct.

Hanafi fiqh is preserved through a chain of commentaries and glosses that explain and refine the rulings of the early imams. This front matter from a discussion of commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar introduces us to the method of one such commentary by al-Isbijabi. It also alerts us to a common pitfall: manuscript misattribution can lead to relying on the wrong text. In this lesson, we will examine the features of a sound commentary and the importance of textual criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the commentary
The primary goal is to establish the mufta bihi (operative ruling) by transmitting and authenticating positions from earlier authorities like al-Allamah Qasim's Tashih al-Quduri and al-Isbijabi's transmissions.
2
Note the sources and evidence used
The author relies on transmitted evidence (naqli) and rational justifications (aqli), and he includes differences among Hanafi imams and with Shafi'is and Malikis.
3
Recognize the method of explanation
The commentary is a complete sharh, not a hashiya — it presents the full text of al-Quduri, then explains it. It also pays attention to wajh al-dalala (the aspect of indication from the proof).
4
Understand the manuscript correction
The passage clarifies that two manuscripts previously thought to be 'Multamis al-Ikhwan' by al-Ghaznawi are actually 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by al-Isbijabi. This is crucial for correct attribution.
5
Reflect on the implications
For a student or researcher, verifying manuscript identity is essential before using a text as authoritative. Misattribution can lead to incorrect citation of positions.

Commentary
This passage is front matter from a biographical or bibliographic discussion of commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The text describes a specific commentary (likely by al-Isbijabi) that relies heavily on two earlier works: Tashih al-Quduri by al-Allamah Qasim, and the transmissions of al-Isbijabi. The author of this commentary is noted for his method: he presents the differences of opinion among the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and also engages with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. He supports his arguments with transmitted evidence (naqli) and rational justifications (aqli), and he clarifies the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalala) from the proofs. The commentary is described as a complete sharh, not a hashiya, as it includes the full text of al-Quduri and then explains it. The passage also includes a note about manuscript confusion: two manuscripts previously thought to be 'Multamis al-Ikhwan' by al-Ghaznawi are actually 'Zad al-Fuqaha' by al-Isbijabi. This clarification is important for bibliographic accuracy.

Key Terms
المفتى به (al-muftā bihi): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwas, as established by the author from earlier authorities like Qasim and al-Isbijabi.
تصحيح القدوري (Tashīḥ al-Qudūrī): A work by al-Allamah Qasim that corrects or authenticates rulings in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
وجه الدلالة (wajh al-dalāla): The aspect of indication from the textual evidence that leads to the ruling.

Key Takeaway
A sound Hanafi commentary combines textual evidence, rational reasoning, and manuscript verification to preserve the mufta bihi.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Introduction to Badayat al-Mubtadi: Al-Marghinani's Compilation
Preface of al-Marghinani explaining the compilation of Badayat al-Mubtadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the composition and purpose of al-Marghinani's Badayat al-Mubtadi and identify its two source texts.

Core Idea
Badayat al-Mubtadi is the bridge between two foundational Hanafi texts, creating a concise beginner's manual that later became al-Hidayah.

This lesson introduces the 15th commentary in our series: Badayat al-Mubtadi by Imam al-Marghinani. While not a ruling text itself, understanding its genesis helps us appreciate how Hanafi legal knowledge was transmitted and condensed. Al-Marghinani's work combines two pillars of the madhhab: al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and al-Jami' al-Saghir. This preface reveals his pedagogical intent and the scholarly environment of his time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his role
Al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) is the author of Badayat al-Mubtadi and later its famous commentary al-Hidayah. Note his full name and scholarly stature.
He is a central figure in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the two source texts
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a concise fiqh manual by Ahmad al-Quduri. Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a collection of rulings by Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
These are authoritative texts in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the author's motivation
Al-Marghinani traveled to Iraq, found al-Quduri's Mukhtasar excellent in conciseness, and observed scholars in Transoxiana encouraging memorization of al-Jami' al-Saghir. He combined them to create a single concise yet comprehensive text.
He avoided repetition to keep the work streamlined.
4
Note the title and its significance
'Badayat al-Mubtadi' means 'The Beginner's Start' – aimed at students beginning their study of fiqh.
The title reflects its educational purpose.
5
Connect to later works
This matn later became the basis for al-Marghinani's own commentary al-Hidayah, which is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh.
Understanding this lineage clarifies the authority chain.

للإمام المرغيناني أبي الحسن علي بن أبي بكر، المتوفى سنة

وهو مختصر، وقد جاء في مقدمة مؤلفه :
(الحمد لله الذي هدانا إلى ينابيع حكمه، وأولانا سابعَ نِعَمه، حمداً نستفيد به رضوانه، ونستزيد به إحسانه، وصلى الله على رسوله محمد الذي جعله الله قدوة لأنامه، في بيان حلاله وحرامه، وعلى آله وأصحابه مصابيح الظلم، وينابيع الحكم، وسلم تسليماً. قال العبد الضعيف أبو الحسن علي بن أبي بكر بن عبد الحليم
المرغيناني، وفقه الله لما فيه الذكر الجميل، والذخر الجزيل : كان يخطر ببالي عند ابتداء حالي أن يكون لي في الفقه كتـاب فـيـه من كل نوع باب، ثم هو صغير الحجم كبير الرسم، يتحفظه الشادي المبتدي، ويتأمله الهادي المهتدي.
وحيث وقع الاتفاق بتطواف ،العراق، وجدت المختصر المنسوب
إلى القدوري أجمل كتاب فى أحسن إيجاز وإعجاب.
ورأيت كبراء الدهر بما وراء النهر يرغبون الصغير والكبير في حفظ الجامع الصغير ، فهَمَمْتُ أن أؤلف كتاباً أجمع بينهما، ولا أتجاوز فيه
عنهما إلا ما دعت الضرورة إليه، وحملتني كثرة وقوعه عليه. وأتحرز فيه عن إيراد المعاد، ليرغـب فيـه كـل حاضـر وبـاد،
وسميته: «بداية المبتدي».
15- Badayat al-Mubtadi: A compilation combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir (by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan).
By Imam al-Marghinani, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abi Bakr, died in 593 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
It is a concise work. In its preface, the author says:
"Praise be to Allah who guided us to the springs of His wisdom and bestowed upon us the seventh of His favors, a praise through which we seek His pleasure and increase His goodness. And blessings and peace be upon His Messenger Muhammad, whom Allah made a model for mankind in explaining the lawful and unlawful, and upon his family and companions, the lamps of darkness and the springs of wisdom. The weak servant Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn Abd al-Halim al-Marghinani, may Allah grant him success to that which brings good remembrance and abundant reward, says: It occurred to me at the beginning of my situation that I should have a book on fiqh containing every type of chapter, yet small in size but great in subject matter, which the beginner student could memorize and the guided seeker could contemplate. And when I happened to travel through Iraq, I found the Mukhtasar attributed to al-Quduri to be the most beautiful book in excellent conciseness and pleasingness. And I saw the great scholars of Transoxiana encouraging both young and old to memorize al-Jami' al-Saghir. So I resolved to author a book combining the two, not going beyond them except what necessity required, and having much occurrence prompted me. I will avoid repetition, so that it may be desired by all present and afar. And I named it 'Badayat al-Mubtadi'."
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is front matter introducing the 15th commentary listed in the chapter: 'Badayat al-Mubtadi' by Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), who is also the author of the famous 'al-Hidayah'. His work combines two foundational Hanafi texts: al-Quduri's Mukhtasar (a concise legal manual) and al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah). Al-Marghinani's preface explains his motivation: he wanted a book that is small yet comprehensive, suitable for beginners and advanced students. He found al-Quduri's Mukhtasar excellent in conciseness, and noted that scholars in Transoxiana (Central Asia) encouraged memorization of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Thus he combined them, avoiding redundancy. The title 'Badayat al-Mubtadi' means 'The Beginner's Start', indicating its target audience. This work eventually formed the basis for his larger commentary 'al-Hidayah', which is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
بداية المبتدي (Badāyat al-Mubtadī): The title of al-Marghinani's work that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmi‘ al-Ṣaghīr): A collection of Hanafi rulings by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

C) Al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Siyar al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
Badayat al-Mubtadi is a compilation of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, serving as a concise introductory text for Hanafi students.

Introduction to Bidayat al-Mubtadi: Al-Marghinani's Compilation
Introduction to a Hanafi fiqh manual combining two core texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose and structure of Bidayat al-Mubtadi and identify its two source texts.

Core Idea
Bidayat al-Mubtadi combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir into one concise manual for Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson introduces the book Bidayat al-Mubtadi by Imam al-Marghinani. It is not a commentary but a compilation that merges two foundational Hanafi texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Shaybani. Understanding the purpose and sources of this work helps students appreciate its role in the Hanafi curriculum as a bridge between beginner and advanced study.

15- Bidayat al-Mubtadi is a compilation between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir (of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan).
By Imam al-Marghinani, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abi Bakr, who died in 593 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
It is a concise book, and his introduction reads:
(Praise be to Allah who guided us to the springs of His wisdom and granted us the seventh of His blessings, praise by which we gain His pleasure and increase His beneficence. And may Allah bless His Messenger Muhammad, whom Allah made a model for mankind in explaining His lawful and unlawful, and his family and companions, lamps of darkness and springs of wisdom, and grant them peace. The weak servant Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn Abd al-Halim al-Marghinani, may Allah guide him to what brings good remembrance and abundant reward, says: It occurred to me at the beginning of my state to have a book on fiqh containing all types of chapters, yet small in size but great in design, to be memorized by the beginner and reflected upon by the guided seeker.
And when I had the opportunity to travel in Iraq, I found the Mukhtasar attributed to al-Quduri to be the most beautiful book in concise and pleasing style.
And I saw the elders of the land beyond the river encouraging both young and old to memorize al-Jami' al-Saghir, so I decided to author a book combining both, not exceeding them except where necessity required and the frequency of occurrence compelled me. And I avoided repetition in it so that every resident and nomad would desire it.
And I named it 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi'.

384
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
And if I am successful in explaining it, I will name that explanation 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', for the beginning is knowledge of the foundations and the end is understanding the meanings.
And I considered the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir to be better, seeking blessing from what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan chose, and what is not mentioned in it, its place is near the chapter on sales, and after it within this collection. I undertook to combine the types to facilitate learning, and Allah is the granter of success to complete it, and He is the one sought for help to conclude it.) End quote. I copied this introduction from a manuscript copy of the book deposited in the 'Arif Hikmat Library in Medina, number (254/29) Hanafi fiqh, in 190 small-sized folios, a beautiful gilded copy but without a copying date. The book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' has been printed separately without al-Hidayah in Cairo, edited by Hamid Ibrahim and Muhammad Abd al-Wahhab Bahiri, edition 1355/1 AH.
As for the edition of al-Hidayah which is a commentary on it, and the edition of commentaries on al-Hidayah such as Fath al-Qadir and others, this introduction is not included.
The book has many manuscript copies; (59) copies are mentioned in al-Fihris al-Shamil (1).
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic introduction to the book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' by Imam al-Marghinani. It is taken from the third chapter of the current work, which discusses commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author states that 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' is a compilation combining two foundational Hanafi texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Shaybani. Al-Marghinani authored this concise work with the aim of creating a small-volume yet comprehensive manual suitable for beginners to memorize and advanced students to ponder. He explains that his motivation came from finding Mukhtasar al-Quduri excellent in its brevity and seeing widespread interest in memorizing al-Jami' al-Saghir among scholars of Transoxiana. The introduction also reveals that al-Marghinani intended to write a commentary on his own book titled 'Kifayat al-Muntahi' if he succeeded. He adopted the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir for its superior order and blessed nature. The passage concludes with notes on the manuscript source and printed editions of the work, indicating that the introduction was preserved in a manuscript in the 'Arif Hikmat Library in Medina. This type of front matter is often omitted from later printings of al-Hidayah (the famous commentary), but the author of the current work has included it for reference.

Key Terms
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual authored by al-Marghinani, compiling Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A collection of Hanafi fiqh rulings compiled by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, widely used as a primer.

The Relationship Between Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Bidayat al-Mubtadi, and al-Hidayah
Describes the compilation of Bidayat al-Mubtadi and the creation of al-Hidayah, with manuscript notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the textual lineage from Mukhtasar al-Quduri to al-Hidayah and identify the omission of the book of inheritance.

Core Idea
Al-Hidayah is a concise commentary based on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which itself merges al-Quduri with al-Jami' al-Saghir but omits faraid.

This lesson introduces three foundational Hanafi fiqh texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Bidayat al-Mubtadi, and al-Hidayah. Understanding their relationship helps students situate rulings and appreciate the pedagogical choices of Imam al-Marghinani. We will also explore a notable omission—the book of inheritance—that has implications for students relying solely on al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and the compilation
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the primary matn, and Bidayat al-Mubtadi combines it with al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad. Note the author's intention: to blend two authoritative sources.
2
Understand the commentary evolution
Al-Marghinani first planned a lengthy commentary (Kifayat al-Muntahi) but replaced it with a more concise one (al-Hidayah) to avoid verbosity. Compare the two approaches.
This shows the importance of practical usability in teaching texts.
3
Detect the textual omission
Observe that al-Marghinani omitted the book of inheritance (faraid) from al-Quduri when compiling Bidayat al-Mubtadi. Confirm that this omission carries over to al-Hidayah. Reflect on why this matters for students.
Students must consult other sources for faraid when using al-Hidayah.

And if I succeed in explaining it, I will name it: 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', because the beginning is knowledge of structures and the end is pausing at meanings. And I saw that the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir is best, blessed by what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan chose, and what is not mentioned in it, its place is just before sales, and after it in the midst of this collection. And I undertook therein to combine the genres, seeking ease of quotation, and Allah is the Grantor of success for its completion, and He is the One sought for help for its conclusion. End quote. I have transmitted this introduction from a manuscript copy of the book deposited in the 'Arif Hikmat Library in Madinah al-Munawwarah, under number (254/29) Hanafi fiqh, in (190) folios of small size, a beautiful gilded copy but without a copying date. And the book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' has been printed separately, without al-Hidayah, in Cairo, Egypt, edited by Hamid Ibrahim and Muhammad 'Abd al-Wahhab Bahiri, edition 1355/1 AH. As for the edition of al-Hidayah which is a commentary on it, and the edition of commentaries on al-Hidayah: Fath al-Qadir and others, this introduction does not appear in them. And the book has many manuscript copies, of which (59) are mentioned in the comprehensive index (1). And I draw attention here that al-Marghinani, when he combined al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, did not include all of al-Quduri, for he omitted from it the book of inheritance, and I do not know the reason for that; therefore you do not find in Bidayat al-Mubtadi nor in its commentary 'al-Hidayah' a book of inheritance, although it exists in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 16 - Al-Hidayah is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi. By Imam al-Marghinani Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr, died 593 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And al-Hidayah is considered among the commentaries on al-Quduri, because as mentioned, Bidayat al-Mubtadi combined al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Marghinani said in the introduction to al-Hidayah: 'He had fulfilled the promise at the beginning of Bidayat al-Mubtadi to explain it, by Allah's help, a commentary that I would name 'Kifayat al-Muntahi'; so I began it, and promise allows some leeway, and when I almost leaned on it as if finishing, I perceived in it some verbosity and feared that the book would be abandoned for that reason, so I turned my attention and concern to another commentary titled 'al-Hidayah', in which I combine, by Allah's help, the cream of narrations and the texts of knowledge, leaving aside excess in every chapter, avoiding this type of prolixity, with it encompassing principles upon which chapters are based. And I ask Allah to grant me success to complete it and to seal it for me with happiness after its conclusion...'. End quote. And thus the author al-Marghinani explained Bidayat al-Mubtadi in a large commentary.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the commentary 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri'. It begins the third chapter, which discusses the various commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author first quotes an earlier preface from a work he calls 'Kifayat al-Muntahi', explaining his methodology: he preferred the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, out of barakah, and he sought to combine related topics for ease of reference. He then notes that this preface is preserved in a manuscript in the 'Arif Hikmat Library in Madinah, describing the copy. He observes that the book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' was printed separately without al-Hidayah, and that al-Hidayah's printed editions do not contain this preface. Importantly, the author points out that al-Marghinani, when compiling Bidayat al-Mubtadi from al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, omitted the entire book of inheritance (faraid) from al-Quduri, and thus al-Hidayah also lacks a section on faraid. The passage then introduces al-Hidayah as a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, by Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH). Al-Marghinani's own introduction is quoted, where he explains that he initially planned a lengthy commentary called 'Kifayat al-Muntahi' but found it too verbose, so he instead wrote a more concise commentary named 'al-Hidayah', which aims to combine the essential narrations and principles while avoiding excess. This introduction gives us important historical and methodological context: al-Hidayah is a selective, practical commentary that prioritizes clarity and usability, and its omission of faraid is noted as a peculiarity inherited from its base text.

Key Terms
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): The title of a Hanafi fiqh compendium by al-Marghinani, which combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A famous Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Marghinani on his own work Bidayat al-Mubtadi; it is known for its concise yet comprehensive treatment.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A collection of Hanafi fiqh rulings by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The book of sales
B) The book of inheritance
C) The book of prayer
D) The book of marriage

Key Takeaway
Al-Hidayah, though comprehensive, omits the section on inheritance because its base text Bidayat al-Mubtadi omitted it from Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

The Omission of Fara'id in Bidayat al-Mubtadi
Historical textual note on omission of fara'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why al-Hidayah lacks a book on fara'id and identify the source text where fara'id is present.

Core Idea
Al-Marghinani omitted the Book of Fara'id from Bidayat al-Mubtadi, so al-Hidayah does not cover inheritance.

This passage records a curious but important fact: al-Marghinani, when compiling his text, omitted an entire book from al-Quduri's work. Understanding this helps students navigate the Hanafi curriculum and avoid confusion when using al-Hidayah for inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action
Al-Marghinani combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir into Bidayat al-Mubtadi.
2
Note the omission
He removed the Book of Fara'id from this compilation.
The reason is unknown.
3
Consequence for al-Hidayah
Since al-Hidayah is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, it also lacks a book on fara'id.
4
Source verification
The original Mukhtasar al-Quduri still contains the fara'id section.
5
Practical implication
When studying inheritance, refer to Mukhtasar al-Quduri or other dedicated texts, not al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
٣٨٥
وأنبه هنا إلى أن المرغيناني حين جمع بين القدوري والجامع الصغير في بداية المبتدي ، لم يضم ما في القدوري كله، فقد حذف منه كتاب الفرائض، ولا أدري ما سبب ذلك، ولهذا لا تجد في بداية المبتدي، ولا في شرحه: «الهداية» كتاباً للفرائض، مع أنه موجود في مختصر القدوري.
١٦ - الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي .
للإمام المرغيناني أبي الحسن علي بن أبي بكر، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٣هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وتعتبر الهداية من شروح القدوري، لما تقدم من أن بداية المبتدي جمع بين القدوري والجامع الصغير
قال المرغيناني في مقدمة الهداية :
وقد جرى على الوعد في مبدأ بداية المبتدي أن أشرحها بتوفيق الله تعالى شرحاً أرسمه ب: «كفاية المنتهي»، فشرعت فيه، والوعد يسوغ بعض المساغ ، وحين أكاد أتكـي عنـه اتكاء الفراغ، تبيَّنت فيه نبذاً من الإطناب وخشيت أن يُهجر لأجله الكتاب، فصرفت العنان والعناية إلى شرح آخر موسوم بـ: «الهداية»، أجمع فيه بتوفيق الله تعالى بين عيون الرواية، ومتون الدراية، تاركاً للزوائد في كل باب، معرضاً عن هذا النوع من الإسهاب، مع ما أنه يشتمل على أصول تنسحب عليها فصول، وأسأل الله تعالى أن يوفقني لإتمامها، ويختم لي بالسعادة بعد اختتامها....». اهـ
وهكذا شرح المؤلف المرغيناني بداية المبتدي» شرحاً كبيراً في نحو ثمانين مجلداً ، سماه : كفاية المنتهي»، ولما تبين فيه الإطناب، وخشي أن يُهجر لأجله الكتاب، شرحه شرحاً مختصراً لطيفاً نافعاً وافياً، بالغاً في الحُسن والتقرير والتحرير والضبط والإتقان، وسماه: «الهداية».
وبالجملة فهو كتاب فاخر ، لم تكتحل عين الزمان بما فيه، كما قال صاحب الوقاية(1).
والهداية في الحقيقة كالشرح لمختصر القدوري، والجامع الصغير، ... ووظيفته أن يشرح مسائل الجامع الصغير والقدوري، وإذا قال صاحب الهداية : قال في الكتاب : أراد القدوري (٢). اهـ (۲)
وعلى الهداية شروح كثيرة جداً، وهي في الحقيقة كلها شروح لمختصر القدوري، لكونه مضمناً في بداية المبتدي»، الذي هو أصل الهداية.
ومن أشهر شروح الهداية: البناية للعيني، وفتح القدير لابن الهمام، والكفاية للخوارزمي والعناية للبابرتي، وهذه كلها مطبوعة. ومنها : غاية البيان للإتقاني والنهاية للسغناقي، والغاية للسروجي، وهذه كلها مخطوطة، وغيرها كثير. فمن أراد شرح شيء من مختصر القدوري وَجَدَ غناءً كبيراً وافياً (1) ينظر مفتاح السعادة لطاش كبري ٢٣٨/٢. (۲) كشف الظنون ۲۰۳۲/۲
The Third Chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 385. And I draw attention here to the fact that al-Marghinani, when he combined al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, did not include all of what is in al-Quduri. Indeed, he omitted from it the Book of Fara'id, and I do not know the reason for that. Thus you do not find in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, nor in its commentary al-Hidayah, a book on fara'id, even though it exists in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 16 - Al-Hidayah, commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi. By Imam al-Marghinani, Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr, died 593 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And al-Hidayah is considered among the commentaries of al-Quduri, because of what preceded that Bidayat al-Mubtadi combines al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Marghinani said in the introduction of al-Hidayah: I had proceeded upon the promise at the beginning of Bidayat al-Mubtadi that I would explain it, with the help of Allah, with a commentary that I would title 'Kifayat al-Muntahi'. So I began it, and a promise allows some leeway. And when I was about to lean upon it with the leaning of completion, I discerned in it some prolixity and feared that the book would be abandoned because of it. So I turned my reins and attention to another commentary titled 'al-Hidayah', in which I combine, with the help of Allah, the choicest narrations and the texts of understanding, leaving out excess in every chapter, turning away from this type of elaboration, while it includes principles upon which sections are drawn. And I ask Allah to grant me success in completing it and to seal it with happiness after its conclusion... end quote. Thus the author al-Marghinani explained Bidayat al-Mubtadi with a large commentary of about eighty volumes, naming it Kifayat al-Muntahi. When its prolixity became evident and he feared that the book would be abandoned because of it, he explained it with a concise, beneficial, sufficient commentary, excellent in beauty, elucidation, refinement, precision, and mastery, and named it al-Hidayah. In summary, it is a splendid book; the eye of time has never seen its like, as the author of al-Wiqayah said. And al-Hidayah is in reality like a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir... and its function is to explain the matters of al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Quduri. When the author of al-Hidayah says 'he said in the book', he means al-Quduri (2). End. And upon al-Hidayah there are very many commentaries, and they are in reality all commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, because it is included in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which is the basis of al-Hidayah. Among the most famous commentaries on al-Hidayah are: al-Binayah by al-'Ayni, Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam, al-Kifayah by al-Khwarizmi, and al-'Inayah by al-Babarti; these are all printed. Among them are: Ghayat al-Bayan by al-Ittiqani, al-Nihayah by al-Sighnaqi, and al-Ghayah by al-Saruji; these are all in manuscript, and many others. So whoever wants an explanation of some part of Mukhtasar al-Quduri will find ample and sufficient enrichment. (1) See Miftah al-Sa'adah by Tash Kubri, 2/238. (2) Kashf al-Zunun, 2/2032.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview from the work 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' explaining the relationship between key Hanafi legal texts. The author notes that al-Marghinani, when compiling 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', did not include all of al-Quduri's text; specifically, he omitted the Book of Fara'id (inheritance). Consequently, neither 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' nor its famous commentary 'al-Hidayah' contains a section on fara'id, although the original 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' does. This highlights that 'al-Hidayah' is not a complete commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' but on the combined text of 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi'. The passage then quotes al-Marghinani's introduction to 'al-Hidayah', where he explains his initial plan to write a large commentary called 'Kifayat al-Muntahi' in about eighty volumes, but due to its prolixity, he feared the original text would be abandoned. Therefore, he wrote a concise yet comprehensive commentary, 'al-Hidayah', which became highly authoritative. The passage emphasizes that 'al-Hidayah' functions as a commentary on both 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and 'al-Jami' al-Saghir'. It then lists famous commentaries on 'al-Hidayah' itself, such as 'al-Binayah' by al-'Ayni, 'Fath al-Qadir' by Ibn al-Humam, 'al-Kifayah' by al-Khwarizmi, and 'al-'Inayah' by al-Babarti (all printed), and others in manuscript. This demonstrates the centrality of 'al-Hidayah' in the Hanafi tradition and provides a roadmap for students seeking detailed explanations of 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'.

Key Terms
الهداية (al-Hidayah): The famous Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Marghinani on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani that amalgamates Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri, widely used as a foundational text.
كتاب الفرائض (Kitab al-Fara'id): The book of inheritance law, omitted from Bidayat al-Mubtadi by al-Marghinani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Hidayah not contain a book on fara'id?
A) Al-Marghinani considered fara'id unimportant.
B) Al-Marghinani omitted the Book of Fara'id from Bidayat al-Mubtadi.
C) The section on fara'id was lost during transmission.
D) Al-Hidayah is a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir only.

Key Takeaway
Al-Hidayah does not cover fara'id because al-Marghinani omitted it from its base text, Bidayat al-Mubtadi.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
From Kifayat al-Muntahi to al-Hidayah: The Art of Concise Commentary
Biographical note on al-Marghinani's commentary writing process

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Marghinani wrote al-Hidayah after initially writing Kifayat al-Muntahi and identify the key features of al-Hidayah as a commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Marghinani replaced his massive commentary Kifayat al-Muntahi with the concise al-Hidayah to avoid prolixity and ensure the text's usability.

This passage reveals the author's own process: he started a huge commentary but feared it would cause the original text to be abandoned. So he wrote a balanced, concise commentary that became the standard. This teaches us the purpose of commentary in the Hanafi tradition: not to overwhelm but to clarify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial project
Al-Marghinani first wrote a large commentary called Kifayat al-Muntahi, about eighty volumes.
2
Recognize the problem
He noticed prolixity (الإطناب) and feared the original text would be abandoned due to its length.
3
Understand the solution
He wrote a new concise commentary, al-Hidayah, to replace it.
4
Note the features of al-Hidayah
It combines the best narrations and understanding, leaving out excess, while covering essential principles.
5
Recognize its status
Al-Hidayah became the authoritative text upon which many later commentaries were written.

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview from the work 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' explaining the relationship between key Hanafi legal texts. The author notes that al-Marghinani, when compiling 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', did not include all of al-Quduri's text; specifically, he omitted the Book of Fara'id (inheritance). الهداية (al-Hidayah): The famous Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Marghinani on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani that amalgamates Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri, widely used as a foundational text.
كفاية المنتهي (Kifayat al-Muntahi): The first, large commentary by al-Marghinani on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, around 80 volumes, later replaced by al-Hidayah.
الإطناب (al-Itnab): Prolixity or excessive length in writing.

Why did al-Marghinani write al-Hidayah despite already having Kifayat al-Muntahi?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Status of Al-Hidayah in Hanafi Fiqh
Historical description of al-Hidayah's origin and commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between al-Hidayah and Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify the major commentaries on al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Al-Hidayah is the central Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and its commentaries are key to mastering the madhhab.

Al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani is one of the most important texts in the Hanafi school. It was written as a concise commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri after a longer work proved too lengthy. This lesson explores the origins of al-Hidayah, its relationship to earlier texts, and the extensive commentarial tradition it generated, highlighting its enduring role in Hanafi teaching and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the origin of al-Hidayah
The passage tells us that al-Hidayah was written as a concise commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, after a longer commentary called Kifayat al-Muntahi (eighty volumes) risked causing the original texts to be abandoned. Identify the problem that led to al-Hidayah's composition.
The author feared prolixity (الإطناب) would deter students.
2
Identify the relationship between al-Hidayah and Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Al-Hidayah is explicitly called a commentary (شرح) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage notes that when al-Marghinani says 'he said in the book,' he means al-Quduri. Also, commentaries on al-Hidayah are effectively commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri because al-Hidayah incorporates Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which is based on the earlier works.
This makes al-Hidayah a gateway to the earlier foundational texts.
3
List the most famous commentaries on al-Hidayah
The passage names several well-known commentaries: al-Binayah by al-'Ayni, Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam, al-Kifayah by al-Khwarizmi, and al-'Inayah by al-Babarti (all printed). Also, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Nihayah, and al-Ghayah (manuscripts). Recognize that these commentaries are a rich resource for studying al-Hidayah and, by extension, Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Many of these are still studied today.
4
Analyze the praise for al-Hidayah
The passage quotes Imam al-'Ayni and Imam al-Babarti praising al-Hidayah as central to teaching and fatwa. Note the phrases: 'the reference of teachers' and 'pride of muftis'. This indicates its authoritative status in the Hanafi school.
Such praise shows its acceptance among scholars.
5
Reflect on the significance for a Hanafi student today
Understanding this history helps a student appreciate why al-Hidayah is a core text. When studying any issue in Hanafi fiqh, one often turns to al-Hidayah and its commentaries, which are built upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri and other early works.
This lesson connects textual study to madhhab history.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Approximately eighty volumes, he named it: Kifayat al-Muntahi. But when prolixity became apparent in it, and he feared that the book might be abandoned for that reason, he commented on it with a brief, elegant, beneficial, comprehensive commentary, reaching the utmost in beauty, explanation, refinement, precision, and perfection, and he named it:
'Al-Hidayah'.
In short, it is a splendid book; the eye of time has not seen its like, as the author of al-Wiqayah said.
And al-Hidayah is in fact a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, ... and its function is to explain the issues of al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Quduri. When the author of al-Hidayah says: 'He said in the book,' he means al-Quduri.
(2)
And there are very many commentaries on al-Hidayah, which are in fact all commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, because it is included in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which is the basis of al-Hidayah.
Among the most famous commentaries on al-Hidayah are: al-Binayah by al-'Ayni, Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam, al-Kifayah by al-Khwarizmi, and al-'Inayah by al-Babarti; all of these are printed. Among them are: Ghayat al-Bayan by al-Ittiqani, al-Nihayah by al-Sighnaqi, and al-Ghayah by al-Saruji; all of these are manuscripts, and many others. Whoever wants a commentary on something from Mukhtasar al-Quduri will find great and complete sufficiency in the commentaries on al-Hidayah. The space here does not allow listing these commentaries.
387
And the book al-Hidayah achieved great acceptance among scholars, and they praised it with great fragrant praise, indicating its high and eminent status in the madhhab. Among those praises are:
What Imam al-'Ayni said in the introduction to al-Binayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah:
'... Indeed, the book al-Hidayah has delighted the scholars of the predecessors and been a source of pride for the virtuous among the successors, until it became the reference of teachers in their schools and the pride of muftis in their assemblies. They have never ceased to occupy themselves with it in every time and study it in every time, because it contains the treasure of subtleties, gathers the symbols of realities, includes the chosen fatwas, is sufficient in the essence of the secrets of al-Hawi, adequate in encompassing events, curative in answering occurrences, founded on amazing principles, detailed with strange benefits, established on clear foundations, solid chapters, abundant issues, many proofs, elegant arrangement, and true composition...'
And Imam al-Babarti said in the introduction to al-'Inayah:
'... After this: Indeed, the book al-Hidayah is the essence of guidance, because it contains the principles of knowledge and includes the texts of narration. Its verbal mines are purified...'
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a historical and bibliographical discussion from the second volume of 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It focuses on the central role of al-Hidayah as a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its numerous commentaries. The author first explains that a lengthy commentary called 'Kifayat al-Muntahi' was initially written in about eighty volumes, but due to its prolixity, it was feared that the original text would be abandoned. Therefore, a concise yet comprehensive commentary was produced and named 'al-Hidayah'. He then quotes the author of al-Wiqayah praising the book. Al-Hidayah is described as a commentary on both Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, and when the author of al-Hidayah says 'he said in the book', he means al-Quduri. The passage then lists the most famous commentaries on al-Hidayah, mentioning both printed and manuscript ones, emphasizing that these are effectively commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri because al-Hidayah is based on Bidayat al-Mubtadi. Finally, the passage cites two major scholars, Imam al-'Ayni and Imam al-Babarti, praising al-Hidayah in the introductions to their own commentaries (al-Binayah and al-'Inayah). This shows the immense respect and acceptance al-Hidayah enjoyed among Hanafi scholars, serving as a primary reference for teaching and fatwa.

Key Terms
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): A concise commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, which became a central Hanafi text.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise fiqh text by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a standard primer for the Hanafi school.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): An intermediate text by al-Marghinani that serves as the basis for al-Hidayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between al-Hidayah and Mukhtasar al-Quduri according to the passage?
A) Al-Hidayah is an independent work unrelated to Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
B) Al-Hidayah is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
C) Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a commentary on al-Hidayah.
D) Al-Hidayah is a summary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Takeaway
Al-Hidayah is the central Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and its numerous commentaries form the backbone of Hanafi fiqh study.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Significance of Al-Hidayah and Early Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describes the acceptance of Al-Hidayah and lists its early commentators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the canonical status of Al-Hidayah in the Hanafi madhhab and name two early commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri with their authors.

Core Idea
Al-Hidayah became the central Hanafi text due to its comprehensiveness, elegant arrangement, and reliance on preferred fatwas.

This passage introduces the immense scholarly acceptance of Al-Hidayah, quoting vivid praises from two later commentators. It also mentions two lesser-known early commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, giving us a glimpse into the rich tradition of Hanafi legal writing. Understanding this context helps you appreciate why Al-Hidayah remains a core reference for Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
Recognize that this is front matter: the author is establishing the authority of Al-Hidayah and recording its commentators.
2
Analyze the praises of Al-Hidayah
Read the quotes from al-'Ayni and al-Babarti. Note what each emphasizes: comprehensiveness, elegant structure, reliability for fatwa.
Al-'Ayni calls it 'the mainstay of teachers'; al-Babarti says it 'emerges like pure gold'.
3
List the two mentioned commentaries
Extract the names: Al-Musta'dhab by al-Kirmani, and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Qadi (al-'Awfi).
Al-Kirmani is also known for his work on manasik (hajj rituals).
4
Understand the chain of transmission
Note that these commentaries are built upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which Al-Hidayah also explains. This shows the layered tradition of Hanafi scholarship.
Al-Hidayah itself is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Regarding the commentaries on Al-Hidayah, there is no room here to list them all.
387
And the book Al-Hidayah gained great acceptance among the scholars, and they praised it with great fragrance, indicating its high and distinguished status in the madhhab. Among those praises:
What Imam al-'Ayni said in the introduction to Al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah:
'... Indeed, the book Al-Hidayah has been delighted in by the scholars of the predecessors and boasted of by the elites of the successors, until it became the mainstay of teachers in their schools and the pride of the references in their gatherings. They have never ceased to be occupied with it in every time and to study it in every time, because it contains the treasure of subtleties, gathers the symbols of realities, includes the preferred fatwas, suffices in encompassing the occurring events, and is sufficient in answering actual incidents. It is founded on amazing principles and detailed with strange benefits, built on clear foundations, solid chapters, abundant issues, numerous evidences, an elegant arrangement, and a true composition...' End quote.
And Imam al-Babarti said in the introduction to Al-'Inayah:
'... To proceed: The book Al-Hidayah is deserving of guidance, for it contains the principles of knowledge and encompasses the texts of transmission. Its verbal mines are purified from the foulness of verbosity, and its meaning coins are free from the falseness of brevity and the innovations of prolixity. So it emerges like pure gold, composed of concise meaning; its sweetness runs through the joints, its delicacy in thoughts, and its newness in minds...' End quote.
17 – Al-Musta'dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri.
By al-Kirmani Muhammad ibn Mukarram ibn Sha'ban, the Hanafi jurist, author of 'Al-Masalik fi al-Manasik', died in 593 AH, or other reports, may Allah have mercy on him.
The author himself mentioned this commentary in his book Al-Masalik.
And al-Baghdadi mentioned it in Hadiyyat al-'Arifin.
18 – Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
By Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi 'Awf, the jurist known as al-Qadi, from the scholars of Yemen. 'Ali al-Qari mentioned this commentary in his Tabaqat and said: 'It is the commentary known among the Hanafis as (al-Qadi).'
He did not mention his year of death, which is before 597 AH.
I found that al-Kirmani, author of Al-Masalik, frequently quoted from him, calling it 'Sharh al-Quduri lil-'Awfi'. The death of al-Kirmani is disputed.

Commentary
This passage is front matter from a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, specifically discussing the significance of the work Al-Hidayah and listing some of its many commentaries. The author first notes the immense acceptance and praise Al-Hidayah received from scholars, quoting two prominent Hanafi scholars: Imam al-'Ayni in his introduction to Al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah, and Imam al-Babarti in his introduction to Al-'Inayah. Both praises highlight the comprehensiveness, elegant organization, and authoritative fatwas contained in Al-Hidayah, marking it as a central text in the Hanafi school. Then, the author lists two specific commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: (1) Al-Musta'dhab fi Sharh al-Quduri by al-Kirmani (d. 593 AH), who also wrote Al-Masalik fi al-Manasik; and (2) Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Hasan ibn Abi 'Awf, known as al-Qadi, who died before 597 AH. It is noted that al-Kirmani frequently quoted from al-Qadi's commentary. The passage serves as a historical and bibliographical note on the scholarly tradition of commenting on al-Quduri's text.

Key Terms
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): A foundational Hanafi legal text (matn) by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, widely studied and commented upon.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Ahmad al-Quduri, which Al-Hidayah is a commentary upon.
المستعذب (Al-Musta'dhab): A specific commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Kirmani.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Transmission of Hanafi Texts: Printing History of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri
Historical and editorial description of publication history and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the printing history of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri and identify key manuscript and commentary sources that guarantee the reliable transmission of a Hanafi fiqh text.

Core Idea
The preservation of Hanafi fiqh depends on careful manuscript transmission and critical scholarly editions.

This passage from the modern edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri provides a window into the book's publication history and the scholarly efforts to preserve and comment upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding these editorial details helps you appreciate the chain of transmission (sanad) through which Hanafi fiqh has reached us.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first edition
Locate the date and place of the first printing of al-Lubab. The text states it was printed in 1318 AH (1901 CE) in Kazan, Russia.
2
Note the later defective edition
Identify the Riyadh edition (1428 AH) and understand why it is considered corrupt (saleem).
3
Trace the scholarly work on this text
Recognize that a doctoral thesis by Sheikh Jasim Qaranfil was left incomplete, and the project was distributed to three master's students.
4
Recognize manuscript copies
Take note of the manuscript copies mentioned: one dated 671 AH in Murad Mulla Library, another from 695 AH in Jarullah Library, and a very old copy from 545 AH mentioned by al-Qurashi.
5
Understand the commentary tradition
Identify Ibn al-Turkumani's Sharh Khulasat al-Dala'il as a commentary on al-Razi's work, and note that Ibn al-Turkumani wrote three ta'aliq (annotations) on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
۳۹۱
ولا اقتحم، ولا اغتمض حقاً ولا اهتضم فمَن أشبه أباه فما ظَلَم. وفقنا الله لما يحبه ويرضاه وصانَنَا ممَّن اقتحم ما يكرهه ويأباه، وجعل ما نقصده ونتوخاه ونلتمسه ونرومه خالصاً لوجهه، وطلباً لجزيل ثوابه، وتحرزاً من أليم عقابه وما توفيقي إلا بالله، عليـه توکلت، وإليه أنيب». اهـ
وقد طبع الكتاب طبعته الأولى سنة (۱۳۱۸هـ = ۱۹۰۱م)، في (۳۲۰) صفحة، في مطابع محمد جان الكريمي وشقيقيه شريف وحسن، في بلدة قازان بروسيا، وهي طبعة مصححة جيدة، ووَضَعَ عليها طابعها بعض التعليقات الموضحة.
وطبع مؤخراً في مكتبة الرشد في الرياض، سنة ١٤٢٨هـ، وهي طبعة سقيمة مليئة بالأخطاء والتصحيفات.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. 391. ... He said: '... and success is only from Allah, upon Him I rely and to Him I turn.' End quote. The book was first printed in 1318 AH = 1901 CE, in 320 pages, in the presses of Muhammad Jan al-Karimi and his two brothers Sharif and Hasan, in the town of Kazan in Russia, a corrected and good edition, and some explanatory comments were placed on its edition. And it was printed recently in Maktabat al-Rushd in Riyadh, in 1428 AH, a corrupt edition full of errors and distortions. Our colleague Sheikh Jasim Qaranfil, may Allah have mercy on him, from Turkish brothers who studied with us at Umm al-Qura University, had presented it as a subject for his doctoral dissertation in the specialization of fiqh, and made progress in serving it, but he died young before completing the work. Then this book was registered and distributed to three students in evening postgraduate studies at the master's level at Umm al-Qura University, and their theses were discussed. The book has many manuscript copies, see al-Fihris al-Shamil (1). (1) 3/1037, and it mentions sixty copies. ... 392. Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Among them is a copy dated 671 AH in the Murad Mulla Library in Istanbul (903), and a copy in the Jarullah Library in Istanbul, written in 695 AH. Al-Qurashi mentioned at the end of the introduction to his book Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa that he saw in the Khanqah of Sa'd al-Su'ada in its library a copy of al-Khulasa with him, its date of writing: the year five and forty and five hundred. End quote. 20 - Sharh Khulasat al-Dala'il (and Khulasat al-Dala'il is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Razi). By 'Ala' al-Din ibn al-Turkumani al-Mardini Ahmad ibn Sahib al-Jawhar al-Naqi, died 744 AH, and it is said 745 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. 'Allamah Qasim said: Ibn al-Turkumani has three ta'aliq on Khulasat al-Dala'il by al-Razi: The first: in solving its problems, clarifying its difficulties, and explaining its words.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the modern edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, discussing the publication history of the book and a specific commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author first quotes a concluding prayer from the original work, then describes the first edition (Kazan, 1318 AH/1901 CE) and a later defective edition from Riyadh. He mentions a deceased colleague's unfinished doctoral work on this book and its distribution to master's students. The passage then lists manuscript copies, including one dated 671 AH and another from 695 AH. Finally, it introduces the commentary 'Sharh Khulasat al-Dala'il' by Ibn al-Turkumani (d. 744/745 AH), noting his three annotations on al-Razi's Khulasat al-Dala'il, the first of which explains its difficulties and words. This is purely historical/biographical content, not a fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). This book is the subject of the commentary al-Lubab.
خلاصة الدلائل (Khulasat al-Dala'il): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri written by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (d. 606 AH), though he was a Shafi'i scholar. The text mentions it as a source for further commentary.
تعليق (ta'liq): An annotation or gloss on a text, often explaining difficulties and adding clarifications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The reliable transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts requires careful attention to manuscript provenance and the quality of printed editions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Takmila: A Supplement to Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describing the Takmila and its commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose, structure, and scholarly contribution of al-Razi's Takmila and its commentary, and identify how this work fits into the Hanafi pedagogical tradition.

Core Idea
The Takmila supplements Quduri with scattered issues from other mukhtasarat; its commentary adds proofs from Hanafi masters.

The Hanafi school has a rich tradition of commentaries and supplements that build upon core texts. One such work is the Takmila by Husam al-Din al-Razi, designed to complete Mukhtasar al-Quduri by incorporating related issues from other authoritative Hanafi summaries. This lesson explores the author's methodology and the value of this layered scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his works
Locate Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH) in the text and note the two books attributed to him: al-Takmila and Sharh al-Takmila.
Author's full name: 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Razi.
2
Understand the motivation for the Takmila
Read the author's own words: he collected 'what was scattered' from issues in other mukhtasarat (like al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi) and arranged them according to Quduri's order, without unnecessary repetition.
This shows the Takmila is a complementary work, not a standalone manual.
3
Analyze the structure of the Takmila
Notice that al-Razi organized the material 'according to the order of his book' (Quduri) and 'according to the homogeneity of its chapters'. He avoided repeating issues unless needed for clarification or detail.
The goal was seamless integration with Quduri.
4
Examine the motivation for the commentary (Sharh al-Takmila)
After presenting the Takmila to students, they requested proofs (dala'il) from the great imams. Al-Razi complied, adding concise proofs to make the work more beneficial.
This highlights the pedagogical expectation that every ruling should be supported by evidence.
5
Assess the significance in Hanafi tradition
The author claims that studying the Takmila after Quduri is like reading five mukhtasarat combined – a powerful endorsement. The existence of early manuscripts shows its widespread use.
This work represents a typical 'layered' learning approach in Hanafi madrasas.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
I wanted to collect what was scattered from the arrangement of his book from the issues published in the mukhtasarat of our companions, such as al-Jami' al-Saghir, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Irshad, and Mujaz al-Farghani.
So I picked them out and arranged them according to the order of his book, and I organized them according to the homogeneity of its chapters,
6
without repeating an issue or reposing a difficulty, except what was difficult to mention without repeating what he mentioned, or it was a detail of what he summarized or a notification of what he omitted, or there was in it an increase of clarification or a narration of someone's statement... and the like and it runs
,
in its manner. So that it may be a completion (takmila) to his classification, and a supplement to his authorship, for it completes the benefits of al-Quduri. So whoever studies it and understands it after having memorized al-Quduri and learned it, is like one who has read the five mukhtasarat and combined the light of the planets and the sun (1). End.
There exist of this Takmila several excellent old copies; see for them (2) al-Fihris al-Shamil. Among these copies is a precious copy in 169 folios, which was read to the author, and its copying was completed in 586 AH, and another in 190 folios, written in 608 AH.
Imam 'Abd al-Qadir al-Qurashi mentioned this Takmila in his book: (1) This introduction was written to me, transmitted from a manuscript in the Suleymaniye Library in Istanbul, by the noble virtuous brother, Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya, may Allah reward him well. 2 (0746/4)
[PAGE_397]
Chapter Three: Commentaries on al-Quduri
397
'Tahdhib al-Asma' al-Waqi'a fi al-Hidaya wa al-Khulasa' (1), after he mentioned the book of Husam al-Din al-Razi, Khulasat al-Dala'il, then said: He has another book in the madhhab which he named 'al-Takmila': it is famous among the companions, and he also has 'Sharh al-Takmila'. End.
25- Commentary on Takmila al-Quduri.
By Husam al-Din al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad, died 598 AH,
May Allah Almighty have mercy on him.
It was mentioned earlier that Husam al-Din al-Razi authored Takmila al-Quduri, then wrote a commentary on this Takmila. In the author's introduction to this commentary he said:
'After praising Allah the Generous for His favors and thanking Him for His bounties and gifts, and prayers upon Muhammad, the master of His messengers and the seal of His prophets, and satisfaction upon the noble ones from his Companions and relatives:
When I wrote the book al-Takmila, I presented it to some fiqh students, and they approved of it and were pleased with it, and were amazed by it and enjoyed it. They asked me to add to those issues some proofs extracted from the speech of the great imams, in a concise and brief manner, so that it would be more complete in benefit and more perfect in return. So I responded to that, seeking help from Allah, relying upon Him, and desiring from Him what is with Him. And my success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely and to Him I return. (2)
(1) p. 51.
6
6
(2) From the introduction of a manuscript copy, obtained through the noble brother, Professor 'Ammar'
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic entry from the 'Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. It discusses the 'Takmila' (Completion) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri authored by Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH) and his subsequent commentary on it. The author of the Lubab cites the introduction of the Takmila, where al-Razi explains his motivation: He collected scattered issues from various mukhtasarat of the Hanafi school (like al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, etc.) and arranged them according to the order of Quduri's work, avoiding repetition except where necessary for clarification. This work was intended as a complementary supplement (takmila) to Quduri. Later, at the request of students, al-Razi wrote a commentary (Sharh al-Takmila) that added proofs (dala'il) extracted from the great Hanafi imams, presented concisely. The text also notes the existence of several old manuscripts and mentions that 'Abd al-Qadir al-Qurashi referenced the Takmila in his biography of Hanafi scholars. This passage is purely informational, providing context about the transmission and reception of Hanafi legal works.

Key Terms
التكملة (al-Takmila): The title of a work by Husam al-Din al-Razi that supplements Mukhtasar al-Quduri with additional issues from other Hanafi mukhtasarat.
شرح التكملة (Sharh al-Takmila): The commentary written by al-Razi on his own Takmila, adding proofs to the issues compiled.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely memorized and commented upon.
حسام الدين الرازي (Husam al-Din al-Razi): This passage identifies him as 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Razi, d. 598 AH, author of al-Takmila and its commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what motivated al-Razi to write the Sharh al-Takmila?
A) He realized the Takmila was incomplete without evidence.
B) Students requested that he add proofs to the issues.
C) He wanted to refute the opinions of other madhhabs.
D) A publisher asked him to expand the work.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's Takmila and its commentary exemplify how Hanafi scholars composed complementary works to enrich the study of core texts, emphasizing the importance of evidence in legal education.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Commentary Tradition of Al-Quduri
Bibliographic listing of commentaries on Al-Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key commentaries on Al-Quduri and explain their relationship to the base text and to each other.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is the foundation; commentaries complete, combine, and preserve Hanafi rulings.

This passage from Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri lists important commentaries on the foundational Hanafi matn. Understanding this chain helps you appreciate how later scholars built upon earlier works, preserving and expanding the madhhab. It also introduces you to the concept of a 'takmila' (completion) and a 'jama' (compilation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Text
Recognize that all listed works are commentaries on or supplements to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise manual of Hanafi fiqh.
Al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) authored this matn which became a core text in the Hanafi curriculum.
2
Distinguish Commentary Types
Note three types: a sharh (commentary) on a takmila, a compilation of benefits from two works, and a comprehensive collection combining both.
3
Analyze al-Fawa'id al-Mushtamila
Al-Mawsili's work uniquely adds the disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, which were omitted by both al-Quduri and al-Razi.
This shows how later works fill gaps in earlier ones.
4
Recognize Manuscript Evidence
The mention of specific manuscript locations and collation details indicates the scholarly effort to preserve reliable copies.
Manuscripts were often copied during the author's lifetime or collated with his original.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح . القدوري
* وتوجد نسخة من هذا الشرح في المكتبة الوطنية في باريس بفرنسا، تقع في (۲۳۲) ورقة ، كتبت في القرن الثامن، ينظر لها الفهرست الشامل .
كما توجد منه نسخة نفيسة في مكتبة فاتح بالسليمانية في اسطنبول، برقم (١٥٣٤) ، كُتبت في حياة المؤلف سنة ٥٩٤هـ في (۲۸۰) ورقة، وقوبلت بنسخة المؤلف .
٢٦- شرح تكملة القدوري التكملة لحسام الدين الرازي.
لرشيد الدين محمد بن عمر بن عبد الله الصانع السنجي النيسابوري الحنفي، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٨هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى.
٢٧ الفوائد المشتملة على المختصر والتكملة .
للإمام أبي الفضل عبد الله بن محمود الموصلي، صاحب «الاختيار»، المتوفى سنة ٦٨٣هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى. جمع فيه فوائد مختصر القدوري والتكملة لحسام الدين الرازي، وزاد فيه ما أغفلاه من الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه.
ومنه نسخة مقابلة مصححة، كتبت من نسخة بخط المؤلف سنة ٨٥٦هـ ، في مكتبة يني جامع في اسطنبول، برقم (٥٣٤)، وتقع في (۱۳۹) ورقة، نقلاً عن نوادر المخطوطات في مكتبات تركيا.
۲۸ - العقود المفصلة في الجمع بين القدوري والتكملة .
للإمام أحمد بن محمد بن حسن العباسي، المتوفى بعد سنة ٨٩٨هـ، وهي سنة شروعه في جَمْع الكتاب، كما صرح في مقدمته، والمراد بالتكملة : تكملة القدوري لحسام الدين الرازي صاحب خلاصة الدلائل، (ت ٥٩٨هـ). ذكره الزركلي في الأعلام، وذكر له نسخة في مكتبة عارف حكمت بالمدينة المنورة برقم (۱۹۰) فقه حنفي. وقد راجعت مكتبة عارف حكمت فوجدتُ النسخة برقم جديد هو (٢٥٤/٢١٤)، ورقم الحفظ (١٢٨٠). وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف: الحمد لله الذي منح بفيض الفضل من شاء من العباد، ووفقه لطرق الهداية والرشاد، ... وبعد : فإن الشيخ الإمام القدوري ألف
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Al-Quduri.
* A copy of this commentary exists in the National Library in Paris, France, consisting of 232 folios, written in the eighth century; see al-Fihris al-Shamil.
Also, a precious copy exists in the Fatih Library at al-Sulaymaniyya in Istanbul, number 1534, written during the author's lifetime in the year 594 AH, in 280 folios, and collated with the author's copy.
26- Sharh Takmilat al-Quduri: The Takmila by Husam al-Din al-Razi.
By Rashid al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar ibn Abd Allah al-Sani' al-Sinji al-Naysaburi al-Hanafi, died 598 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
27- al-Fawa'id al-Mushtamila 'ala al-Mukhtasar wa al-Takmila.
By Imam Abu al-Fadl Abd Allah ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili, author of al-Ikhtiyar, died 683 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He compiled in it the benefits of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Takmila of Husam al-Din al-Razi, and added what both omitted regarding the disagreement between the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his two companions.
From it there is a corrected collated copy, written from a copy in the author's hand in the year 856 AH, in the Yeni Cami Library in Istanbul, number 534, consisting of 139 folios, transmitted from Nawadir al-Makhtutat fi Maktabat Turkiya.
28- al-Uqud al-Mufassala fi al-Jam' bayn al-Quduri wa al-Takmila.
By Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Abbasi, died after 898 AH, which is the year he began compiling the book, as he stated in his introduction. The meaning of al-Takmila is: Takmilat al-Quduri by Husam al-Din al-Razi, author of Khulasat al-Dala'il, d. 598 AH. Mentioned by al-Zirikli in al-A'lam, and he mentioned that a copy exists in the Arif Hikmat Library in Medina, number 190, Hanafi fiqh. I have checked the Arif Hikmat Library and found the copy with a new number 254/214 and shelf number 1280. In the author's introduction: 'Praise be to Allah who has granted by the flow of grace whom He wills of servants, and guided them to the paths of guidance and rectitude... After this: Shaykh al-Imam al-Quduri authored...'
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical listing from the front matter of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri, documenting various commentaries and manuscript copies of the Quduri mukhtasar. The author first notes a copy of the commentary (likely Al-Lubab itself) in Paris and a precious copy in Istanbul written during the author's lifetime and collated with his original. Then he lists three specific works: (26) a commentary on the Takmila by Rashid al-Din al-Sinji al-Naysaburi; (27) al-Fawa'id al-Mushtamila by al-Mawsili, which combines benefits from both al-Quduri and al-Razi's Takmila and adds intra-Hanafi differences (between Abu Hanifa and his two companions); and (28) al-Uqud al-Mufassala by al-Abbasi, a compilation of al-Quduri and al-Takmila. For each, he provides author names, death dates, and manuscript locations. The passage concludes with the beginning of al-Abbasi's introduction. This information helps students understand the scholarly transmission and reliance on the Quduri text.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of the mukhtasar (concise fiqh manual) that forms the base text for these commentaries.
التكملة (al-takmila): The completion or supplement, specifically Husam al-Din al-Razi's work completing al-Quduri's text.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text.
الفوائد المشتملة (al-Fawa'id al-Mushtamila): A work by al-Mawsili that collects benefits from both al-Quduri and al-Razi's Takmila, and adds omitted intra-Hanafi disagreements.
العقود المفصلة (al-Uqud al-Mufassala): A compilation by al-Abbasi that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its Takmila into a single work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which work by al-Mawsili adds the disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions?
A) Sharh Takmilat al-Quduri
B) al-Fawa'id al-Mushtamila 'ala al-Mukhtasar wa al-Takmila
C) al-Uqud al-Mufassala
D) Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tradition is built on layered commentaries; knowing the sources and their relationships is essential for accurate fiqh study.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding Hanafi Commentarial Works: Al-Razi's Takmila and Al-Abbasi's Al-Uqud Al-Mufassala
Bibliographic entry listing two commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relationship between al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, al-Razi's Takmila, and al-Abbasi's al-Uqud al-Mufassala, and explain why such compilations were produced in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A Hanafi text does not stand alone; supplements and compilations preserve intra-madhhab disagreements and enrich the legal tradition.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri introduces two key works that build upon al-Quduri's foundational Mukhtasar. Al-Razi's Takmila adds the disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, while al-Abbasi's al-Uqud al-Mufassala combines both texts. Understanding how these texts relate helps you navigate the layered nature of Hanafi scholarship and the importance of preserving scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
The starting point is al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a concise summary of Hanafi fiqh. Confirm its role as the core text being commented upon.
2
Analyze the first commentary: al-Razi's Takmila
Al-Razi's Takmila is not a standalone work but a supplement that adds missing content, specifically the disagreements (khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
3
Examine the compound work: al-Abbasi's al-Uqud al-Mufassala
Al-Abbasi merges al-Quduri's Mukhtasar with al-Razi's Takmila, arranging them per al-Quduri's order. Note his method: he began compilation after memorizing al-Quduri and obtaining the Takmila, and he added extra issues.
4
Note the manuscript tradition
The passage provides manuscript details (location, numbers, date) for both works. This shows the importance of manuscript verification in textual scholarship.
5
Understand the scholarly motivation
Al-Abbasi was motivated by requests from fellow memorizers and a desire to complete the text. He also acknowledges a predecessor, al-Balidaji. This reflects the collaborative nature of Hanafi scholarship.

الفصل الثالث : شروح القدوري. الرازي، وزاد فيه ما أغفلاه من الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه. ومنه نسخة مقابلة مصححة، كتبت من نسخة بخط المؤلف سنة ٨٥٦هـ ، في مكتبة يني جامع في اسطنبول، برقم (٥٣٤)، وتقع في (۱۳۹) ورقة، نقلاً عن نوادر المخطوطات في مكتبات تركيا. ٢٨ - العقود المفصلة في الجمع بين القدوري والتكملة . للإمام أحمد بن محمد بن حسن العباسي، المتوفى بعد سنة ٨٩٨هـ، وهي سنة شروعه في جَمْع الكتاب، كما صرح في مقدمته، والمراد بالتكملة : تكملة القدوري لحسام الدين الرازي صاحب خلاصة الدلائل، (ت ٥٩٨هـ). ذكره الزركلي في الأعلام ، وذكر له نسخة في مكتبـة عـارف حکمت بالمدينة المنورة برقم (۱۹۰) فقه حنفي. وقد راجعت مكتبة عارف حكمت فوجدتُ النسخة برقم جديد هو (٢٥٤/٢١٤)، ورقم الحفظ (١٢٨٠). وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف: الحمد لله الذي منح بفيض الفضل من شاء من العباد، ووفقه لطرق الهداية والرشاد، ... وبعد : فإن الشيخ الإمام القدوري ألف مختصراً أبدع في تصنيفه، ... وقد حفظه كاتبه العبد الفقير الضعيف بن محمد بن حسن بن علي بن سالم بن محمد بن محمد أحمد العباسي الحنفي غفر الله تعالى ذنوبه، وستر عيوبه. فعند انتهاء الحفظ منه ، بلغني أن له تكملة لشخص من العلماء عظيم المنزلة، وقد منّ الله بحصوله، والوقوف على أبوابه وفصوله ونقل العباسي مقدمة صاحب التكملة، ثم قال: «فلما وعى كاتبه مقالة الشيخ سنح لي الجمع بينهما، فمنعني اشتغال الفكرة الخامدة، والقريحة الجامدة، ... وكان قد سألني بعض الإخوان المشاركين في حفظ هذا المختصر، وذكرت العلة المانعة، فرأيتُهم لا يقبلون عذر من اعتذر ، ... فعند ذلك استخرت الله تعالى، وأجبتهم لمقالهم، وامتثال سؤالهم. فلما كان الأحد يوم الثالث من شهر الله المحرم ، عام ثمان وتسعين وثمانمائة ، شرع العبد الفقير المفتقر إلى عفو الملك القدير في تأليفه، ورتبته على ترتيب القدوري، مستعينا بالله تعالى في جمع أموري، وألحقت في كل كتاب أو باب من أبوابه ما يكون تكملـة لـه من المسائل المذكورة وغيرها وكان قد سبقني إلى هذا الجمع الشيخ الإمام والحبر الهمام مفتي الفرق عبد الله بن محمود بن مودود البلدجي ، تغمده الله برحمته ورضوانه، وأسكنه فسيح جناته.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on al-Quduri. al-Razi, and he added in it what they omitted of the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions. And from it is an compared and corrected copy, written from a copy in the author's handwriting in the year 856 AH, in the Yeni Cami library in Istanbul, number (534), consisting of 139 folios, quoted from Rare Manuscripts in Turkish Libraries. 28 - al-Uqud al-Mufassala fi al-Jam' bayn al-Quduri wa al-Takmila. By Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Abbasi, who died after the year 898 AH, which is the year he began compiling the book, as he stated in his introduction. By al-Takmila is meant: the Takmila of al-Quduri by Husam al-Din al-Razi, author of Khulasat al-Dala'il, (d. 598 AH). Al-Zirikli mentioned it in al-A'lam, and mentioned a copy in the Arif Hikmat library in Medina, number (190) Hanafi fiqh. And I checked the Arif Hikmat library and found the copy with a new number (254/214), and shelf number (1280). And it came in the author's introduction: Praise be to God who bestows overflowing favor on whom He wills of His servants, and guides them to paths of guidance and rectitude... Thereafter: Indeed, the Sheikh Imam al-Quduri wrote a summary that he excelled in its composition... And his scribe, the poor weak servant, ibn Muhammad ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Salim ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad Ahmad al-Abbasi al-Hanafi (may God forgive his sins and conceal his faults) memorized it. When he finished memorizing it, he learned that it had a supplement (takmila) by a person of great rank among scholars, and God graced him with obtaining it and becoming familiar with its chapters and sections. And al-Abbasi quoted the introduction of the author of the Takmila, then said: 'When his scribe understood the Sheikh's statement, it occurred to me to combine them, but my dull mind and barren intellect prevented me... And some brothers who were participating in memorizing this summary had asked me, and I mentioned the preventing reason, and I saw that they would not accept an excuse from one who apologizes... Therefore, I sought guidance from God, and answered their request, and complied with their question. Then on Sunday, the third of Muharram, in the year 898, the poor servant in need of the pardon of the Mighty King began its composition, and I arranged it according to the arrangement of al-Quduri, seeking help from God in managing my affairs, and I attached in every book or chapter of its chapters what would be a completion of it from the mentioned issues and others. And I was preceded in this compilation by the Sheikh Imam, the erudite scholar, the Mufti of the sects, Abdullah ibn Mahmud ibn Mawdud al-Balidaji, may God envelop him with His mercy and pleasure, and grant him a spacious place in His paradise.'
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory section of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, specifically the third chapter which lists commentaries on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author mentions two key works: first, a commentary by al-Razi (Husam al-Din al-Razi, d. 598 AH) that additionally covers disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani); second, a combined work titled al-Uqud al-Mufassala fi al-Jam' bayn al-Quduri wa al-Takmila by Ahmad al-Abbasi (d. after 898 AH), which merges al-Quduri's text with al-Razi's Takmila. The passage notes that al-Abbasi was inspired to compile this work after memorizing al-Quduri and learning of al-Razi's supplement. He began writing on Sunday, 3 Muharram 898 AH, arranging it per al-Quduri's order and adding extra issues. He acknowledges being preceded in such a compilation by Abdullah ibn Mahmud al-Balidaji (author of al-Ikhtiyar). This bibliographic entry is useful for understanding the transmission of Hanafi texts and the scholarly tradition of supercommentaries.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of the Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
التكملة (al-Takmila): A supplement to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar written by Husam al-Din al-Razi, containing additional rulings and disagreements.
العقود المفصلة (al-Uqud al-Mufassala): A work by Ahmad al-Abbasi that combines al-Quduri's Mukhtasar with al-Razi's Takmila, arranged per al-Quduri's order.
الخلاف (al-khilaf): Disagreement, specifically the legal differences between mujtahids. In this context, it refers to the intra-madhhab disagreements between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Abdullah ibn Mahmud al-Balidaji
C) Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abbasi
D) The author of al-Lubab

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's Takmila supplements al-Quduri by adding intra-madhhab disagreements, and al-Abbasi's al-Uqud al-Mufassala merges both into one work, exemplifying the layered tradition of Hanafi scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
