Author's Preface: Compiling a Completion (Takmila) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Author's preface describing compilation method and attribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of a takmila and identify the scholarly practice of attribution in Hanafi works.

Core Idea
A takmila completes a matn; proper attribution upholds scholarly integrity.

This passage introduces us to the scholarly practice of writing completions (takmila) to foundational Hanafi texts. Al-Abbasi describes his journey from memorizing Mukhtasar al-Quduri to compiling his own takmila, and crucially, he models the ethical standard of attributing verbatim quotations to their original authors. Understanding this context deepens our appreciation for how Hanafi knowledge was transmitted and built upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Read the passage to determine why al-Abbasi wrote this takmila. He mentions his own memorization and then learning of an existing completion by another scholar.
Note the phrase 'فلما وعى كاتبه مقالة الشيخ سنح لي الجمع بينهما' – the idea to combine them.
2
Analyze the timeline and trigger
Identify when he started (3rd Muharram 898 AH) and what prompted him: the requests from fellow students ('بعض الإخوان المشاركين في حفظ هذا المختصر').
He initially hesitated due to mental fatigue but was persuaded.
3
Examine the compilation method
Notice that he arranged the work according to the order of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and added completions to each chapter.
The method: 'رتبته على ترتيب القدوري' and 'ألحقت في كل كتاب أو باب... ما يكون تكملة له'.
4
Assess the attribution practice
Focus on the final part where he states that the faraid section was taken verbatim from al-Baladji and he explicitly notes this as not his own authorship.
Key phrase: 'وقد نقلت منه في كتابي هذا ما قاله في الفرائض بحروفه، ولذا نبهت عليه أنه ليس من تأليفي بل تأليفه'.
5
Contextualize in Hanafi tradition
Reflect on how this passage illustrates the importance of chains of transmission (sanad) and intellectual honesty in Hanafi scholarship.
This is a model for later scholars compiling commentaries or completions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
مختصراً أبدع في تصنيفه، ... وقد حفظه كاتبه العبد الفقير الضعيف بن محمد بن حسن بن علي بن سالم بن محمد بن محمد أحمد العباسي الحنفي غفر الله تعالى ذنوبه، وستر عيوبه.
فعند انتهاء الحفظ منه ، بلغني أن له تكملة لشخص من العلماء عظيم المنزلة، وقد منّ الله بحصوله، والوقوف على أبوابه وفصوله
ونقل العباسي مقدمة صاحب التكملة، ثم قال:
«فلما وعى كاتبه مقالة الشيخ سنح لي الجمع بينهما، فمنعني اشتغال الفكرة الخامدة، والقريحة الجامدة، ... وكان قد سألني بعض الإخوان المشاركين في حفظ هذا المختصر، وذكرت العلة المانعة، فرأيتُهم لا يقبلون عذر من اعتذر ، ... فعند ذلك استخرت الله تعالى، وأجبتهم لمقالهم، وامتثال سؤالهم.
فلما كان الأحد يوم حد، الثالث من شهر الله المحرم ، عام ثمان وتسعين وثمانمائة ، شرع العبد الفقير المفتقر إلى عفو الملك القدير في تأليفه، ورتبته على ترتيب القدوري، مستعينا بالله تعالى في جمع أموري، وألحقت في كل كتاب أو باب من أبوابه ما يكون تكملـة لـه من المسائل المذكورة وغيرها
وكان قد سبقني إلى هذا الجمع الشيخ الإمام والحبر الهمام مفتي الفرق عبد الله بن محمود بن مودود البلدجي ، تغمده الله برحمته ورضوانه، وأسكنه فسيح جناته.
(1) الموصلي صاحب الاختيار كما تقدم عند ذكر كتابه.
وقد نقلت منه في كتابي هذا ما قاله في الفرائض بحروفه، ولذا نبهت عليه أنه ليس من تأليفي بل تأليفه». اهـ من مقدمة المؤلف. ونسخة عارف حكمت هذه تقع في (١٨٤) ورقة، وفي كل صفحة (١٩) سطراً، وتاريخ نسخها سنة ٩٠٤هـ.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. A unique composition in its authorship... Its scribe, the poor weak servant, Ibn Muhammad ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Salim ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad Ahmad al-Abbasi al-Hanafi, may Allah forgive his sins and conceal his faults, memorized it. Upon completing its memorization, news reached me that there was a completion (takmila) of it by a person of great scholarly rank, and Allah granted its acquisition and access to its chapters and sections. Al-Abbasi transmitted the preface of the author of the completion, then said: 'When its scribe understood the shaykh's statement, the idea occurred to me to combine them, but I was prevented by the sluggishness of thought and stagnant intellect... Some brothers who were also memorizing this mukhtasar had asked me, and I mentioned the preventing reason, but they did not accept any excuse from one who excuses himself... Thereupon, I sought Allah's guidance and responded to their request and complied with their question. So on Sunday, the third of the sacred month of Muharram, in the year 898 AH, the poor needy servant began his authorship, arranging it according to the arrangement of al-Quduri, seeking Allah's help in all my affairs, and I attached to each book or chapter of its chapters what would serve as a completion for it from the mentioned and other issues. And the eminent Imam, the great scholar, the mufti of the sects, Abdullah ibn Mahmud ibn Mawdud al-Baladji, had preceded me in this compilation – may Allah envelop him in His mercy and pleasure, and grant him spacious gardens. (1) He is al-Mawsili, author of al-Ikhtiyar, as previously mentioned. And I transmitted from him in this book what he said about faraid verbatim, and therefore I pointed out that it is not from my own authorship but his.' End quote from the author's introduction. This copy of 'Arif Hikmat consists of 184 folios, with 19 lines per page, and its copying date is 904 AH.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note about the author of the work (al-Abbasi) and his motivation for compiling a completion (takmila) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author states that after memorizing the Mukhtasar, he learned of an existing completion by another scholar. He was initially hesitant to combine his own work with that completion due to mental fatigue, but was persuaded by companions. He eventually started his compilation on the 3rd of Muharram 898 AH, organizing it like al-Quduri. He acknowledges that the faraid section was taken verbatim from an earlier work by al-Baladji, giving credit. The passage also includes bibliographic details of a manuscript copy.

Key Terms
تكملة (takmila): A supplementary work that completes or adds to the original Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A famous concise text of Hanafi fiqh by Imam al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He was ordered by the caliph.
B) He was asked by some fellow students who were memorizing the same text.
C) He wanted to correct errors in the existing completion.
D) He received a dream commanding him to write.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi scholar's compilation must give proper attribution for verbatim quotations, as exemplified by al-Abbasi's takmila.

Introducing Abu Ya'qub al-Uzjandi and His Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Introduces Abu Ya'qub al-Uzjandi's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, purpose, and significance of al-Uzjandi's sharh on Mukhtasar al-Quduri within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Uzjandi's commentary explains each transmitted version with concise comprehension, bridging the matn and the student.

This passage introduces a Hanafi commentary from the 6th century AH. The author, Abu Ya'qub al-Uzjandi, wrote a concise yet comprehensive explanation of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text. Understanding the context of such commentaries helps us appreciate the scholarly chain and pedagogical methods of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name
Look for the complete name: Abu Ya'qub Zahir al-Din Yusuf ibn Uthman ibn al-Fadl al-Uzjandi. Note his title 'Shaykh al-Islam' and his century (6th AH).
The nisbah 'al-Uzjandi' is uncertain; some sources read 'al-Arzanjani'.
2
Understand the nisbah uncertainty
The editor mentions a variant reading and clarifies that manuscript evidence supports 'al-Uzjandi'. This shows the importance of manuscript verification in Hanafi scholarship.
Such nisbah debates are common in biographical studies.
3
Read the author's stated purpose
In the preface, al-Uzjandi says he was asked by a brother to write a sharh. He promised to explain each riwayah (transmitted version) with 'dirayah' (comprehension) in a concise manner.
This highlights the twin goals: transmitting the text and understanding its meanings.
4
Reflect on the role of such commentaries in Hanafi pedagogy
This sharh is one of many that bridge the foundational matn and the student. Commentaries like this ensure the living tradition of Hanafi fiqh remains accessible.
Recognize that learning fiqh involves engaging with both matn and sharh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢۹- شرح مختصر القدوري.
لأبي يعقوب ظهير الدين يوسف بن عثمان بن الفضل ، من علماء القرن السادس الهجري، رحمه الله تعالى.
الأوزجندي(1)( وسماه سزكين في تاريخ التراث العربي ١١٩/٣: (الأرزنجاني)، وهو من الشرح جاءت الكلمة واضحة في الديباجية تحريف، ففي نسخة جار الله هذا هكذا: (الأوزجندي)، والله أعلم.)
وتوجد نسخة منه في مكتبة جار الله باسطنبول، برقم (۷۳۱)، كتبت سنة ٦٠٣هـ ، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل(۲)( ٤٥٩/٥).
(۳)( كما كتب إلي بذلك من اسطنبول الأخ الكريم الأستاذ محمد فاتح قايا، جزاه الله خيراً.)
وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف ما يلي قال الشيخ الإمام الأجل السيد شيخ الإسلام ظهير الدين أبـو يعقوب يوسف بن عثمان بن الفضل بن محمد الأوزجندي:
إنه سألني بعض إخواني شرح مختصر القدوري، ببيان المعاني، فضمنتُ أن أبين لكل رواية دراية على وجه له كفاية، بعبارة موجزة
29 – Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Abu Ya'qub Zahir al-Din Yusuf ibn Uthman ibn al-Fadl, from the scholars of the sixth century AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Uzjandi (1)(Sezgin named him in ‘History of Arabic Heritage’ 3/119 as al-Arzanjani, and it is from the commentary that the word is clearly a distortion in al-Dibaji, as in the Jarallah manuscript it is al-Uzjandi, and Allah knows best.) A copy exists in the Jarallah Library in Istanbul, number 731, written in 603 AH, see al-Fihris al-Shamil (2)(5/459). (3)(As written to me from Istanbul by the noble brother Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya, may Allah reward him.) And in the author’s preface, the great Imam, the noble master, the Shaykh al-Islam Zahir al-Din Abu Ya'qub Yusuf ibn Uthman ibn al-Fadl ibn Muhammad al-Uzjandi said: 'One of my brothers asked me to write a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining the meanings, so I undertook to explain for each transmitted version a comprehension in a sufficient manner, with a concise expression.'
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage introduces the commentary of Abu Ya'qub al-Uzjandi on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It provides the author's full name and affiliation, noting uncertainty in the nisbah (al-Uzjandi vs. al-Arzanjani). A manuscript location and date are given. The author's own preface explains that he wrote the commentary at the request of a friend, aiming to explain meanings with a concise but sufficient expression. This highlights the pedagogical purpose of many Hanafi commentaries.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary or exposition of a base text (matn), here Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
الأوزجندي (al-Uzjandi): Nisbah of the author, likely referring to a place in Transoxiana; variant al-Arzanjani mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To refute all opposing schools.

C) To include hadith chains for every ruling.
D) To write a lengthy commentary with multiple volumes.

Key Takeaway
Al-Uzjandi's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri exemplifies the Hanafi tradition of concise yet comprehensive sharh, prioritizing both transmission and understanding.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction to al-Yanabi' and its Author Mahmud bin Ramadan
Introducing the book al-Yanabi' and its author's preface

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author of al-Yanabi', explain his motive for writing it, and identify the book's relationship to Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Yanabi' is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, written to aid both beginners and advanced scholars with comprehensive legal issues.

This lesson introduces you to a Hanafi commentary called al-Yanabi' (The Springs) and its author, Mahmud bin Ramadan al-Rumi al-Hanafi. The passage provides not only the book's title and manuscript details but also the author's own preface, in which he explains his intention to compile a work that covers the principles and branches of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this preface helps you appreciate the scholarly effort behind such commentaries and their role in transmitting the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and author
From the opening lines, note the full title 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'' and its author Mahmud bin Ramadan al-Hanafi (also known as Rashid al-Din). Recognize that this work is a commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
The author's nisbah 'al-Rumi' indicates his origin from the region of Rûm (Anatolia).
2
Examine the author's preface for purpose
Read Mahmud bin Ramadan's opening statement: he states that hearts naturally store provision for the Hereafter and seek praise. He explains that his soul prompted him to compile a book that helps both the beginner and the advanced scholar, along with the 'mudmaraat' (implications) of al-Quduri and many contemporary issues (nawazil).
The phrase 'mudmaraat al-Quduri' refers to the hidden implications and detailed rulings derived from the concise matn.
3
Analyze the author's method
Mahmud bin Ramadan says he exerted his utmost effort to find the issues recorded, their principles and branches transmitted. He then transmitted them as they were and pointed out what they led to. He describes himself as an 'interpreter and intermediary', indicating that his role is to convey the existing scholarship faithfully.
This reflects the typical Hanafi commentary style: collecting, organizing, and clarifying without introducing novel rulings.
4
Consider the critical note on modern scholarship
The passage includes a note criticizing a modern researcher (Ahmad al-Naqib) for hastily declaring the author unknown and doubting the book's attribution. This shows the importance of careful verification in textual scholarship.
Take away the lesson that even well-known works can be subject to undue skepticism.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
صاحب الينابيع، وهو بدر الدين محمد بن عبد الله الشبلي صاحب آكام المرجان، قال في ترجمته بعد أن ذكر الينابيع :
يقول الجامع الفقير - أي صاحب هدية العارفين ــ قـد ملكـتُ كتاب «الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع نسخة قديمة مكتوبة في صفر من شهور سنة ٧١٩هـ تأليف رشيد الدين أبي عبد الله محمود ابن رمضان الرومي الحنفي ، ألَّفه وبيّضه في حلب في مدرسة نور الدين، المسمى بالحلاوية، في أواخر جمادى الأولى، من سنة ٦١٦هـ، أولها:
«الحمد لله الذي أوضح السبل للسالكين، ونــور بـــره قـلـوب الشاكرين، وبعد: قال المذنب أبو عبد الله محمود بن رمضان أصلح الله باله... الخ». اهـ وفي مكان آخر من هدية العارفين قال عنه : «هو في مجلد كبير». اهـ
تنبيه : قد عرف بكتاب الينابيع الأستاذ أحمد النقيب في رسالته للماجستير، التي طبعها باسم : المذهب الحنفي» (٢)، لكن كلامه في الكتاب وفي مؤلفه لم يكن عن علم ، فقـد تـسـرع بتجهيل مؤلفه، وشكك بدون تريث في نسبة الكتاب إليه، والكمال الله وحده.
* وأنقل فيما يلي مقدمة صاحب الينابيع، ليعـرف عـملـه فيـه، وجهده، جزاه الله خيراً، فقد قال رحمه الله :
الحمد لله الذي أوضح السبيل للسالكين، ونور بنوره قلوب الشاكرين، وصلى الله على محمد خاتم النبيين، وعلى آله وأصحابه الطاهرين، وسلم تسليماً كثيراً.
قال العبد المذنب أبو عبد الله محمود بن رمضان أصلح الله باله، وتقبل أعماله ، أما . بعد :
فإن القلوب مجبولة على ادخار الزَّاد ليوم المعاد، ونشر الثناء إلى يوم التناد، وقد دَعَتْني نفسي إلى القسم الأول، إذ هو من الذخر الأجزل، أن أجمع كتاباً حاوياً لما سبق إليه فهم المبتدي، وجامعاً لما يفتقر إلى معرفته المنتهي مع مضمرات القدوري وأتباعها، وكثير من الواقعات وأنواعها، لكثرة سؤال طالبها، وعُسر إجابة سائلها.
فقد بذلت جهدي حتى وجدتُ المسائل مسطورة، وأصولها وفروعها منقولة، ثم نقلتها على ما هي عليه، ونبهت عنها لما أدت إليه، واستخرت الله على إتمامه، فأخار لي إلى اختتامه، وأنا في ذلك معبر وسفير، والله بالتجاوز عن زللي قدير، وسميته كتاب: «الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع، وما توفيقي إلا بالله، عليه توكلت، نعم المولى ونعم النصير، وهو المستعان على اختتامه». اهـ
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
The author of al-Yanabi', who is Badr al-Din Muhammad bin Abdullah al-Shabli, author of Akam al-Marjan, said in his biography after mentioning al-Yanabi':
The poor compiler - meaning the author of Hadiyyat al-Arifin - said: I obtained a copy of the book 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'' written in Safar of the months of the year 719 AH, authored by Rashid al-Din Abu Abdullah Mahmud bin Ramadan al-Rumi al-Hanafi. He authored and fair-copied it in Aleppo at the Nur al-Din School, known as al-Hallawiyyah, at the end of Jumada al-Ula of the year 616 AH. Its beginning is: 'Praise be to Allah who has made clear the paths for the seekers, and illuminated the hearts of the grateful with His light...' etc. And in another place in Hadiyyat al-Arifin he said about it: 'It is in a large volume.'
Note: The book al-Yanabi' has been known by Professor Ahmad al-Naqib in his Master's thesis, which he published under the name 'al-Madhhab al-Hanafi', but his discussion about the book and its author was not based on knowledge. He hastily declared its author unknown and doubted without deliberation the attribution of the book to him. Perfection belongs to Allah alone.
* I will now quote the preface of the author of al-Yanabi' so that his work and effort may be known, may Allah reward him well. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said:
'Praise be to Allah who has made clear the way for the seekers, and illuminated the hearts of the grateful with His light. And may Allah bless Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and his family and pure Companions, and grant him abundant peace.
The sinful servant Abu Abdullah Mahmud bin Ramadan - may Allah reform his state and accept his deeds - said: To proceed:
Indeed, hearts are naturally inclined to store provision for the Day of Return and to spread praise until the Day of Summoning. My soul prompted me to undertake the first part, as it is the greatest treasure, to compile a book encompassing what the beginner's understanding has preceded, and gathering what the advanced scholar needs to know, along with the implications (mudmaraat) of al-Quduri and their corollaries, and many occurrences and their types, due to the frequent questions of those seeking them and the difficulty of answering the questioners.
I exerted my utmost effort until I found the issues recorded, their principles and branches transmitted. Then I transmitted them as they were, and pointed out what they led to. I sought Allah's guidance to complete it, and He chose for me its conclusion. In that, I am merely an interpreter and intermediary. Allah is capable of forgiving my slips. I named it the book 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari''. My success is only from Allah. Upon Him I rely. What an excellent Protector and what an excellent Helper. He is the One whose help is sought for its conclusion.' End.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical introduction to the book 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari' (The Springs in Knowledge of the Principles and Branches). The author, the commentator on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, introduces this work and provides its author's own preface. The text first identifies the author of al-Yanabi' as Mahmud bin Ramadan al-Rumi al-Hanafi, also known as Rashid al-Din, and gives details about the manuscript copy and its composition in the year 616 AH in Aleppo. The commentator then mentions a note criticizing a modern researcher's treatment of the book. Finally, the full preface of Mahmud bin Ramadan is quoted, in which he explains his motivation: hearts are inclined to store good deeds and seek praise, so he compiled this work to help both beginners and advanced scholars. He collected the issues from the sources, transmitted them faithfully, and sought Allah's guidance. He names his book al-Yanabi' and prays for success.

Key Terms
الينابيع (al-Yanabi'): Title of a Hanafi fiqh book by Mahmud bin Ramadan, meaning 'The Springs'
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri, widely studied in the Hanafi school.
مضمرات القدوري (mudmaraat al-Quduri): The implications and detailed rulings derived implicitly from the concise text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
معبر وسفير (mu'abhir wa safir): An interpreter and intermediary; the author describes himself as a mere transmitter of the established rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Yanabi' is a Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, authored by Mahmud bin Ramadan to help scholars access principles, branches, and contemporary rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Two Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical listing of two Hanafi commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the two key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri mentioned in the passage, including their authors, scope, and status.

Core Idea
Two major commentaries: one incomplete by al-Mawsili, one comprehensive by al-Zahidi.

This passage introduces two important commentaries on the foundational Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding these works helps students choose reliable explanations for their study. The passage also includes an excerpt from another commentary's introduction, showing the author's motivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
The base text being commented on is Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri. Recognize this as a core Hanafi matn.
2
Name the two specific commentaries
The passage lists two commentaries: (33) Sharh al-Quduri by al-Mawsili and (34) al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Zahidi.
Note the numbering in the original text indicates their order in a list.
3
Examine the status of each
Al-Mawsili's commentary was not completed (as per Kashf al-Zunun), while al-Zahidi's is a large three-volume work, described as precious and beneficial by al-Lakhnawi.
This affects usability: one is fragmentary, the other is comprehensive.
4
Note the biographical details
Al-Mawsili died 638 AH; al-Zahidi died 658 AH and is noted as Hanafi in fiqh but Mu'tazili in creed, a common combination.
Creed does not necessarily affect fiqh rulings, but it provides context about the author.
5
Understand the introduction excerpt
The opening lines from Mahmud ibn Ramadan's 'al-Yanabi'' show the purpose of compiling a fiqh work: to help beginners and advanced scholars by including principles and branches.
This is not a commentary proper but a separate work built on al-Quduri.

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
قال رحمه الله : الحمد لله الذي أوضح السبيل للسالكين، ونور بنوره قلوب الشاكرين، وصلى الله على محمد خاتم النبيين، وعلى آله وأصحابه الطاهرين، وسلم تسليماً كثيراً.
قال العبد المذنب أبو عبد الله محمود بن رمضان أصلح الله باله، وتقبل أعماله ، أما بعد : فإن القلوب مجبولة على ادخار الزَّاد ليوم المعاد، ونشر الثناء إلى يوم التناد، وقد دَعَتْني نفسي إلى القسم الأول، إذ هو من الذخر الأجزل، أن أجمع كتاباً حاوياً لما سبق إليه فهم المبتدي، وجامعاً لما يفتقر إلى معرفته المنتهي مع مضمرات القدوري وأتباعها، وكثير من الواقعات وأنواعها، لكثرة سؤال طالبها، وعُسر إجابة سائلها.
فقد بذلت جهدي حتى وجدتُ المسائل مسطورة، وأصولها وفروعها منقولة، ثم نقلتها على ما هي عليه، ونبهت عنها لما أدت إليه، واستخرت الله على إتمامه، فأخار لي إلى اختتامه، وأنا في ذلك معبر وسفير، والله بالتجاوز عن زللي قدير، وسميته كتاب: «الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع، وما توفيقي إلا بالله، عليه توكلت، نعم المولى ونعم النصير، وهو المستعان على اختتامه». اهـ
(33) شرح القدوري .
للإمام أبي إسحاق إبراهيم بن عبد الكريم بن أبي السعادات بن كريم الموصلي، المتوفى سنة 638 هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. ذكره العلامة قاسم(2)، وقال: «شرح قطعة كبيرة من القدوري». اهـ، كما ذكره صاحب كشف الظنون(3)، وقال: لم يتم.
(34) المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري.
للإمام نجم الدين مختار بن محمود الزاهدي الخوارزمي، المتوفى سنة 658هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وكان قد رحل من خوارزم إلى بغداد وبلاد الروم، وهو حنفي الفروع، معتزلي الاعتقاد.
وشرحه من أكبر شروح مختصر القدوري، يقع في ثلاث مجلدات.
قال الإمام اللكنوي عنه : «وشَرْحُه نفيس نافع». اهـ
وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف : ... لما عمَّت الفتنة العامة ديار الإسلام، وطمت هذه الطامة.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: Praise be to Allah who has made clear the path for the seekers, and illuminated with His light the hearts of the grateful. May Allah bless Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets, and his pure Family and Companions, and grant abundant peace. The sinful servant, Abu Abdullah Mahmud ibn Ramadan, may Allah rectify his condition and accept his deeds, said: To proceed: Hearts are inclined to store provisions for the Day of Return and to spread praise until the Day of Summons. My soul urged me to the first part, for it is the greatest treasure: to compile a book encompassing what a beginner's understanding can reach, and gathering what the advanced scholar needs to know, along with the implications of al-Quduri and its followers, and many occurrences and their types, due to the frequent questions of seekers and the difficulty of answering them. I exerted my effort until I found the issues recorded, and their principles and branches transmitted. Then I transmitted them as they are, and alerted to what they lead to. I sought Allah's guidance to complete it, and He guided me to its conclusion. In that, I am an interpreter and an envoy, and Allah is Able to overlook my slips. I named it the book 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari' (The Springs in Knowing the Principles and Branches). My success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely. He is the best Master and the best Helper. He is the one sought for its completion. End. (33) Sharh al-Quduri. By Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Abi al-Sa'adat ibn Karim al-Mawsili, died in 638 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Allamah Qasim mentioned him and said: 'He commented on a large portion of al-Quduri.' End. As mentioned by the author of Kashf al-Zunun, who said: 'It was not completed.' (34) al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Imam Najm al-Din Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Zahidi al-Khwarizmi, died in 658 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He had traveled from Khwarizm to Baghdad and the lands of the Romans. He was Hanafi in branches, Mu'tazili in creed. His commentary is among the largest commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, consisting of three volumes. Imam al-Lakhnawi said about him: 'His commentary is precious and beneficial.' End. It is mentioned in the author's introduction: '...When the great tribulation spread throughout the lands of Islam, and this calamity overwhelmed...'
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of two Hanafi commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The first part quotes the introduction of a work called 'al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'' by Mahmud ibn Ramadan, explaining his motivation to compile a comprehensive fiqh work. Then it lists two specific commentaries: (33) 'Sharh al-Quduri' by Abu Ishaq Ibrahim al-Mawsili (d. 638 AH), which was incomplete as noted by the author of Kashf al-Zunun; and (34) 'al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Najm al-Din Mukhtar al-Zahidi (d. 658 AH), described as a large three-volume work. Al-Zahidi is noted as being Hanafi in fiqh but Mu'tazili in creed, a common background for some Hanafi scholars of that era. Imam al-Lakhnawi praises his commentary as precious and beneficial. The passage is informative for students of the Hanafi school to recognize key commentaries on al-Quduri's foundational text.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Hasan Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), summarizing rulings according to Abu Hanifa and his disciples.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon the original text, providing proofs, details, and clarifications.
الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع (al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari'): A book by Mahmud ibn Ramadan that aims to cover principles and branches of fiqh, building on al-Quduri's work.
المجتبى شرح مختصر القدوري (al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A comprehensive three-volume commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Najm al-Din Mukhtar al-Zahidi (d. 658 AH).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Author's Motivation and Methodology in al-Lubab
Author's preface stating motivation and methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten characteristics of the author's commentary and explain the historical context that motivated its composition.

Core Idea
A rigorous commentary must detail, prove, and avoid error.

The author opens by lamenting the decline of scholars and the neglect of fiqh in his time. He was asked by fellow students to write a commentary on the foundational Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Noting that previous commentators had left many summaries undetailed and problems unsolved, he accepts the task and outlines ten characteristics that define his approach. This preface sets the standard for a thorough Hanafi commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Read the opening lines describing the state of scholarship. What specific problem prompted the author to write?
The author points to the destruction of scholars and the neglect of fiqh foundations.
2
Extract the Ten Characteristics
Find and list the ten numbered commitments the author makes. They appear after 'ملتزماً فيه عشر خصال'.
Some numbers may be missing or disordered in the text; use the Arabic list as given.
3
Categorize the Commitments
Group the ten into three categories: explanation (e.g., detailing summaries), proof (e.g., supporting with evidence), and caution (e.g., avoiding recklessness).
This helps understand the multidimensional nature of the commentary.
4
Analyze the Author's Tone
Note the author's humility and reliance on Allah. Why does he mention his own limitations?
This reflects the adab of a Hanafi scholar.
5
Apply the Methodology
Consider how these characteristics would improve the study of a specific fiqh chapter, like salah or zakat.
For example, 'detailing summaries' means breaking down every condition and pillar.

شارع الشرائع والأحكام واستولت يد التدمير على طلبة العلم والعلماء، وأنشبت المنية أظفارها في يواقيح الفضلاء، لم يبق في عالم الفضل منهم إلا شيخ تحرير قد بلغ ساحل الحياة، أو شاب عزيز شغلته شواغل العيش واللذات. فبقيت مباني الفقه سدىً هَمَلاً، وأهملت معانيه علماً وعملاً، لتحصيل الفقه همة فهزت بعض إخواني همة الارتقاء إلى مراقي الفقهاء، وبعضهم اللقا مواطن بعد الأدب، والإحاطة فيه لمسالك العرب والعجم، فطلبوا إلي شرح المختصر المنسوب إلى إمام الأئمة، وفقيه آخر هذه الأمة أبي الحسين أحمد بن محمد أحمد بن ابن جعفر بن أحمد القدوري، طيب الله ثراه، وجعل حظيرة القدس مأواه. فإنه أعظم دواوين الفقه بركة وخطَراً، وأرفعها شأناً وقَدْراً، وأدورها في أندية الفضلاء والمدارس، وأيمنها للمدرس والدارس. وقد ترك أعمُّ المُشَرِّحين له لغاية وضوحه عندهم تفصيل مُجملاته، وتفسير مهماته، وكشف مشكلاته، فأجبتهم إلى ذلك، مستعيناً بتوفيق الله تعالى وعصمته وفضله، ملتزماً فيه عشر خصال بعونه ولطفه وحوله: ١- تفصيل مجملاته. ٢- وتحصيل رواياته ومهملاته. وحل مشكلاته. ٤- وكشف معضلاته. ه وتفسير العويصة من ألفاظه ومبانيه. ٦- وتبيين الغوامض من إشاراته ومعانيه. وتقسيم الأحكام والمسائل. ه وذكر أصولها وفصولها، مبرهنة بالدلائل. والتنبيه على مواضع الزلل -١٠- والاتقاء عن المجازفة في نقل الأحكام والعلل. مع إيجاز لا يُخِل بفهم الذكي، وتطويل لا يُمِل خاطر الألمعي. راجياً من ربي الكريم العفو عن الخطأ والخلل في القول والعمل، ومؤملاً من الناظر فيه الدعاء لي والاستغفار، وإصلاح ما زل القلم به، أو الخاطر فيه والاستذكار. فمن أنا مع قلة علومي وكثرة اشتغالي وهمومي، حتى تصديتُ لشرح مثل هذا الكتاب، وتعرضت له في معرض الإبانة وفصل الخطاب، لكن حَمَلني عليه حرصي على التحصيل، ومخافة
The path of laws and rulings; and the hand of destruction has taken control of students of knowledge and scholars, and death has sunk its claws into the strong ones among the virtuous; there remains in the world of virtue among them except a revising elder who has reached the shore of life, or a dear youth occupied by the distractions of livelihood and pleasures. So the foundations of fiqh remained empty and neglected, and its meanings were abandoned in knowledge and practice. For the acquisition of fiqh, a determination stirred some of my brothers to ascend to the ranks of the jurists, and some of them to meet stations after learning, and to gain comprehensive knowledge of the ways of Arabs and non-Arabs therein. So they asked me to comment on the abridged work attributed to the Imam of Imams, the jurist of the last of this nation, Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad Ahmad ibn ibn Ja'far ibn Ahmad al-Quduri, may Allah make his soil fragrant and make the abode of paradise his refuge. For it is the greatest of the books of fiqh in blessing and importance, the highest in rank and status, the most circulated in the circles of the virtuous and the schools, and the most beneficial for the teacher and student. Most of the commentators on it have left, due to its apparent clarity to them, the detailing of its summaries, the explanation of its difficulties, and the uncovering of its problems. So I responded to them, seeking help from the success, protection, and favor of Allah Almighty, committing myself in it to ten characteristics with His help, grace, and power: 1- Detailing its summaries. 2- Obtaining its narrations and its neglected matters. And solving its problems. 4- Uncovering its perplexities. 5- Interpreting the obscure of its words and structures. 6- Clarifying the subtleties of its indications and meanings. And dividing the rulings and issues. 7- Mentioning their principles and branches, supported by proofs. And alerting to places of error. 10- Avoiding recklessness in transmitting rulings and reasons. With conciseness that does not impair the understanding of the intelligent, and expansion that does not bore the mind of the brilliant. Hoping from my Generous Lord for forgiveness of error and fault in speech and action, and expecting from the observer in it supplication for me and seeking forgiveness, and correction of what the pen or mind has slipped, and remembrance. So who am I, with the scarcity of my knowledge and the abundance of my preoccupations and concerns, that I should undertake to comment on such a book, and present myself in the context of clarification and decisive speech? But it carried me my eagerness for acquisition and fear...
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. He begins by lamenting the decline of scholarship in his time, describing how the hand of destruction has overtaken students and scholars, and how only a few advanced elders or distracted youth remain. Consequently, the principles of fiqh have been neglected. However, some of his brothers were motivated to attain the ranks of the jurists and sought his assistance in writing a commentary on the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, whom he praises as the greatest Imam and jurist of the later generation. He extols the Mukhtasar as the most blessed and significant book of fiqh, widely circulated in scholarly circles. Noting that previous commentators have left many of its summaries undetailed and its problems unsolved due to its apparent clarity, he answers the call. He then outlines ten characteristics of his commentary: 1) detailing summaries, 2) gathering narrations and neglected aspects, 3) solving problems, 4) uncovering perplexities, 5) interpreting obscure words, 6) clarifying subtle indications, 7) dividing rulings and issues, 8) mentioning principles and branches supported by proofs, 9) alerting to errors, and 10) avoiding recklessness in transmitting rulings and reasons. He aims for a balanced style: concise yet not puzzling the intelligent, and expanded yet not boring the brilliant. He concludes with a humble supplication, asking forgiveness for any errors and seeking the reader's prayers and corrections. The preface sets the stage for a meticulous, well-structured commentary grounded in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text.
مختصر (mukhtasar): An abridged work summarising a larger field of fiqh.
مجمل (mujmal): A summary or concise statement that needs detail.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Replacing the original text with his own rulings.
B) Detailing the summaries of the Mukhtasar.
C) Writing in a very long style to impress readers.
D) Ignoring the proofs to keep the commentary brief.

Key Takeaway
A thorough Hanafi commentary must detail summaries, provide proofs, and avoid recklessness in transmitting rulings.

The Ten Methodological Commitments of Al-Lubab
Author enumerates ten qualities of his commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten qualities of al-Maydani's commentary and explain how each contributes to a systematic Hanafi fiqh study.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's ten commitments ensure clarity, evidence-based rulings, and humility — a model for Hanafi scholarship.

Before diving into the fiqh rulings, it is crucial to understand the methodology the author commits to. In this passage, al-Maydani sets out ten principles that govern his commentary. These principles reveal his scholarly rigor and serve as a guide for the reader. By internalizing these commitments, you will better appreciate the structure and depth of the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten commitments
Read the Arabic text carefully and list each of the ten numbered items. They are introduced as 'عشر خصال' and numbered 1-10 in the passage.
Note that numbers 3 and 4 are written as 2 and 4 in the original list, but the intended sequence is ten items.
2
Classify the commitments into thematic groups
Group the commitments into categories: (a) explanation and clarification (1,3,4,5,6,7), (b) evidence and sources (2,8), (c) error prevention (9,10). This helps see the overall purpose.
3
Understand the author's purpose
Al-Maydani states the result of these commitments: brevity that does not impair understanding and length that does not bore. This balance is essential for a beneficial commentary.
He also expresses humility, seeking forgiveness and correction.
4
Relate to the study of Hanafi fiqh
Consider how each commitment enhances the study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. For example, 'collecting transmissions' helps the student see the variety within the Hanafi school.
This methodology makes the commentary not just an explanation but a tool for deeper learning.

Commentary
This passage is the author's front matter from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It opens with basmalah and then enumerates ten methodological commitments. The author explains that his commentary will: (1) expand summaries, (2) gather variant transmissions and ambiguous points, (3) resolve problems, (4) uncover difficult issues, (5) interpret obscure words and structures, (6) clarify subtle indications, (7) classify ahkam and masail, (8) state principles and branches with evidence, (9) point out potential errors, and (10) avoid exaggeration in transmitting rulings and causes. He then notes that he balances brevity and thoroughness, and expresses humility, emphasizing that he undertook this work due to his desire for knowledge, fear of forgetting, and requests from colleagues. This passage sets the tone for a scholarly, systematic Sharh.

Methodology of Expansion in al-Lubab
Discussion of commentary's breadth and additions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author of al-Lubab added supplementary chapters beyond al-Quduri and identify the Hanafi principle of 'umum al-balwa' as justification.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab expands al-Quduri with fatwa supplements where 'umum al-balwa' necessitates practical guidance.

Al-Lubab is renowned as the most comprehensive and widely cited commentary on al-Quduri. In this passage, we learn that the author did not merely explain al-Quduri's matn; he actively supplemented it with additional fatawa, especially in the Book of Permission and Prohibition. His justification is revealing: he added a twenty-chapter supplement because of 'umum al-balwa' (general need). This shows how Hanafi commentaries often serve as living fiqh manuals, not just academic expositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and commentary
Recognise that al-Quduri's matn is the foundation, and al-Lubab is its commentary. Note that al-Lubab goes beyond mere explanation by adding new material.
The author states he includes extra issues 'even though they are not from the branches of the issues mentioned in this book'.
2
Locate the specific addition
The author appended a twenty-chapter supplement at the end of Kitab al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah. This is a concrete example of expansion.
Kitab al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah covers rulings on permissible and impermissible actions.
3
Understand the justification: 'umum al-balwa'
The author explicitly states he added the supplement 'due to the general need' (عموم البلوى). This Hanafi principle allows rulings to be addressed when a matter becomes widespread, even if not directly from the original matn.
'Umum al-balwa' is a key concept in Hanafi usul affecting exemptions and practical fatwa.
4
Recognise the reliance on external sources
The author mentions that most of the additional issues are found in al-Bahr al-Muhit (Munyat al-Fuqaha'). This shows his methodology of drawing from authoritative works.
Al-Bahr al-Muhit is a significant Hanafi reference by Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه المقدمة من المؤلف تبين بوضوح عمله في هذا الشرح والمنهج الذي سار عليه والنقاط التي اهتم بها في شرحه، والتي قام بها خير قيام.
وهو أوسع شروح القدوري، وأكثرها انتشاراً بين علماء المذهب ممن جاء بعده، فتراهم يكثرون النقل عنه، معتمدين ذلك، وبخاصة في الفروع الفقهية التي يُلحقها بمسائل الكتاب، كصاحب البحر الرائق، وغيره.
وكمثال لإيراده مسائل زائدة على ما في القـدوري، فإنـه لمـا انتهى من شرح كتاب الحظر والإباحة من القدوري، قال: "ومسائل هذا الكتاب كثيرة غير محصورة، لا يحتمل بيانها في هذا الشرح الموجز وأكثرها في البحر المحيط (۱)". اهـ ثم ذكر تتمة لكتاب الحظر والإباحة، وقال: «وإنما أوردتها وإن لم تكن من فروع المسائل المذكورة في هذا الكتاب، لعموم البلوى بها، وهي تشتمل على عشرين فصلاً». اهـ
كما يمتاز هذا الشرح بكثرة مصادره بشكل واضح لمن طالع (۱) ويسمى أيضاً: منية الفقهاء الشيخ الزاهدي، واسمـه بـديـع بـن منـصـور القُربني، الإمام القاضي الفقيه من انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية في زمانه، وله تصانيف معتبرة منها : البحر المحيط، الموسوم بـ منية الفقهاء، كما في الفوائد البهية ص .٥٤
This introduction from the author clearly shows his work in this commentary and the methodology he followed and the points he paid attention to, which he carried out in the best way.
It is the most comprehensive commentary of al-Quduri and the most widespread among scholars of the madhhab who came after him. You see them frequently quoting from it, relying on it, especially in the subsidiary fiqh issues that he adds to the book's topics, such as the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and others.
As an example of his inclusion of additional issues beyond what is in al-Quduri, when he finished commenting on the Book of Permission and Prohibition from al-Quduri, he said: 'The issues of this book are many and unlimited, it is not possible to explain them in this brief commentary; most of them are in al-Bahr al-Muhit.' End. Then he mentioned a supplement to the Book of Permission and Prohibition, saying: 'I have only mentioned them, even though they are not from the branches of the issues mentioned in this book, due to the general need for them, and it includes twenty chapters.' End.
Also, this commentary is distinguished by its abundance of sources, which is clear to anyone who reads it. (1) It is also called: Munyat al-Fuqaha' by al-Shaykh al-Zahidi, his name is Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini, the imam, judge, jurist to whom the leadership of the Hanafis in his time was attributed, and he has respectable works including al-Bahr al-Muhit, known as Munyat al-Fuqaha', as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 54.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a later commentator's or editor's description of the commentary's qualities, though it may be part of al-Maydani's own text. It states that al-Lubab is the most comprehensive Sharh of al-Quduri and the most widely consulted by later Hanafi scholars. It highlights that the author added extra fatawa and issues not directly from al-Quduri, especially in the Book of Permission and Prohibition, because these issues were commonly needed by people. The author admits he added a twenty-chapter supplement on this topic. The passage also notes the work's reliance on multiple sources, specifically mentioning al-Bahr al-Muhit (also called Munyat al-Fuqaha') by Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini. This shows the author's method of supplementing the matn with practical fatwa material.

Key Terms
كتاب الحظر والإباحة (Kitab al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah): The chapter on Permission and Prohibition, which deals with rulings on permissible and impermissible actions.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A common occurrence or widespread need; used as a justification for including extra legal material.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because of general need (عموم البلوى)
C) To show off his knowledge
D) To correct al-Quduri's mistakes

Key Takeaway
Hanafi commentators often expand their works by adding fatwa supplements justified by the principle of 'umum al-balwa' to meet practical community needs.

Features and Methodology of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri
Describes the commentary's scope, sources, and author's approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Al-Zahidi's methodology in his commentary Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri and identify its distinctive features.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is the most comprehensive Hanafi commentary on Al-Quduri, adding extra issues from a vast library.

This lesson explores the structure and methodology of one of the most influential Hanafi commentaries: Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri by Al-Zahidi. Understanding how Al-Zahidi compiled his work—adding supplementary issues, citing multiple sources, and humbly inviting corrections—gives us insight into the standards of Hanafi scholarship and the development of the madhhab's textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentary's scope and reputation
Note the author's claim that it is the broadest and most widespread commentary, frequently quoted by later scholars. Understand its role as a standard reference.
2
Examine the addition of extra issues
See how Al-Zahidi appended a supplement of twenty chapters to the book of al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah because of public need (عموم البلوى). This reflects practical jurisprudence.
3
Analyze the source richness
The text mentions that Al-Zahidi owned a large library and quoted many earlier Hanafi imams, such as Al-Karkhi and Al-Jassas. This demonstrates the depth of his research.
4
Understand the author's humility and request for corrections
Al-Zahidi's concluding remarks show his awareness of human fallibility and his invitation to readers to correct errors. This reflects scholarly integrity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
النسيان، وإلحاح عامة الشركاء والإخوان، والله المستعان، وعليه التكلان. اهـ
وهذه المقدمة من المؤلف تبين بوضوح عمله في هذا الشرح والمنهج الذي سار عليه والنقاط التي اهتم بها في شرحه، والتي قام بها خير قيام.
وهو أوسع شروح القدوري، وأكثرها انتشاراً بين علماء المذهب ممن جاء بعده، فتراهم يكثرون النقل عنه، معتمدين ذلك، وبخاصة في الفروع الفقهية التي يُلحقها بمسائل الكتاب، كصاحب البحر الرائق، وغيره.
وكمثال لإيراده مسائل زائدة على ما في القدوري، فإنه لما انتهى من شرح كتاب الحظر والإباحة من القدوري، قال: ومسائل هذا الكتاب كثيرة غير محصورة، لا يحتمل بيانها في هذا الشرح الموجز وأكثرها في البحر المحيط (۱). اهـ ثم ذكر تتمة لكتاب الحظر والإباحة، وقال: «وإنما أوردتها وإن لم تكن من فروع المسائل المذكورة في هذا الكتاب، لعموم البلوى بها، وهي تشتمل على عشرين فصلاً». اهـ
كما يمتاز هذا الشرح بكثرة مصادره بشكل واضح لمن طالع (۱) ويسمى أيضاً: منية الفقهاء الشيخ الزاهدي، واسمه بديع بن منصور القُربني، الإمام القاضي الفقيه من انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية في زمانه، وله تصانيف معتبرة منها : البحر المحيط، الموسوم بـ منية الفقهاء، كما في الفوائد البهية ص .٥٤
فيه، ويظهر أن مؤلفه كان يملك مكتبةً كبيرة نادرة، فيها أُمات كتاب المذهب، وكتب من سبقه من أئمة الحنفية.
فتراه مثلاً في مسألة وجوب الحج زمن خروج القرامطة، وفتنتهم وقتلهم للحجاج، ينقل نقولاً كثيرة عن أئمة المذهب الذين عاصروا تلك الفتنة أو قاربوا زمانها، كالكرخي والجصاص، وأبي عبد الله البلخي، وأبي قاسم الصفار، وأبي الليث، والوبري، وأبي بكر الوراق، وغيرهم، فينقل رأي كل واحد منهم، وأن منهم من أوجب ومنهم من أسقط، ووجهة نظر كل منهم، وهكذا...
وقد قال الزاهدي في خاتمة المجتبى :
«لقد بذلت جهدي وطاقتي، وأعملت مكنتي واستطاعتي في التحاشي عن التبديل والتحريف والتجنب في نقل المسائل والعلل على الكتب الموثوق بها عن التغيير المخل والتصحيف، لكن القلب بوسواس الدنيا عليل، والخاطر بسبب الكبر وكثرة الدرس حسير كليل، والنسيان من خصائص الإنسانية، والخطأ والزلل شعار الآدمية.
فالمأمول ممن كرَّم هذا الشرح بالنظر فيه، والإحاطة بدقائق مبانيه، وأسرار معانيه : أن يتدارك هفواته وزلاته فيه، بعد ما أتقن وجوب تلافيه، فإني ما ركبتُ فيه تركيباً، ولا آثرت في بسط المسائل والعلل وإيجازها وتلفيقها ترتيباً، إلا بعد طول التأمل، وكثرة المراجعات إليه والتفكر والله ولى العصمة واللطف والتوفيق...». اهـ
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Forgetfulness, and the importunity of common partners and brothers, and Allah is the Helper, and upon Him is reliance. End.
This introduction from the author clearly shows his work in this commentary, the methodology he followed, and the points he cared about in his commentary, which he carried out excellently.
It is the broadest of the commentaries on al-Quduri, and the most widespread among scholars of the school who came after him. You see them frequently quoting from it, relying on it, especially in the jurisprudential branches that he appends to the book's issues, like the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and others.
As an example of his adding extra issues beyond what is in al-Quduri: when he finished explaining the book of al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah from al-Quduri, he said: 'The issues of this book are numerous and uncountable; it is not possible to explain them in this concise commentary, and most of them are in al-Bahr al-Muhit (1).' End. Then he mentioned a supplement to the book of al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah, and said: 'I have only mentioned them, even if they are not from the branches of issues mentioned in this book, due to the general need for them, and they comprise twenty chapters.' End.
Also, this commentary is distinguished by its abundance of sources, clearly apparent to whoever studies (1) Also called: Munyat al-Fuqaha' by al-Shaykh al-Zahidi, and his name is Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini, the imam, judge, jurist, to whom the leadership of the Hanafis in his time reached, and he has authoritative works including: al-Bahr al-Muhit, known as Munyat al-Fuqaha', as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 54.
it, and it appears that its author owned a large, rare library, containing the primary books of the school, and the books of the Hanafi imams who preceded him.
For example, on the issue of the obligation of Hajj at the time of the Qaramita's emergence, their sedition, and their killing of pilgrims, he transmits many quotes from the imams of the school who lived through that sedition or were close to its time, such as al-Karkhi, al-Jassas, Abu Abdullah al-Balkhi, Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar, Abu al-Layth, al-Wabiri, Abu Bakr al-Warraq, and others. He transmits the opinion of each one of them, and that some made it obligatory and some dropped it, and the viewpoint of each, and so on.
And al-Zahidi said in the conclusion of al-Mujtaba:
'I have exerted my effort and capacity, and employed my ability and capability in avoiding substitution and distortion, and in avoiding, in transmitting issues and causes from the trustworthy books, detrimental changes and corruption. But the heart is ill with the whisperings of this world, and the mind, due to old age and much study, is weary and dull. Forgetfulness is among the characteristics of humanity, and error and stumbling are the emblem of mankind.
So the hope from anyone who honors this commentary by looking into it, and grasping the subtleties of its structures and the secrets of its meanings, is that he rectify its lapses and slips, after he has mastered the necessity of making amends. For I have not composed any composition in it, nor preferred in expanding issues and causes and summarizing and compiling them any arrangement, except after lengthy contemplation and numerous revisions and reflection. And Allah is the Guardian of infallibility, kindness, and success...' End.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage provides an overview of the commentary 'Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri' by Al-Zahidi (Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini). It first establishes that this commentary is the most comprehensive and widely circulated among later Hanafi scholars, who frequently quote from it, especially in supplementary issues. The author demonstrates how Al-Zahidi added extra issues beyond the original text of Al-Quduri, such as after finishing the book on prohibitions and permissions, he appended a supplement containing twenty chapters due to public need. The commentary is noted for its extensive use of sources, reflecting Al-Zahidi's large and rare library containing core Hanafi texts and works of earlier imams. An example is given: on the issue of the obligation of Hajj during the Qaramita rebellion, Al-Zahidi transmits multiple opinions from contemporary and near-contemporary scholars like Al-Karkhi, Al-Jassas, and others, showing who deemed it obligatory and who dropped it. Finally, the passage quotes Al-Zahidi's concluding remarks from his work 'Al-Mujtaba', where he humbly acknowledges human fallibility and asks readers to correct any errors, emphasizing his thorough effort in composing the work.

Key Terms
اللباب شرح القدوري (Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri): A famous Hanafi commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini al-Zahidi.
الزاهدي (Al-Zahidi): Badi' ibn Mansur al-Qurbini, a leading Hanafi jurist and author of Al-Lubab and Al-Bahr al-Muhit.
البحر المحيط (Al-Bahr al-Muhit): Another work by Al-Zahidi, also known as Munyat al-Fuqaha', containing extensive fiqh issues.
عموم البلوى (Umum al-balwa): A principle meaning 'general public need' or 'widespread occurrence,' used to justify including extra issues in a fiqh work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Al-Zahidi gave for appending a supplement to the book of al-Hathr wa al-Ibahah?
A) He wanted to show off his knowledge.
B) The issues were relevant to many people (عموم البلوى).
C) He was required to do so by his teacher.
D) He had extra space in his commentary.

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri is distinguished by its comprehensive scope, addition of practical issues, reliance on an extensive library, and the author's humble scholarly attitude.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
On the Authority of al-Zahidi's al-Mujtaba
Defends al-Mujtaba's reliability despite weak narrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why occasional weak narrations in a Hanafi commentary do not necessarily invalidate its authority and apply the principle of restricted acceptance.

Core Idea
A commentary's authority survives weak narrations; only direct contradictions to established principles are rejected.

You may have heard that some scholars critique al-Zahidi's al-Mujtaba for containing weak narrations. Does that mean we should discard this major commentary? This lesson examines how the Hanafi tradition handles such criticisms, showing that even respected works like Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah have been corrected without losing their standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the critique
What specific objection is raised against al-Mujtaba? The author states that some weak narrations (riwayat da'ifah) may be found that contradict the established principles of the madhhab.
The objection is not that the book is full of errors, but that occasional weak reports exist.
2
Understand the author's response
The author argues that this possibility does not 'demolish al-Mujtaba' nor invalidate reliance on it. He likens it to other authoritative works like Hashiyat Ibn Abidin, which have been corrected but remain relied upon.
Correction is a normal part of scholarly verification, not a reason to reject a work.
3
Extract the general principle
The principle is: any narration in a commentary that contradicts the usul of the madhhab is not accepted, but this does not render the entire book unreliable. The reader must be vigilant, but the work's overall authority remains intact.
This is not specific to al-Zahidi; it applies to all extended books.
4
Apply to other works
The author gives the example of Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah, which despite many corrections by later scholars (al-Sindi, al-Rafi'i, Ahmad Rida Khan), is still considered a primary source. Similarly, al-Mujtaba remains authoritative.
Even the most revered works undergo istidrak (correction).

الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
الفقهاء، لـه اليد الباسطة في المذهب، والباع الطويل في الكلام والمناظرة، وله التصانيف التي سارت بها الركبان كالقنية، وشرح مختصر القدوري، المسمى بالمجتبى». اهـ
وأيضاً بالنظر فيما قاله الزاهدي في مقدمة كتابه المجتبى، مما نقلته عنه قبل قليل، وما قاله في خاتمة كتابه هذا: «من إعمال جهـده في النقل عن الكتب الموثوق بها متحاشياً عن التبديل والتحريف، متقياً عن المجازفة في نقل الأحكام والعلل، وما ركب تركيباً إلا بعد طول التأمل، وكثرة المراجعات إليه والتفكر...الخ.
وهكذا بالنظر أيضاً إلى كثرة النقول في كتب الشراح من أئمـة المذهب عن المجتبى، واعتمادهم عليه مثل تبيين الحقائق، وفتح القدير، والبحر الرائق، وغيرها كثير، وقد ذكر ابن نجيم في مقدمة البحر حيـن عـد مصادره التي أخذ منها، فذكر منها المجتبى للزاهدي. وهكذا، يمكن أن يعلق على كلام الإمام اللكنـوي وكـلام مـن قبله، ومن جاء بعده، بما قيل أيضاً في الحداد صاحب السراج الوهاج، والجوهرة النيرة، مما سيأتي ذكره بأنه لا مانع من أن يكون في كتب الزاهدي بعض الروايات الضعيفة التي تخالف ما عليه قواعد المذهب، لكن هذا الاحتمال لا ينسف المجتبى هذا الشرح العظيم النفيس لمختصر القدوري ولا يبطل الاعتماد على الزاهدي وعموم كتبه بهذا الكلام المجمل مما تقدم ذكره
ويبقى القارئ متنبهاً يقظاً لمثل تلك الروايات والأقوال، التي لا يخلو في الغالب منها كتاب مبسوط ط مطول، قد أخذ صاحبه على نفسه التوسع في النقل، فلا يُقبل ما فيها إن كان فيه مخالفة ظاهرة لأصول المذهب وقواعده، فالأمر مقيَّد، وليس مطلقاً، وليس هذا خاصاً بكتب الزاهدي، بل هو عام في كل كتاب.
وعلى سبيل المثال : فإن حاشية ابن عابدين مشهورة جداً في اعتمادها وقبولها، لكن مع هذا جاء عصريه الإمام الفقيه المحدث الشيخ محمد عابد السندي الأنصاري (ت ١٢٥٧هـ)، فاستدرك عليـه أشياء كثيرة في كتابه الواسع : طوالع الأنوار شرح الدر المختار ثم لخصها العلامة الرافعي (ت ۱۳۲۳هـ) في تقريراته على ابن عابدين، وزاد عليها، ثم جاء العلامة الفقيه المحقق المدقق أحمد رضا خان ت ١٣٤٠هـ) ، فألف كتابه الدقيق النافع: «جد الممتار على رد المحتار»، واستدرك أيضاً أموراً كثيرة على ابن عابدين، تدل على إمامته في الفقه الحنفي، ومع هذا كله لا يُمكن أبداً أن يقول قائل بعدم اعتبار حاشية ابن عابدين، وعدم اعتمادهـا بـسبب مـا اسـتدرك عليه من أمور كثيرة. وهكذا ما زال العلماء يستدرك بعضهم على بعض ؛ تحقيقـاً للعلم، وإثباتاً للصواب أو بياناً للأصح.

The jurists, he had a widespread hand in the madhhab, and a long capacity in speech and debate, and he has authored works that traveled far and wide such as al-Qunyah, and the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri named al-Mujtaba. Also, by considering what al-Zahidi said in the introduction of his book al-Mujtaba, which I quoted earlier, and what he said at the end of this book: 'He exerted his effort in transmitting from trustworthy books, avoiding alteration and distortion, refraining from rashness in transmitting rulings and underlying reasons, and he did not compose a composition except after lengthy reflection, numerous revisions, and contemplation... etc.' Likewise, by considering also the abundance of quotations in the books of the commentators from the imams of the madhhab from al-Mujtaba, and their reliance upon it, such as Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Fath al-Qadir, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and many others. Ibn Nujaym mentioned in the introduction of al-Bahr when he counted his sources that he took from, he mentioned among them al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi. Thus, one may comment on the statements of Imam al-Lucknowi and those before him and after him, including what was also said about al-Haddad, author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, which will be mentioned later, that there is no harm if there are some weak narrations in al-Zahidi's books that contradict the established rules of the madhhab. However, this possibility does not demolish al-Mujtaba, this great precious commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, nor invalidate reliance on al-Zahidi and his general books with this general statement mentioned earlier. The reader remains alert and vigilant for such narrations and statements, which most extended books are not free from, the author having taken upon himself to expand in transmission. So what is in them is not accepted if it contains an apparent contradiction to the fundamentals of the madhhab and its principles. The matter is restricted, not absolute, and this is not specific to al-Zahidi's books, but is general to every book. For example: Indeed, the Hashiyah of Ibn Abidin is very famous in its reliance and acceptance, but along with this, his contemporary, the imam, jurist, and hadith scholar Sheikh Muhammad Abid al-Sindi al-Ansari (d. 1257 AH) came and corrected many things in his extensive book Tawali' al-Anwar Sharh al-Durr al-Mukhtar, then summarized them by al-Allama al-Rafi'i (d. 1323 AH) in his notes on Ibn Abidin, and added to them. Then came the distinguished, exacting jurist and scholar Ahmad Rida Khan (d. 1340 AH) and authored his precise and beneficial book 'Jadd al-Mumtar ala Radd al-Muhtar', and also corrected many things on Ibn Abidin, indicating his imamate in Hanafi fiqh. Yet despite all this, no one can ever say that Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah is not considered or not relied upon due to the many things corrected upon it. Thus, scholars continue to correct one another for the verification of knowledge, proof of correctness, or clarification of the most correct. Among the important texts praising al-Zahidi's books and his statements and corrections, which confirm reliance on al-Zahidi, is what Imam al-Dhahabi said. (1) (1) Tarikh al-Islam 14/901 (474), 1st ed., Dar al-Maghrib al-Islami, 1424 AH.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion from the third chapter of the author's work, which surveys commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author defends the authority of al-Zahidi's commentary 'al-Mujtaba' against potential criticisms that it contains weak narrations contradicting the established madhhab. He establishes a key principle: the existence of some weak narrations in a large commentary does not negate its overall authority, provided that such contradictions are not openly accepted. He supports this by referencing that even Ibn Abidin's famous Hashiyah, despite being extensively corrected by later scholars, remains a relied-upon source. Thus, the passage clarifies that scholarly correction does not undermine a work's standing; rather, it is a normal part of scholarly verification. The author emphasizes that al-Zahidi's work is widely cited by major Hanafi authorities and that al-Dhahabi's praise further confirms its reliability.

Key Terms
الروايات الضعيفة (al-riwāyāt al-ḍaʿīfah): Narrations or reports that are weak in authenticity or do not meet the standards for establishing legal rulings.
أصول المذهب (uṣūl al-madhhab): The foundational principles and methodological rules of the Hanafi school that govern legal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument of the author regarding occasional weak narrations in al-Mujtaba?
A) It makes the book completely unreliable.
B) It does not invalidate the book's overall authority.
C) It proves al-Zahidi was careless.
D) It requires rejecting all of al-Zahidi's works.

Key Takeaway
Occasional weak narrations in a commentary do not undermine its authority; only narrations clearly contradicting the madhhab's usul are rejected, and the work remains relied upon.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Three Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Listing and describing commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, state their authors and approximate dates, and explain their significance in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
These commentaries show the living tradition of Hanafi fiqh—each work builds on al-Quduri's matn.

The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational text in the Hanafi school, studied for centuries. To master it, scholars produced commentaries (shuruh) and summaries (talkhis) that clarify, expand, and sometimes critique the original. This lesson introduces three such works from the 7th/13th century, connecting you to the chain of Hanafi learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three commentaries mentioned.
List the titles exactly as given in the source: Al-Bayan, Al-Fawa'id al-Badriyya (or al-Badriyya), and Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Each serves a different purpose: full commentary, gloss, and summary.
2
Note the authors and their death dates.
Al-Muqani (664 AH), al-Ramishi (667 AH), and al-Nujabadi (668 AH). These dates show they were contemporaries.
Knowing the death dates helps assess the reliability and chronology of the works.
3
Observe the manuscript and library details.
The author cites specific copies (e.g., Library of Congress, al-Khalidiyya) and variations in naming. This shows the importance of manuscript verification.
A single work may be known by multiple titles (e.g., al-Badriyya).
4
Understand the genre difference.
Al-Bayan is a sharh (full commentary), Al-Fawa'id al-Badriyya is a gloss (ta'liq) or shorter commentary, and Talkhis is a summary. Each serves different study levels.
Students should first consult a sharh for detailed explanation, then a talkhis for quick review.

(1) As for manuscripts of al-Mujtaba, there are many copies of it, including an Azhari copy which Allah facilitated for me to obtain an image of; it is in two large volumes, the first in 430 folios and the second in 405 folios, copied in the year 1127 AH. The book has been fully edited at the University of Baghdad - may Allah relieve its people - and several master's and doctoral theses have been registered on it. It is now confined to the university shelves, after having been in the manuscript shelves. May Allah Almighty facilitate its publication so that its benefit may be widespread. 35. Al-Bayan Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. (A) By Muhammad ibn Rasul ibn Yunus ibn Muhammad al-Muqani, died 664 AH (3), may Allah have mercy on him. 36. Al-Fawa'id al-Badriyya 'ala al-Quduri. By Hamid al-Din Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Darir al-Ramishi al-Bukhari. (1) See the remainder of the copies in al-Fihris al-Shamil 9/64. (2) As informed to me during the Hajj season of 1430 AH by the noble and excellent brother, the brilliant Dr. Ahmad al-Ani from Fallujah, may Allah protect him and benefit the people and the country through him. 168, Kashf (3) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 3/154, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p., Kashf al-Zunun 2/1632, and in Hadiyyat al-Arifin 2/128 he is called al-Mawqufati. Died 667 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. (2) 419 Brockelmann mentioned him in Tarikh al-Adab al-Arabi (3), and mentioned that there is a copy in the library of Qul 1/381, as mentioned by the authors of al-Fihris al-Shamil (3), and that it is anonymous, and that there is a copy in the Library of Congress, Washington (100), written in 842 AH. They mentioned in al-Fihris al-Shamil (4) a book entitled al-Badriyya fi Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri, anonymous, and that there is a copy in al-Khalidiyya in Jerusalem (64), written in 858 AH. Perhaps it is al-Fawa'id al-Badriyya; so let it be verified by referring to these copies. 37. Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By the jurist Imam Zahir al-Din Muhammad ibn Umar al-Nujabadi (al-Nuhabadi) al-Bukhari al-Hanafi, Imam of al-Mustansiriyya in Baghdad, died 668 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. *(0) Al-Qurashi mentioned him in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, and others. (1) His biography is in Taj al-Tarajim p. 215. (2) 3/271, followed by Sezgin in al-Turath al-Arabi 3/120. (3) 7/739. (E) 90/Y. (5) 3/291, and Kashf al-Zunun 2/1634, and see Taj al-Tarajim p. 572, where the book's name is incorrectly given as 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and the word 'Talkhis' is omitted.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic listing of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author first discusses the manuscripts of al-Mujtaba (likely another work) and then proceeds to enumerate three specific commentaries: Al-Bayan Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Muhammad ibn Rasul al-Muqani (d. 664 AH), Al-Fawa'id al-Badriyya 'ala al-Quduri by Hamid al-Din al-Ramishi (d. 667 AH), and Talkhis Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Zahir al-Din al-Nujabadi (d. 668 AH). For each, he provides the author's name, death date, and references to manuscript locations. He notes that the second commentary is also known as al-Badriyya and that there is an anonymous copy possibly identical to it. The third commentary is a summary (talkhis) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This passage is part of the front matter of the current book, providing context on the scholarly tradition surrounding Al-Quduri's work.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal text by Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a core textbook of the Hanafi school.
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a prominent Hanafi jurist.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains the text in detail, often providing proofs and discussions.
تلخيص (talkhis): A summary that condenses the original text, often omitting proofs for brevity.

Verifying Hanafi Manuscript Traditions
Manuscript bibliography for Hanafi commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a Hanafi commentary manuscript reference and state its significance for the madhhab.

Core Idea
A Hanafi text's authority depends on its chain of transmission — manuscript verification safeguards the madhhab.

The Hanafi tradition is preserved not only in printed texts but in countless manuscripts. Understanding how scholars trace and verify these manuscripts is essential for assessing the reliability of a transmitted ruling. This lesson introduces you to the scholarly apparatus used to identify commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core text
Note the primary work being commented upon — Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This is the referent for all commentaries listed.
The matn (text) is by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
2
Parse the death date
The entry states 'المتوفى سنة ٦٦٧ هـ' — the commentator died in 667 AH. This helps date the commentary and locate the author in Hanafi history.
No name is given here; cross-reference with other sources.
3
Locate the manuscript references
The text cites Brockelmann's Geschichte der Arabischen Litteratur and the Comprehensive Index (fihris shamil). These are standard bibliographic tools for Islamic manuscripts.
Manuscript locations: Qulu Library, Library of Congress, al-Khalidiyya (Jerusalem).
4
Assess the anonymous status
The entry notes 'لمجهول' (anonymous) for the commentary al-Badriyya. Anonymity reduces the authority of the work for fiqh derivation, but the text itself may still be valuable for historical study.
Later verification using manuscript copies may identify the author.
5
Connect to broader madhhab history
This list shows the living tradition of sharh (commentary) around a core text — each commentary refines, explains, and transmits Hanafi fiqh across generations.
Knowing the commentator and his era helps assess the weight of his interpretations.

Three Classical Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Bibliographical Introduction
Biographical listing of three commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and state their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri's scholarly progeny includes abridgments, commentaries, and combined works – each with unique features.

When studying a foundational Hanafi matn like Mukhtasar al-Quduri, it is crucial to know the key commentaries that explicate or abridge it. This lesson introduces three such works: an abridgment by a Shafi'i scholar, a standard commentary, and a unique combination of matn and poetic text. Understanding these works will help you navigate Hanafi references and appreciate the scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify each work and its author
Read the passage and list the three works: Jawami' al-Kalim al-Sharifah (al-Mawsili), Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri (al-Khabbazi), and Majma' al-Bahrayn (Ibn al-Sa'ati). Note the death dates and any special affiliations.
Al-Mawsili was Shafi'i but wrote this work on Hanafi fiqh at the request of a vizier.
2
Categorize the type of work
Determine whether each is an abridgment (mukhtasar), a commentary (sharh), or a combined work (jami'). Al-Mawsili's is an abridgment of Quduri; al-Khabbazi's is a commentary; Ibn al-Sa'ati's combines Quduri with al-Nasafi's poem.
Ibn al-Sa'ati's work is particularly innovative.
3
Note manuscript and publication details
Observe where copies are located (e.g., Atif Efendi Library in Istanbul, Ahmadiyya in Tunis) and any date discrepancies (al-Mawsili's death year confusion). These details are important for scholarly verification.
Death dates may vary between sources; always cross-check.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

38. An abridgment of Mukhtasar al-Quduri called: (Jawami' al-Kalim al-Sharifah on the Madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifah).
By Imam Taj al-Din Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Muhammad ibn Yunus al-Mawsili al-Shafi'i, died in 670 AH, or 671 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It was at the suggestion of Ata Malik al-Juwayni. Its opening: 'Praise be to Allah, the Eternal...' end.
The author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned it in two places, first in 2/1632, and said: 'He was a sign in the ability to summarize,' and here he made
his death year 771 AH, one and seventy and seven hundred, thus in numerals and writing. And the second place in 2/1634, and made his death year 670 AH, seventy and six hundred, thus in numerals and writing, then he wrote his death year: (671 AH), only in numerals. And the compilers of al-Fihris al-Shamil (1) mentioned a copy for him in the Ahmadiyya in Tunis (2259), and they mentioned his death year as 671 AH.

39. Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
By al-Khabbazi Jalal al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad, died in 691 AH, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him.
He has a copy in the Atif Efendi Library in Istanbul, no. (906), with 216 folios, dated 723 AH, as in Mu'jam al-Makhtutat al-Mawjuda fi Maktabat Istambul wa-Anatoli, and the compilers of al-Fihris al-Shamil mentioned it without the previous data.

40. Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn (He combined between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Poem of al-Nasafi).
By Muzaffar al-Din Ibn al-Sa'ati Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Taghlib, the great imam and jurist, died in 694 AH, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him.
And he combined in this book between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Poem of al-Nasafi 'Nazm al-Khilafiyyat', with additions, and arranged it well, and excelled in its abridgment.
And the Poem of al-Nasafi is a poem in Hanafi fiqh, coming in (2669) verses, by Abu Hafs al-Nasafi Umar ibn Muhammad, died in 537 AH, author of Talibat al-Talabah.
The author of Kashf al-Zunun said about Majma' al-Bahrayn:
.1( 2/1026) p.
(2) 5/460, and see Sezgin 3/120 .
(3) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 1/209, Taj al-Tarajim p. 95, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah 26, Kashf al-Zunun 2/1599 .
.4( 2/1600)
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of three works that serve as commentaries or abridgments of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri. It is from the introduction of the modern edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, typically detailing the scholarly works that expanded upon or condensed the original matn. The first entry is 'Jawami' al-Kalim al-Sharifah' by Taj al-Din al-Mawsili al-Shafi'i, which is an abridgment of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Despite being a Shafi'i scholar, al-Mawsili authored this work on the Hanafi madhhab at the request of the vizier Ata Malik al-Juwayni. The passage notes confusion regarding his death date, with Kashf al-Zunun recording differing years. The second entry is a commentary by al-Khabbazi, with manuscript details locating it in Istanbul. The third is 'Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn' by Ibn al-Sa'ati, which uniquely combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri with al-Nasafi's poetic work on Hanafi fiqh, 'Nazm al-Khilafiyyat'. This listing helps identify authoritative commentaries for study and reference, showing the scholarly tradition of explaining and abridging core Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), central to the Hanafi curriculum.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn), clarifying its rulings and providing evidence.
منظومة النسفي (Manzumat al-Nasafi): A didactic poem on Hanafi fiqh by Abu Hafs al-Nasafi (d. 537 AH), containing 2669 verses, known as 'Nazm al-Khilafiyyat'.
جوامع الكلم الشريفة (Jawami' al-Kalim al-Sharifah): An abridgment of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Mawsili, meaning 'Collections of Noble Words'.
مجمع البحرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn): A combined work by Ibn al-Sa'ati that merges Mukhtasar al-Quduri with al-Nasafi's poem, meaning 'The Confluence of the Two Seas'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowing the key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri is essential for deepening one's study of Hanafi fiqh and locating authoritative references.
