Majma' al-Bahrayn: A Combined Commentary on Two Hanafi Texts
Describes a commentary combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Nazm al-Nasafi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two texts combined in Majma' al-Bahrayn and state the significance of Ibn al-Sa'ati's work in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Sa'ati's Majma' al-Bahrayn merges two key Hanafi texts into one concise, authoritative commentary.

This lesson introduces a unique work in Hanafi literature: Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn by Muzaffar al-Din Ibn al-Sa'ati. The passage describes how this commentary combines the well-known Mukhtasar al-Quduri with the versified Manzumat al-Nasafi, creating a compact yet comprehensive reference. Understanding the nature of such combined works helps students appreciate the scholarly methods of transmission and compilation in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two base texts
Mukhtasar al-Quduri (prose) by Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) and Manzumat al-Nasafi (poetry) by Abu Hafs al-Nasafi (d. 537 AH). Recognize their foundational roles in Hanafi fiqh.
Mukhtasar is an introductory manual; Manzuma is a versified work on points of disagreement (khilaf).
2
Recognize the purpose of the compilation
Ibn al-Sa'ati aimed to conjoin these works to facilitate comparison and memorization, arranging them excellently in a concise format.
The text says: 'جمع بين مختصر القدوري ومنظومة النسفي مع زوائد ورتبه فأحسن وأبدع في اختصاره'.
3
Note the scholarly apparatus and manuscript evidence
The passage provides details of manuscripts (dates, locations) and transcribes the author's ijaza (permission) to Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi, emphasizing accuracy and preservation.
Ijaza is a key aspect of reliable textual transmission in the Hanafi tradition.

الفصل الثالث: شروح مختصر القدوري
منه نسخة بخط المؤلف، موقوفة بجامع السلطان محمد الفاتح، وقد ضرب في بعض مواضعه، وكشط، وفرغ من تأليفه سنة ٦٩٠هـ. وهو كتاب حفظه سهل؛ لنهاية إيجازه، حَلُه صَعْب؛ لغاية إعجازه، بحر مسائله، جم فضائله...». اهـ
كما توجد نسخة نفيسة من مجمع البحرين، نقلت عن نسخة المؤلف، ثم كتب عليها مؤلفه بخطه: قوبلت هذه النسخة، وكتبت من أصلي، فصحت ووافقت، والله يعفو عما طغى به القلم، أو تجاوز عنه النظر.
وقد أجزتُ لمالكها الشيخ الإمام العالم الفاضل، والورع الكامل، ذي الأخلاق الكريمة، والفضائل الجسيمة، ركن الدين السمرقندي، أدام الله حراسته، وكتب سلامته، أن يرويها عني. وكذلك أجزتُ له رواية الشرح الذي صنفته بعد، إذا وقعت له نسخة يثق إلى صحتها، وكذلك جميع ما يصح عنده أنه من مقولاتي، أو منقولاتي، أو مسموعاتي، أو مستجازاتي، فهو ـ أدام الله أيامه ـ يُجَمل ما يرويه، وأنا معتمد على الله تعالى، ثم ملتمس من خدمته أن يصون هذا الكتاب، ويحفظه عن تغيير يقع فيه...». اهـ من الجواهر المضية (١).
وتوجد نسخ عديدة لمجمع البحرين، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل (۳).
.۲۱۱ - ۲۱۰/۱ (۱)
۸۲/۹ (۲)
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri (421). It has a copy in the Atif Efendi Library in Istanbul, numbered (906), with 216 folios, dated 723 AH, as in the dictionary of manuscripts in Istanbul libraries and mentioned by the authors of the Comprehensive Index without the previous information. (2) 40 - Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn (a compilation between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Manzuma of al-Nasafi) by Muzaffar al-Din Ibn al-Sa'ati Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Taghlub, the great jurist imam, died 694 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. (3) He compiled in this book between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Manzuma of al-Nasafi 'Nazm al-Khilafiyyat' with additions, arranged it well, and excelled in conciseness. The Manzuma of al-Nasafi is a poem in Hanafi fiqh, consisting of 2669 verses, by Abu Hafs al-Nasafi Umar ibn Muhammad, died 537 AH, author of Talbat al-Talaba. The author of Kashf al-Zunun (4) said about Majma' al-Bahrayn: 'A copy in the author's handwriting, endowed in the Sultan Muhammad al-Fatih mosque, with some places struck and scraped, and completed its authorship in 690 AH. It is a book easy to memorize due to its extreme conciseness, difficult to solve due to its extreme brevity, a sea of issues, comprehensive in virtues...' End quote. There is also a precious copy of Majma' al-Bahrayn, copied from the author's copy, on which the author wrote in his own handwriting: 'This copy has been collated, and I wrote it from my original, so it is correct and conforms. Allah forgives what the pen slipped or the eye overlooked.' And I have given permission to its owner, the virtuous and ascetic scholar, the perfect ascetic, of noble character and great virtues, Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi, may Allah preserve his safety and write his security, to narrate it from me. Likewise, I permitted him to narrate the commentary I composed afterwards, if he obtains a copy he trusts in its authenticity, and likewise all that he finds correct from my sayings, transmissions, hearings, or licenses. He – may his days be blessed – may include what he narrates, and I rely on Allah Almighty, then I request from his service to preserve this book and protect it from any change that may occur...' End quote from al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya (1). There are multiple copies of Majma' al-Bahrayn, see the Comprehensive Index (3). (1) 1/210-211 (2) 9/82
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage belongs to the front matter of the book, specifically the third chapter which lists and describes commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It introduces one such commentary: Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn by Muzaffar al-Din Ibn al-Sa'ati (d. 694 AH). The author explains that this work combines two classical Hanafi texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri (a foundational legal text) and the Manzuma (poem) of al-Nasafi, which is a versified work on points of doctrinal disagreement (al-Khilafiyyat). The passage then provides manuscript details, including a copy in the Atif Efendi Library in Istanbul dated 723 AH, and another in the author's own hand from 690 AH, which was endowed in the Sultan Muhammad al-Fatih mosque. Notably, the author's permission (ijaza) is transcribed, where he authorizes Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi to transmit the book, and also his later commentary, stressing the importance of accuracy and preservation. This ijaza is a typical scholarly practice for ensuring reliable transmission of texts. The passage ends by stating that multiple copies exist as per the Comprehensive Index. No legal rulings or proofs are present; this is purely bibliographical and historical.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied as an introductory manual.
منظومة النسفي (Manzumat al-Nasafi): A poem by Abu Hafs al-Nasafi (d. 537 AH) containing 2669 verses on Hanafi fiqh, focusing on points of khilaf (disagreement).
مجمع البحرين وملتقى النهرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn): A commentary by Ibn al-Sa'ati that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Manzumat al-Nasafi, adding benefits and arranging them concisely.
الإجازة (al-Ijaza): A scholarly permission granted by an author to a specific person to transmit and teach a book.

Key Takeaway
Majma' al-Bahrayn is a combined commentary of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Manzumat al-Nasafi, known for its conciseness and the author's personal ijaza ensuring reliable transmission.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Understanding Hanafi Commentarial Tradition
Bibliographic listing of commentaries with manuscript and ijazah details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a Hanafi commentarial tradition as presented in a bibliographic passage, including manuscript details, ijazah, and the author's own super-commentary.

Core Idea
Hanafi scholarly works are transmitted through careful manuscript chains and ijazah; commentaries often generate further super-commentaries.

This passage from Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri provides a window into the rich tradition of Hanafi scholarship. It is not a legal ruling but a bibliographic survey that details manuscripts of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, including the famous Majma' al-Bahrayn and its super-commentary Multaqa al-Nayrayn. Understanding this passage equips you to navigate Hanafi primary sources and appreciate the chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chapter and its purpose
Read the title 'Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. This signals that the passage is a survey of works that comment on the foundational Hanafi matn by al-Quduri.
2
Parse the manuscript description and ijazah
Locate the description of the author's manuscript copy (in his handwriting, endowed at Sultan Muhammad al-Fatih mosque) and the ijazah (permission to narrate) granted to Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi. Note the terms: what is permitted and the author's concern for accuracy.
The author wrote on the copy: 'it is correct and agrees, and Allah forgives what the pen has slipped...'
3
Note the author's super-commentary
Find where the passage mentions that the author himself wrote a super-commentary on his own work: 'وقد شرح المؤلف نفسه مجمع البحرين في مجلدين كبيرين سماه : (ملتقى النيرين)'. Understand that this shows a multi-layered commentarial tradition.
4
Recognize the listed commentaries
The passage ends with two commentaries: number 41 by Ibn al-Muhaddith (incomplete) and number 42 by al-Khalkhali. Note their status: one is lost, the other exists in manuscript.

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
منه نسخة بخط المؤلف، موقوفة بجامع السلطان محمد الفاتح، وقد ضرب في بعض مواضعه، وكشط، وفرغ من تأليفه سنة ٦٩٠هـ. وهو كتاب حفظه سهل؛ لنهاية إيجازه، حَلُه صَعْب؛ لغاية إعجازه، بحر مسائله، جم فضائله ...».
كما توجد نسخة نفيسة من مجمع البحرين، نقلت عن نسخة المؤلف، ثم كتب عليها مؤلفه بخطه : قوبلت هذه النسخة، وكتبت من أصلي، فصحت ووافقت، والله يعفو عما طغى به القلم، أو تجاوز عنه النظر.
وقد أجزتُ لمالكها الشيخ الإمام العالم الفاضل، والورع الكامل، ذي الأخلاق الكريمة، والفضائل الجسيمة، ركن الدين السمرقندي، أدام الله حراسته، وكتب سلامته، أن يرويها عني. وكذلك أجزتُ له رواية الشرح الذي صنفته بعد، إذا وقعت له نسخة يثق إلى صحتها، وكذلك جميع ما يصح عنده أنه من مقولاتي، أو منقولاتي، أو مسموعاتي، أو مستجازاتي، فهو أدام الله أيامه يُجمل ما يرويه، وأنا معتمد على الله تعالى، ثم ملتمس من خدمته أن يصون هذا الكتاب، ويحفظه عن تغيير يقع فيه ...». اهـ من الجواهر المضية.
وهو كتاب مطبوع بدار الكتب العلمية، بتحقيق إلياس قبلان. * وقد شرح المؤلف نفسه مجمع البحرين في مجلدين كبيرين سماه : (ملتقى النيرين) مخطوط، بعد، ومنه أيضاً نسخ عديدة في تركيا وغيرها، ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل.
وقد حقق شرح المؤلف في ثلاث رسائل للدكتوراه، في المعهد العالي للقضاء في الرياض، ولكن لم يطبع بعد.
٤١۔ شرح مختصر القدوري .
لإبراهيم بن عبد الرزاق بن خلف الرَّسعَني، المعروف بابن المحدث، المتوفى بدمشق سنة ٦٩٥هـ ، وفي بعض نسخ تاج التراجم : توفي سنة ٦٧٥هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد توفي المؤلف رحمه الله ولم يتم شرحه، كما ذكر مترجموه، ولم أقف على شيء من نُسخه.
٤٢- شرح مختصر القدوري.

ذكره بهذه المعلومات الزبيدي في تاج العروس، وأنه شرح.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Among them is a copy in the author's handwriting, endowed at the Sultan Muhammad al-Fatih Mosque, and it has been struck through in some places and scraped, and completed in the year 690 AH. It is a book easy to memorize due to its extreme conciseness, but difficult to understand due to its extreme brevity, a sea of issues, a collection of virtues... There is also a precious copy of Majma' al-Bahrayn, copied from the author's copy, then the author wrote on it in his own handwriting: 'This copy was collated and written from my original, so it is correct and agrees, and Allah forgives what the pen has slipped or the eye has overlooked.' And I have granted permission to its owner, the scholar, the Imam, the virtuous, the complete abstinent, of noble character and great virtues, Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi, may Allah preserve him and write safety for him, to narrate it from me. Likewise, I have granted him permission to narrate the commentary I authored afterward, if he obtains a copy whose authenticity he trusts, and likewise all that is correct in his view from my sayings, narrations, hearings, or permissions. He, may his days endure, summarizes what he narrates, and I rely on Allah, then I request from his service that he protect this book and guard it against any alteration that may occur...' End quote from al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah. It is a book published by Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah, edited by Ilyas Qablan. The author himself commented on Majma' al-Bahrayn in two large volumes, naming it Multaqa al-Nayrayn, still in manuscript, and there are also many copies in Turkey and elsewhere, see al-Fihris al-Shamil. The author's commentary has been studied in three doctoral theses at the Higher Judicial Institute in Riyadh, but has not yet been printed. 41. Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Razzaq ibn Khalaf al-Ras'ani, known as Ibn al-Muhaddith, died in Damascus in 695 AH, and in some copies of Taj al-Tarajim: died in 675 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The author died before completing his commentary, as his biographers mention, and I have not come across any copy of it. 42. Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Khalkhali Muwaffaq al-Din Yusuf, Imam of the Khanqah al-Samisatiyya al-Khalkhali, died in 709 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Zabidi mentioned him with this information in Taj al-Arus, and that he commented.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic section from Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri. It introduces the third chapter, which surveys commentaries on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. The text begins by describing a manuscript of a commentary (likely Majma' al-Bahrayn) in the author's handwriting, noting its location and condition. It then presents an ijazah (permission to narrate) granted by the author to Rukn al-Din al-Samarqandi, detailing the terms of transmission. The passage mentions a published edition and the author's own super-commentary ('Multaqa al-Nayrayn') on his earlier work. Finally, it lists two specific commentaries: number 41 by Ibn al-Muhaddith (incomplete) and number 42 by al-Khalkhali, providing brief biographical details. The section serves to document the scholarly legacy and transmission of the Hanafi matn.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal text by Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi matn.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary that expands and explains a matn, here referring to works based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مجمع البحرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, mentioned as having a precious manuscript.
ملتقى النيرين (Multaqa al-Nayrayn): The author's own commentary on his earlier work Majma' al-Bahrayn, in two volumes.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Commentarial Tradition on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Bio-bibliographical listing of four sharh works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain their authors and significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a core Hanafi text that inspired generations of commentators.

This passage lists four commentaries on the foundational Hanafi fiqh text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. While it does not contain legal rulings, it illustrates the scholarly tradition of sharh (commentary) that has preserved and transmitted Hanafi fiqh across centuries. Understanding these authors and their works helps you appreciate the depth of the madhhab's textual heritage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the matn (core text) being commented upon. All listed works are sharh (commentaries) on this same matn.
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) is a standard introductory Hanafi fiqh text.
2
List each commentator and his death date
For each entry (41-44), note the commentator's name and year of death. This helps place them chronologically and understand the chain of transmission.
Death dates: Ibn al-Muhaddith (695 or 675 AH), al-Khalkhali (709 AH), al-Saruji (710 AH), al-Nasafi (710 AH).
3
Note the status of each commentary
Determine whether the commentary was completed (al-Khalkhali, al-Saruji, al-Nasafi) or incomplete (Ibn al-Muhaddith), and note its reported size (e.g., al-Saruji's in fifty parts).
Incomplete commentaries indicate the author's death before completion; size estimates give a sense of scholarly depth.
4
Recognize the scholarly chain
The passage mentions sources (e.g., al-Zubaydi, al-Ayni) that transmit knowledge of these commentators. This shows how later scholars preserved and transmitted knowledge about earlier works.
This chain of bio-bibliographical information is itself part of the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

الفصل الثالث : شروح القدوري
وهو كتاب مطبوع بدار الكتب العلمية، بتحقيق إلياس قبلان. وقد شرح المؤلف نفسه مجمع البحرين في مجلدين كبيرين سماه : (ملتقى النيرين) مخطوط ، ومنه أيضاً نسخ عديدة في تركيا وغيرها. وقد حقق شرح المؤلف في ثلاث رسائل للدكتوراه، في المعهد العالي للقضاء في الرياض، ولكن لم يطبع بعد.
٤١- شرح مختصر القدوري .
لإبراهيم بن عبد الرزاق بن خلف الرَّسعَني، المعروف بابن المحدث، المتوفى بدمشق سنة ٦٩٥هـ ، وفي بعض نسخ تاج التراجم : توفي سنة ٦٧٥هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. وقد توفي المؤلف رحمه الله ولم يتم شرحه، كما ذكر مترجموه، ولم أقف على شيء من نُسخه.
٤٢- شرح مختصر القدوري.
للخَلْخَالي موفق الدين يوسف إمام الخانقاه السميساطيَّة الخَلْخَالي، المتوفى سنة ٧٠٩هـ، رحمه الله تعالى. ذكره بهذه المعلومات الزبيدي في تاج العروس، وأنه شرح القدوري، وذكر أنه ترجمه الإمام العيني في طبقات الحنفية، وشيخ مشايخنا. وقد ذكر الخلخالي هذا بدون أي معلومة عنه القرشي في الجواهر المضية، والعلامة قاسم في تاج التراجم.
٤٣- شرح مختصر القدوري
للإمام السروجي أحمد بن إبراهيم بن عبد الغني، قاضي القضاة بمصر، المتوفى سنة ٧١٠هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى. ذكره له الكَفَوِيُّ في كتائب أعلام الأخيار (مخطوط)، كما نقل هذا عنه محقق الجواهر المضية، وذكر الكفوي أنه رأى على هامش نسخة من الجواهر، أنه في خمسين جزءاً. اهـ
قلت : والجزء يعادل (٢٠) ورقة، فيكون حجم هذا الشرح في ألف ورقة، والله أعلم.
٤٤- الوافي .
للإمام الكبير أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي، المتوفى سنة ٧١٠هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى.
Chapter Three: Commentaries of al-Quduri. It is a book printed by Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah, edited by Ilyas Qablan. The author himself explained Majma' al-Bahrayn in two large volumes which he called (Multeqa al-Nirayn) manuscript, and there are also many copies in Turkey and elsewhere. And the author's commentary has been investigated in three doctoral dissertations at the Higher Institute of the Judiciary in Riyadh, but it has not yet been printed. 41- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Razzaq ibn Khalaf al-Ras'ani, known as Ibn al-Muhaddith, who died in Damascus in 695 AH, and in some copies of Taj al-Tarajim: he died in 675 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. The author died without completing his commentary, as his biographers mentioned, and I did not find any copy of it. 42- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By al-Khalkhali Muwaffaq al-Din Yusuf, Imam of the Khanqah al-Samisatiyya al-Khalkhali, who died in 709 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Zubaydi mentioned him with this information in Taj al-Urus, and that he commented on al-Quduri, and he mentioned that Imam al-Ayni translated him in Tabaqat al-Hanafiyyah, and the shaykh of our shaykhs. And al-Qurashi mentioned this al-Khalkhali in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah without any information about him, and also Allamah Qasim in Taj al-Tarajim. 43- Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Imam al-Saruji Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Ghani, Chief Judge in Egypt, who died in 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Kafawi mentioned him in Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar (manuscript), as the editor of al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah transmitted from him, and al-Kafawi said that he saw on the margin of a copy of al-Jawahir that it was in fifty parts. End. I say: And the part equals (20) folios, so the size of this commentary is a thousand folios, and Allah knows best. 44- Al-Wafi. By the great Imam Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi, who died in 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section listing four commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri. The section begins by noting that the book is published and that the author of this work (the commentator on al-Quduri) also wrote a commentary on Majma' al-Bahrayn. Then it enumerates commentaries numbered 41-44: (41) A commentary by Ibn al-Muhaddith (d. 695 or 675 AH), which remained incomplete; (42) A commentary by al-Khalkhali (d. 709 AH), mentioned by al-Zubaydi; (43) A commentary by al-Saruji (d. 710 AH), reported to be in fifty parts; (44) Al-Wafi by al-Nasafi (d. 710 AH). This list is typical of Hanafi bibliographical works, providing death dates and brief notes on the authors and the status of their works. The text shows the scholarly interest in expounding al-Quduri's Mukhtasar across generations.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely commented upon.
شرح (Sharh): A commentary or exposition on a base text (matn).
الوافي (Al-Wafi): A commentary by al-Nasafi, one of the works listed.
جزء (Juz' (pl. ajza')): A part or volume of a book; here each juz' is approximately 20 folios.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Commentary by al-Khalkhali
C) Commentary by al-Saruji
D) Al-Wafi by al-Nasafi

Key Takeaway
The Mukhtasar al-Quduri has been extensively commented upon by many scholars; this list shows just a few examples of the rich commentarial tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction to Al-Wafi: A Multi-Source Compendium of Hanafi Fiqh
Preface describing the compilation and notation of Al-Wafi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five main sources compiled in al-Wafi and explain the notation system used to attribute opinions to different scholars.

Core Idea
Al-Wafi combines five core Hanafi texts into one, using single-letter abbreviations to indicate the preferred opinion of each leading imam.

This passage introduces al-Wafi, a comprehensive Hanafi fiqh compendium authored by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi. It is not a fiqh ruling itself, but a front matter that explains the book's structure, sources, and a unique notation system. Understanding this system is essential for using the text to find relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five source texts compiled in al-Wafi
Look for the names of the texts mentioned: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat.
Each of these is a major work in the Hanafi tradition.
2
Recognise the notation abbreviations for each imam
The passage lists single-letter codes: ح for Abu Hanifa, س for Abu Yusuf, م for Muhammad, ز for Zufar, ف for al-Shafi'i, ك for Malik, and و for a transmission or weak analogy.
These abbreviations allow the author to note different opinions without lengthy discussion.
3
Understand the purpose of omitting explicit disputes
Al-Nasafi states he included only what is relied upon and used abbreviations to avoid prolixity. The goal is a concise, practical reference.
The notation system implicitly indicates the preferred view.
4
Compare al-Wafi with Ibn al-Sa'ati's Majma' al-Bahrayn
The passage notes a similar contemporary work that also combined al-Quduri and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat but omitted the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
This comparison highlights al-Wafi's comprehensiveness.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
وهو متن لطيف معتبر في فروع الحنفية، جمع فيه مؤلفه بين مختصر القدوري، والجامعين الكبير والصغير، والزيادات لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، وأضاف إليها منظومة النسفي «نظم الخلافيات»، للنسفي نجم الدين عمر بن محمد، المتوفى سنة ٥٣٥ هـ، صاحب طلبة الطلبة، والتفسير ، وهذا النظم يقع في (٢٦٦٩) بيتاً، وأضاف إلى ذلك مسائل وواقعات أخرى.
وللكتاب نسخ عديدة ينظر لها الفهرس الشامل.
(۲)
وقد جاء في مقدمة الوافي:
«الحمد لله من من على عباده وعباده بإرسال رسله، وهدايــة سبله، والصلاة والسلام على سيد الخلائق، محمد المخصوص بأفضل الخلائق.
قال العبد الضعيف الفقير إلى الله الودود أبو البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي غفر الله له ولوالديه ، وأحسن إليهما وإليه : قد كان يخطر ببالي إيَّان فراغي أن أؤلف كتاباً جامعاً لمسائل الجامعين والزيادات، حاوياً لما في المختصر، ونظم الخلافيات،
مشتملاً على بعض مسائل الفتاوى والواقعات.
وكنت أتوانى في هذا الأمر الأمر إلى أن ترادفت الخواطر، وتوالت الخُطَّاب، وتوفّرت الدواعي، وازدحمت الطلاب، وانضم إليه التماس مَن حَرُم عليَّ ردُّه ، لوُفُور نصيبه في المنقول والمعقول، وكمال نصاب في الفروع والأصول، وذكاء فهمه، وصفاء قريحته، وخلاص نيته، ونصوع طويته.
فشرعت فيه بتوفيق الله وتيسيره، وأتممته في أسرع مدة، بعونه وتقديره، وسميتُه : «الوافي»، ولو وفُقت لشرحه لأوسمته بـ:
«الكافي». ولقد أوردت في هذا الكتاب ما هو المعول عليه في الباب،
وطويت ذكر الاختلافات، واكتفيت بالعلامات.
فالحاءُ: علامة لأبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه، والسين: لأبي يوسف رحمه الله ، والميم لمحمد رحمه الله والزاي: لزفر رحمه الله ، والفاء : للشافعي رحمه الله والكاف: لمالك رحمه الله.
والواو : رواية عن أصحابنا رحمهم الله، أو قياس مرجوح؛ تحامياً عن الإطناب، وتفادياً عن الإسهاب، وهو ولي التوفيق». اهـ مـن مقدمة الوافي. وعمل النسفي هذا في «الوافي»، يشبه كثيراً عمل عـصـريـه ابـن الساعاتي، (ت ٦٩٤هـ) في كتابه : (مجمع البحرين وملتقى النهرين)، الذي جمع فيه بين القدوري ومنظومة النسفي، لكن دون كتب محمد بن الحسن الجامعين والزيادات
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It is a refined and authoritative text on Hanafi jurisprudence, in which its author combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, and added to them the poetic work of al-Nasafi 'Nazm al-Khilafiyyat' by al-Nasafi Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad, died 535 AH, author of Talbat al-Talaba and the Tafsir. This poem consists of 2669 verses, and he added to it other issues and occurrences. The book has many copies; see al-Fihris al-Shamil. (2) And it is mentioned in the introduction of al-Wafi: 'Praise be to Allah who has bestowed favors upon His servants by sending His messengers and guiding His paths. Blessings and peace be upon the master of creation, Muhammad, distinguished by the best of character.' The weak servant in need of the Loving Allah, Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi, may Allah forgive him and his parents and be gracious to them and him, said: 'It had occurred to me at the time of my leisure to author a comprehensive book encompassing the issues of al-Jami'ayn and al-Ziyadat, containing what is in al-Mukhtasar and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat, including some issues from fatawa and real events. I hesitated in this matter until thoughts multiplied, requests followed, incentives increased, students crowded, and the request of one whom I could not refuse joined, due to his abundant share in transmitted and rational knowledge, his complete mastery in subsidiary and fundamental matters, his sharp intellect, pure nature, sincere intention, and clear conscience. So I began it with Allah's success and facilitation, and completed it in the shortest time with His help and decree, and I named it 'al-Wafi', and if I were successful in explaining it I would have titled it 'al-Kafi'. I have included in this book what is relied upon in the subject, and I have omitted mentioning differences, being satisfied with indicators. So: ح is a sign for Abu Hanifa (RA), س for Abu Yusuf (RA), م for Muhammad (RA), ز for Zufar (RA), ف for al-Shafi'i (RA), ك for Malik (RA). And و is for a transmission from our companions (RA) or a weak analogy; avoiding prolixity and escaping verbosity. He is the granter of success.' End of the introduction of al-Wafi. Al-Nasafi's work in 'al-Wafi' greatly resembles the work of his contemporary Ibn al-Sa'ati (d. 694 AH) in his book 'Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn', who combined al-Quduri and al-Nasafi's poem, but without the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, al-Jami'ayn and al-Ziyadat.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a front matter from the chapter on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, introducing the book al-Wafi by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi. It describes al-Wafi as a compilation that brings together five key Hanafi texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, and Nazm al-Khilafiyyat by Najm al-Din al-Nasafi. The author explains his motivation and the request of a distinguished student. He adopted a system of abbreviations using single letters to denote different jurists: ح for Abu Hanifa, س for Abu Yusuf, م for Muhammad, ز for Zufar, ف for al-Shafi'i, ك for Malik, and و for a transmission from the Hanafis or a weak analogy. This notation allowed him to present relied-upon views without lengthy discussions of ikhtilaf. The passage also notes the similarity to Ibn al-Sa'ati's 'Majma' al-Bahrayn', but without the works of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. This introduction is important for understanding the methodology and structure of al-Wafi, a significant intermediate text in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
الحاء (al-Ḥā’): Abbreviation used in al-Wafi to indicate the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa.
السين (as-Sīn): Abbreviation for Imam Abu Yusuf’s opinion.
الميم (al-Mīm): Abbreviation for Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani’s opinion.
الزاي (az-Zāy): Abbreviation for Imam Zufar’s opinion.
الفاء (al-Fā’): Abbreviation for Imam al-Shafi'i’s opinion.
الكاف (al-Kāf): Abbreviation for Imam Malik’s opinion.
الواو (al-Wāw): Abbreviation for a transmission from the Hanafi companions (riwaya) or a weak analogy (qiyas marjuh).
الوافي (al-Wāfī): The title of the book authored by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, meaning 'The Comprehensive'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) الميم
D) الفاء

Key Takeaway
Al-Wafi is a comprehensive Hanafi fiqh text compiled from five core sources, using letter abbreviations to indicate the preferred opinion of each major imam.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Al-Nasafi's Wafi, Kafi, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq: Structure and Symbol System
Introduction to al-Nasafi's three works and symbol system

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three key works of al-Nasafi, describe their interrelationship, and recall the symbol system used in al-Wafi for different Hanafi and non-Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Al-Nasafi's three works form a hierarchy: al-Wafi (concise, symbols for views), al-Kafi (commentary with proofs), Kanz al-Daqa'iq (further abridgment for easy reference).

In this lesson, we explore the textual landscape of Hanafi fiqh through the lens of al-Nasafi's contributions. You will learn how he combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri with the Zahir al-Riwayah works of Imam Muhammad, suppressed disagreements by using symbols, and later produced a self-commentary and an abridgment. Understanding these texts is crucial for navigating later Hanafi scholarship and fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of al-Wafi
Al-Nasafi's al-Wafi combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Jami'ayn (al-Kabir wa al-Saghir), al-Ziyadat of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and his own poetic summary (Manzuma). Recognize that these are core Hanafi sources, the first two from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the most authoritative category in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the symbol system
Al-Nasafi uses single Arabic letters to indicate which imam's opinion is being stated: ح for Abu Hanifa, س for Abu Yusuf, م for Muhammad, ز for Zufar, ف for al-Shafi'i, ك for Malik, و for a narration or outweighed analogy. This allows concise presentation while noting ikhtilaf.
The symbol و typically represents a rarer or weaker view.
3
Trace the evolution to al-Kafi and Kanz al-Daqa'iq
Al-Nasafi wrote al-Kafi as a commentary on his own al-Wafi, fulfilling his earlier wish; it includes proofs. Later, he abridged al-Wafi into Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a concise matn that became highly popular and widely commented upon.
Kanz al-Daqa'iq is considered a very reliable matn for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مشتملاً على بعض مسائل الفتاوى والواقعات.
وكنت أتوانى في هذا الأمر الأمر إلى أن ترادفت الخواطر، وتوالت الخُطَّاب، وتوفّرت الدواعي، وازدحمت الطلاب، وانضم إليه التماس مَن حَرُم عليَّ ردُّه ، لوُفُور نصيبه في المنقول والمعقول، وكمال نصاب في الفروع والأصول، وذكاء فهمه، وصفاء قريحته، وخلاص نيته، ونصوع طويته.
فشرعت فيه بتوفيق الله وتيسيره، وأتممته في أسرع مدة، بعونه وتقديره، وسميتُه : «الوافي»، ولو وفُقت لشرحه لأوسمته بـ: «الكافي». ولقد أوردت في هذا الكتاب ما هو المعول عليه في الباب، وطويت ذكر الاختلافات، واكتفيت بالعلامات.

ثم إن النسفي من (نَسَفَ)، بلدة عظيمة في بلاد بخارى، وابن الساعاتي بغدادي ثم بعلبكي.
٤٥ـ الكافي شرح الوافي .
للنسفي أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد المتوفى سنة ٧١٠هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وهو شرح لمؤلف الوافي نفسه، فقد قال في مقدمة الوافي: «ولو وفقت لشرحه لأوسمته بـ: الكافي. اهـ
وقد وفقه الله تعالى لما رجاه، وألف كتاب: «الكافي»، وفيه أدلة، بخلاف الوافي.
٤٦ - كنز الدقائق .
للإمام أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود النسفي، المتوفى سنة ٧١٠ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وقد اختصره النسفي من كتابه: «الوافي»، الذي جمع فيه بين مختصر القدوري، والجامعين الكبير والصغير والزيادات لمحمد بن الحسن، ومنظومة النسفي.
وكنز الدقائق متن متين معتبر جداً عند الحنفية، ومتداول بينهم، وعليه شروح عديدة.

... لما رأيتُ الهمم مائلة إلى المختصرات، والطباع راغبةً عن المطولات، أردت أن ألخص الوافي»، بذكر ما عم وقوعه،
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Including some issues of fatwas and occurrences. And I hesitated in this matter until thoughts followed one another, and seekers came successively, and motives multiplied, and students crowded, and joined to that the request of one whose rejection is forbidden to me, due to the abundance of his share in transmitted and rational knowledge, and the perfection of his capacity in furu' and usul, and the sharpness of his understanding, the clarity of his mind, the sincerity of his intention, and the purity of his inner self. So I began it with the success of Allah and His facilitation, and I completed it in the shortest time with His help and decree, and I named it 'al-Wafi', and if I were successful in explaining it I would have marked it with 'al-Kafi'. And I have included in this book what is relied upon in the chapter, and I suppressed the mention of differences, and sufficed with symbols. So al-Ha' is a symbol for Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), and al-Sin for Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), and al-Mim for Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), and al-Zay for Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him), and al-Fa for al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and al-Kaf for Malik (may Allah have mercy on him). And al-Waw is a narration from our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) or a outweighed analogy; avoiding prolixity and escaping verbosity, and He is the Grantor of success. End from the introduction of al-Wafi. And this work of al-Nasafi in 'al-Wafi' greatly resembles the work of his contemporary Ibn al-Sa'ati (d. 694 AH) in his book 'Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn', which he compiled between al-Quduri and the versification of al-Nasafi, but without the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan: al-Jami'ayn and al-Ziyadat. Then al-Nasafi is from Nasaf, a great city in the land of Bukhara, and Ibn al-Sa'ati is Baghdadi then Ba'labakki. 45 - al-Kafi: Commentary on al-Wafi. By al-Nasafi, Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad, died 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It is a commentary by the author of al-Wafi himself, for he said in the introduction of al-Wafi: 'And if I were successful in explaining it I would have marked it with al-Kafi.' End. And Allah facilitated for him what he hoped, and he authored the book 'al-Kafi', and it contains proofs, unlike al-Wafi. 46 - Kanz al-Daqa'iq. By Imam Abu al-Barakat Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Nasafi, died 710 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And al-Nasafi abridged it from his book 'al-Wafi', which he compiled between Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and al-Jami'ayn al-Kabir wa al-Saghir and al-Ziyadat of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and the versification of al-Nasafi. And Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a solid and very reliable matn among the Hanafis, widely circulated among them, and there are numerous commentaries on it. And it came in the introduction of its author: '... When I saw that ambitions incline toward abridgments, and natures are averse to lengthy works, I wanted to summarize al-Wafi, mentioning what commonly occurs...'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, presenting the third chapter which lists commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It begins with a quotation from the introduction of al-Nasafi's work 'al-Wafi'. In this introduction, al-Nasafi explains his motivation and method: he compiled the book due to the urging of a respected individual, included only relied-upon rulings, and used symbols instead of lengthy discussions of differing opinions. He outlines the symbols: ح for Abu Hanifa, س for Abu Yusuf, م for Muhammad, ز for Zufar, ف for al-Shafi'i, ك for Malik, and و for a narration from the Hanafi companions or a outweighed analogy (qiyas marjuh). Then the commentator notes that al-Nasafi's work resembles that of his contemporary Ibn al-Sa'ati, who authored 'Majma' al-Bahrayn', but al-Nasafi included the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (al-Jami'ayn and al-Ziyadat) while Ibn al-Sa'ati did not. A brief biographical note follows: al-Nasafi is from Nasaf in Bukhara, and Ibn al-Sa'ati is from Baghdad and later Ba'labakk. Next, the passage lists 'al-Kafi', which is al-Nasafi's own commentary on his work al-Wafi, fulfilling his earlier wish. Unlike al-Wafi, al-Kafi includes proofs (adillah). Finally, 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq' is introduced as an abridgment of al-Wafi by the same author. It is a highly regarded matn among Hanafis, widely studied, and many commentaries have been written upon it. The author's preface explains that he abridged al-Wafi because people prefer concise works. This passage is important for understanding the structure and reliability of these three key texts in the Hanafi tradition: al-Wafi (a concise compendium without proofs), al-Kafi (a commentary with proofs), and Kanz al-Daqa'iq (a further abridgment).

Key Terms
الوافي (al-Wāfī): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Nasafi combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri with other sources, using symbols for different imams and suppressing disagreements.
الكافي (al-Kāfī): Al-Nasafi's own commentary on al-Wafi, including proofs (adillah), unlike al-Wafi which omits them.
كنز الدقائق (Kanz al-Daqā’iq): A concise Hanafi fiqh matn abridged by al-Nasafi from his own al-Wafi, widely relied upon and commented upon.
الجامعين (الكبير والصغير) (al-Jāmi'ayn (al-Kabīr wa al-Ṣaghīr)): Two of the six authoritative books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani comprising the Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الزيادات (al-Ziyādāt): Another of the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani within the Zahir al-Riwayah, additional to al-Jami'ayn.
منظومة النسفي (Manẓūmat al-Nasafī): A versification of Hanafi rulings by al-Nasafi, incorporated into al-Wafi alongside Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Wafi
B) Al-Kafi
C) Kanz al-Daqa'iq
D) Majma' al-Bahrayn

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi's three works—al-Wafi, al-Kafi, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq—form a progressive hierarchy from concise compendium to detailed commentary to popular abridgment, with a unique symbol system denoting the preferred imams' views.

Nazm Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Poetic Version
Biographical entry on a nazm of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a nazm (poetic versification) of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and state its author and approximate date.

Core Idea
Poetic versions of legal texts helped memorization and transmission.

This passage comes from a biographical dictionary listing works based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi matn. The entry describes a nazm (poetic arrangement) composed by Fakhr al-Din al-Duruki in the 8th century AH. Such versifications were common in Islamic scholarship to aid memorization, and this one is noted for its eloquence and comprehensiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work type
The passage begins by naming the work: 'Nazm Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. 'Nazm' means a poetic arrangement. So this is a versification of the prose text.
2
Identify the author and his background
The author is Fakhr al-Din Muhammad ibn Mustafa al-Duruki. His multiple nisbas indicate his origin: al-Duruki (from Duruk?), al-Salghari, al-Siwasi al-Rumi, then al-Qahiri – he moved to Cairo. He died in 713 AH/1313 CE.
3
Note the reception and current availability
Al-Qurashi praises the nazm as eloquent, easy, and comprehensive. However, the author of this biographical entry says he has not found any copies – meaning the text is not widely preserved.

Biographical listing of a commentary author

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A commentary on a foundational Hanafi text is a link in the chain of transmission and explanation.

This passage presents a biographical note on Siraj al-Din al-Hamili, the author of a sharh (commentary) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a core Hanafi fiqh text. Understanding the authors of commentaries helps us trace the development of Hanafi scholarship and the transmission of authoritative rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Read the passage to find the commentator's full name: Siraj al-Din Abu Bakr ibn Ali ibn Musa al-Hamili al-Yamani.

Note the death date
The death date is 769 AH. This places the author in the 14th century CE, well after the founding Imams.
Later commentators expand and clarify earlier matn texts.
3
Recognize the base text
The commentary is on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is one of the earliest and most authoritative matn in the school.
4
Understand the sharh's function
A sharh explains difficult passages, provides evidence, and sometimes resolves disputes. Al-Hamili's work is an expansion and clarification of the original matn.

Listing a comprehensive Hanafi work combining multiple sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three sources that al-Minhaj combines and state the biographical discrepancy concerning its author.

Core Idea
Al-Minhaj condenses three foundational Hanafi texts into one accessible compendium.

This lesson introduces a valuable Hanafi work that compiles rulings from multiple authoritative sources in a concise format. Understanding the structure and provenance of such compendia is essential for navigating the Hanafi tradition efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
Read the passage to determine the title of the work and the name of its author, along with his death date as given by Kashf al-Zunun.
2
List the three sources it combines
Note the three Hanafi texts that al-Minhaj synthesizes: al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, a work by al-Tahawi, and the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri.
3
Locate the biographical discrepancy
Compare the dates given by Kashf al-Zunun (734 AH) and Hadiyyat al-'Arifin (660 AH) and note the different attribution of the author's father.
4
Understand the commentator's resolution
The commentator advises that further investigation is needed to resolve the discrepancy; the student should be aware of this irresolution.

وهو مشتمل على أصول وفروع ، جمع فيـه بـيـن الجامع الصغير لمحمد بن الحسن، وبين تصنيف الطحاوي، والقدوري، بأوجز لفظ، وأوضح بيان كما وصفه بذلك صاحب كشف الظنون (۱).

51 - Al-Minhaj 'ala Madhhab al-Hanafiyya. By Qadi Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn al-'Adim al-Halabi, died 734 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It contains principles and branches, combining between al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and the work of al-Tahawi, and al-Quduri, in the briefest wording and clearest expression, as described by the author of Kashf al-Zunun. As for the author of Hadiyyat al-'Arifin, he named it 'Minhaj fi al-Usul wa al-Furu' 'ala Madhhab Abi Hanifa' and attributed it to Ibn al-'Adim Umar ibn al-Qadi Majd al-Din Ahmad ibn Hibbat Allah, born 586 AH and died 660 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Based on this, one should determine which author is correct.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage presents a complex biographical entry for al-Minhaj, a work synthesizing three major Hanafi texts: Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Tahawi's Mukhtasar, and al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author notes a discrepancy: the death date given by Kashf al-Zunun (734 AH) conflicts with the date given by Hadiyyat al-'Arifin (660 AH) and a different attribution of the author's father. The commentator advises that further investigation is needed to resolve the discrepancy.

Key Terms

تصنيف الطحاوي (Tasnif al-Tahawi): Mukhtasar al-Tahawi or another work by al-Tahawi, a Hanafi scholar.
المختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by al-Quduri.

Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: A Reliable Hanafi Commentary
Describing the commentary and refuting criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the purpose, features, and reliability of Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and evaluate the critique leveled against it.

Core Idea
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a comprehensive Hanafi commentary that clarifies al-Quduri with evidence and examples, despite Birgili's baseless criticism.

This lesson introduces you to 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj', a key commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage from the editor's introduction describes the book's purpose and features, and then addresses a historical criticism of its reliability. Understanding how to evaluate such sources is vital for any student of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its author
Recognize that Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by an unnamed author (died 800 AH). Note that different manuscript copies vary in volume count (three, four, or eight volumes).
The author's name is not given in this excerpt, but the commentary is well-known.
2
Understand the author’s purpose
Read the author's preface: he wrote the book to clarify problematic points and difficulties in Mukhtasar al-Quduri, aiming for a moderate length between brevity and prolixity, with concise expressions and beneficial meanings.
The author named it 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' (The Blazing Lamp).
3
Note the commentary’s features
The editor praises the commentary for its focus on evidences (adillah), moderate discussions, abundant examples, inclusion of many branches (furu') not found in the original, and mention of differences among the four Sunni schools.
These features make it a valuable resource for understanding Hanafi fiqh in depth.
4
Evaluate the criticism of unreliability
Birgili (Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Rumi) apparently considered the book weak and unreliable. The editor points out that Birgili was a scholar of Arabic, not necessarily an authoritative Hanafi jurist, and that al-Laknawi repeated the claim without critique. This suggests the criticism is unfounded.
The editor's analysis encourages critical evaluation of such claims based on the actual content and scholarly reception of the work.

The Third Chapter: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Died in the year 800 AH. May Allah have mercy on him.
433
Al-Allamah Qasim mentioned that it is in eight volumes, and that its abridgement by its author, 'Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira', is in four volumes.
As for the author of Kashf al-Zunun, he mentioned that it is in three volumes, and thus each describes the copy he came across.
The book has numerous copies. The number of folios of the Azhar copy reached 3871 folios. There are also copies of the book in the Mahmudiyya Library in Medina under numbers 1036 and 1286.
* The author's introduction states:
'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad, the master of the messengers, and upon all the prophets of Allah and His angels, and may Allah be pleased with the Companions and the Followers.
This is a book I authored as a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, clarifying its problematic points, elucidating its difficulties, moderate between brevity and prolixity, balanced between elaboration and conciseness. I compiled it with concise expressions and beneficial meanings, easy in derivation and benefit, close in meaning and utility. I clarified it for every needy student and named it 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. I sought help in that from the Most Merciful, the Most Compassionate. My success is only from Allah; upon Him I rely, and He is the Lord of the Mighty Throne. Glory be to You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us. Indeed, You are the All-Knowing, the All-Wise.' End.
It is a magnificent and great commentary, concerned with mentioning evidences, with discussions that are not lengthy, and it frequently mentions examples for issues that clarify them, remove confusion about them, and make them pictured in the mind of the reader with many branches that the author added to the original he commented on. It also mentions the differences among the four schools.
6
Discussion of what was said about the unreliability of 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj':
(1). The author of Kashf al-Zunun quoted from the master known as Birgili that he counted the book 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' among the commonly circulated weak and unreliable books.
Al-Allamah al-Laknawi followed him in that without any critique.
I say: The one from whom this judgment about 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' is quoted is Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Rumi, known as Birgili, died in 981 AH. Al-Zirikli translated his biography and described him as a scholar of Arabic. He is the author of the book...
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from the editor's introduction to 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' discusses the commentary 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. The passage first provides bibliographical details: different scholars gave varying numbers of volumes for the commentary, reflecting different manuscript copies. The author's introduction is then quoted, in which he states his purpose: to write a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri that is moderate in length, clear, and beneficial. He named it 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' (The Blazing Lamp). The editor praises the commentary as magnificent, noting its focus on evidences (adillah), moderate discussions, abundant examples, and inclusion of many branches (furu') not found in the original work. Importantly, it also mentions the differences among the four Sunni schools. The passage then addresses a criticism: the famous Ottoman scholar Birgili (Imam Birgivi) allegedly considered this book weak and unreliable. The editor notes that al-Laknawi repeated this without critique, but then identifies Birgili as Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Rumi (d. 981 AH), a respected Arabic scholar. The editor implies that this criticism may be unfounded, as Birgili's own works are not necessarily authoritative in Hanafi fiqh. The commentary 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' remains a valuable resource for students of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
السراج الوهاج (Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, known for its moderate length, evidence-based approach, and inclusion of examples and branches.
بركلي / بركوي (Birgili / Birgivi): Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Rumi (d. 981 AH), an Ottoman scholar of Arabic, known for his work on beliefs and Arabic grammar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To clarify problematic points and difficulties in Mukhtasar al-Quduri with moderate length
C) To critique the four schools of law

Key Takeaway
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a valuable Hanafi commentary that should not be dismissed based on isolated criticism; its features make it a reliable source for understanding Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Authority and Utility of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
Describing a commentary's authority and features.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the importance of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah in the Hanafi tradition and identify its relationship to Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
A commentary's authority is established by its acceptance among later jurists, not merely by the absence of weak reports.

Not every commentary on a foundational Hanafi matn carries equal weight. Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by Abu Bakr al-Haddad has earned its place as a standard reference despite containing some weak narrations. This lesson explores how the Hanafi tradition evaluates and relies on such texts, and why this commentary is especially valued for teaching Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Book and Author
First, note that the text describes Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu Bakr al-Haddad (d. 800 AH). He also wrote a larger commentary, Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, from which this was abridged.
The author's death date places him in the later Hanafi tradition, which is important for understanding his authority.
2
Understand the Author's Purpose
From the introduction, al-Haddad states he compiled the commentary with concise expressions and clear phrases, aiming to clarify matters for those of limited understanding. This tells us the target audience and pedagogical approach.
The work is meant to be accessible, not exhaustive.
3
Recognize the Criteria for Reliability
The passage addresses a criticism: despite some weak narrations, the book is still relied upon. This shows that Hanafi scholars evaluate a text's overall utility and acceptance, not just its individual flaws.
Similar discussions occurred regarding Al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi.
4
Place It in the Tradition
Ibn Nujaym cites it as a source in Al-Bahr al-Raiq, demonstrating its acceptance among later authorities. The book also discusses Shafi'i differences, adding comparative value.
It is considered essential for anyone teaching Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
5
Observe Practical Utility
The passage highlights the author's use of examples to clarify issues, making it particularly helpful for beginners. Its moderate size makes it manageable for study.
This explains why it has been printed multiple times and remains in use.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
...and Ibn Abidin and others as they used to rely on his summary, which is Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah.
And what is said that in them there are some weak narrations and statements transmitted, this does not prevent relying on them and accepting them, and we do not make that a reason to demolish them or count them among the unreliable books in the madhhab.

57- Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah (Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri)
By Abu Bakr bin Ali bin Muhammad al-Haddad, died 800 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
And its author abridged it from his previously mentioned book: 'Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. And in the author's introduction:
... After: This is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which I compiled with concise expressions and clear phrases containing many meanings and discussions. I clarified it for those of limited understanding and modest aspirations, and I named it 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah'... End.
It has been printed in three editions and photocopied many times.
(1) Kashf al-Zunun 2/1631, and they mentioned in his biography in al-Badr al-Tali' 1/166 that he has two commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: a small one and a large one.

The first edition came in two volumes: the first in 382 pages, and the second in 420 pages, an Ottoman edition, at Mahmud Bey's printing press, near Bab al-Ali, in 1301 AH.
The second edition, with its margin 'Al-Lubab' commentary on the book by al-Maydani, also in two volumes, an Ottoman edition, at the flourishing printing house in Istanbul, in 1316 AH.
It was also printed in Delhi, India, in 1328 AH.
In all the editions there are many typographical errors.

There are many manuscripts of the book, see the index. There is also a manuscript in the Arif Hikmat Library in Medina, deposited in the King Abdulaziz Library, number (254/81) Hanafi fiqh, consisting of 244 folios, 30 lines per page, copied in 1114 AH.
And 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' is a famous, widespread book. Ibn Nujaym counted it among his sources in the introduction to al-Bahr al-Raiq. It is a commentary that cannot be dispensed with by anyone who wants to teach Mukhtasar al-Quduri, especially in terms of the examples that the author gives to depict the issue in the reader's mind.
Also, its size is moderate, and it discusses the disagreement of the Shafi'is.
(1) 3/313.

Commentary
This is a front-matter passage from a larger work (likely Al-Lubab) describing the commentary Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by Abu Bakr al-Haddad (d. 800 AH) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage explains that despite some weak narrations in the book, it remains reliable and widely accepted in the Hanafi school. It notes that similar concerns were raised about Al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi but were addressed. The author's introduction states that he wrote the commentary concisely and clearly for those of average understanding. The passage then provides bibliographic details: three printed editions (Ottoman 1301 AH, Ottoman 1316 AH with Al-Lubab in the margin, and Delhi 1328 AH), existence of manuscripts, and praise from Ibn Nujaym in Al-Bahr al-Raiq. The book is considered essential for teaching Mukhtasar al-Quduri due to its helpful examples and moderate length, and it also discusses Shafi'i differences. This passage serves to establish the authority and utility of Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu Bakr al-Haddad, known for its concise expressions and clear examples.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh matn by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH/1037 CE), widely studied in the Hanafi school.
السراج الوهاج (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): The original, larger commentary by al-Haddad from which Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah was abridged.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Al-Bahr al-Zakhir and Ibn Danishmand's Sharh
Listing and describing two important commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the purpose and content of two key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain how they contribute to the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Commentaries expand and clarify foundational texts, adding new rulings and preserving the living Hanafi tradition.

Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a core Hanafi matn that has been studied for centuries. Scholars wrote commentaries to explain its concise wording, add new cases (furu'), and note differences among Imams. This lesson introduces two such commentaries: Al-Bahr al-Zakhir and Ibn Danishmand's Sharh, giving you insight into how Hanafi scholarship builds upon its foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational concise fiqh text. Its popularity led many scholars to write commentaries (shuruh) to explain and expand it.
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is often the first complete fiqh text memorized in Hanafi curricula.
2
Examine the first commentary: Al-Bahr al-Zakhir
This is an abridgment (tajrid) of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, which itself is a commentary by al-Haddad. Al-Bahr al-Zakhir condenses the larger work into a more concise form.
The abridgment was made by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Iqbal after 800 AH.
3
Examine the second commentary: Ibn Danishmand's Sharh
This commentary by Abu 'Abd al-Rahman 'Umar ibn Danishmand, written after 800 AH, aims to clarify difficulties, detail summaries, reveal hidden aspects, and include differences among the Imams.
The author's preface explains his motivation: despite many previous commentaries, none had fully done justice to the matn.
4
Analyze the preface excerpt
Read the preface to understand the author's goals: to benefit students like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and to include reasons (ilal), meanings, needed branches (furu'), and inter-Imam differences.
This shows the purpose of a commentary: not mere repetition but real expository work.
5
Understand the chain of transmission
Recognize the progression from matn (Mukhtasar al-Quduri) to commentary (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) to abridgment (Al-Bahr al-Zakhir), and also independent commentary (Ibn Danishmand). Each step adds value: original conciseness, detailed explanation, condensed reference, or renewed commentary.
This chain exemplifies the living tradition of Hanafi scholarship.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. * His statement: 'And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He owns it by reviving [dead land]' – this is if he abandons seeking permission out of ignorance. But if he abandons it out of neglect, the Imam takes it back from him. Thus in al-Fawa'id. End quote from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. I say: By this example appear the new branches that al-Haddad added in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, which he did not mention in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. And by this the clear difference between the original and the abridgment appears. Perhaps Allah will facilitate someone to kindle this illuminating lamp, so that students of knowledge increase in light upon light. 58 – Al-Bahr al-Zakhir is an abridgment of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Haddad). It was abridged by the scholar jurist Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Iqbal. The author of Kashf al-Zunun did not mention the date of his death, but it is after 800 AH, the year of al-Haddad's death. (1). 59 – Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri. By Abu 'Abd al-Rahman 'Umar ibn Danishmand, who died after 800 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It appears from the author's preface – as will come – that it was after 800 AH because he quotes from the book 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by al-Haddad, who died in 800 AH. (1: 1631/2). A copy of this commentary exists in the 'Ashir Efendi Library in Istanbul, see al-Fihris al-Shamil (1). My noble brother, Professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya, informed me in a letter from Istanbul that there is another copy of the book in the Hafid Efendi Library in Istanbul, numbered (76), in (195) folios, which is an incomplete copy ending at the end of the chapter on forgetfulness prostrations. And in its preface, the author says: '... To proceed: The poor servant of his Rich and Great Lord, Abu 'Abd al-Rahman 'Umar ibn Danishmand – may his Lord and his parents treat him with sublime kindness – says: The book of al-Quduri has been delighted in by students and boasted about by desirous ones, until it became a mainstay among them and a pride in their gatherings. They have never ceased occupying themselves with it at every time and studying it in every place, because it is the most beautiful book in conciseness and the most comprehensive in containing the chosen fatwa. Therefore, a group of virtuous people have undertaken to explain it with clarification and to elucidate its secrets with disclosure. Yet with all this, no one has given it its due right. So I intended, at the request of some beloved friends, despite my limited capacity, to comment on it with a commentary that clarifies its difficulties, details its compendious points, reveals its hidden aspects, and benefits every needy student, like the benefit of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. I have mentioned the reasons for its issues and their meanings, and branches that are needed, and differences among the Imams...' End quote. (1: 871/0)
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic section from the book 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' that lists and describes commentaries on the foundational Hanafi matn, 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. The author first quotes a fiqh ruling from the commentary 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by al-Haddad, concerning reviving dead land: if one revives land without seeking the imam's permission due to ignorance, he owns it according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; but if he neglects to seek permission out of disdain, the imam takes it back. The author then notes that this example shows the new subsidiary rulings that al-Haddad added beyond those in 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira'. Next, he lists two commentaries: (1) 'al-Bahr al-Zakhir', an abridgment of 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Iqbal (d. after 800 AH), and (2) a commentary by Abu 'Abd al-Rahman 'Umar ibn Danishmand (d. after 800 AH). The author provides information about manuscript copies of Ibn Danishmand's commentary in Istanbul libraries, and then quotes extensively from its preface. In the preface, Ibn Danishmand praises the excellence and widespread use of al-Quduri's book, notes that many have attempted to explain it but none have done it justice, and states his intention to write a beneficial commentary that clarifies difficulties, details summaries, reveals hidden aspects, and notes differences among the Imams. This passage serves as an introduction to the various scholarly efforts in explaining and expanding upon 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational matn.
السراج الوهاج (Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Haddad (d. 800 AH), known for adding new subsidiary issues (furu').
البحر الزاخر (Al-Bahr al-Zakhir): An abridgment (tajrid) of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, made by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Iqbal.
أبو عبد الرحمن عمر بن دانشمند (Abu 'Abd al-Rahman 'Umar ibn Danishmand): A Hanafi scholar who wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri after 800 AH.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, like Al-Bahr al-Zakhir and Ibn Danishmand's Sharh, illustrate the layered nature of Hanafi scholarship: matn, commentary, abridgment, and independent works each serve distinct purposes.

Introduction and Front Matter

Decoding the Abbreviations of Jami' al-Mudmarat
Author's preface and source abbreviations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five key Hanafi commentaries abbreviated in Jami' al-Mudmarat and state their symbols.

Core Idea
Jami' al-Mudmarat uses abbreviations (Ya, Mim, Alif, Ha, Ba) to refer to five key Hanafi commentaries.

This passage introduces the author's preface and the system of abbreviations used to reference sources. You will learn the names of the main works and how to decode the symbols.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type
This is the front matter of a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author explains his use of abbreviations for frequent sources.
2
List the abbreviations
Find the five abbreviations: (Ya), (Mim), (Alif), (Ha), (Ba). For each, note the full title and author.
3
Match each abbreviation to its source
Match: (Ya) = al-Yanabi' by al-Shaybli; (Mim) = al-Manafi' by al-Nasafi; (Alif) = al-Anfa' (not specified); (Ha) = al-Hidayah; (Ba) = al-Maghrib.
Al-Anfa' is less known; the text does not elaborate.
4
Understand the scope of the commentary
The author also included chapters on fatwa, virtue of fiqh, and etiquettes of mufti. The book is a comprehensive collection of branches.
5
Review the manuscript evidence
Note the manuscripts: Topkapi (2 vols) and Medina copy. This establishes the work's transmission history.

And the rest of the books of rulings, and others for rulings, may Allah make the benefits of the springs of their branches more beneficial than the cloud of the canopy, until the smiles of hidden things appeared removing the veil, and the forms of difficult problems became a lamp in darkness, so it contained from them the essence of what he saw of their narration, even if it occurred repeatedly to quench the thirst of opinions. And he adorned the transmitted from al-Yanabi' with (Ya), and al-Manafi' with (Mim), and al-Anfa' with (Alif), and al-Hidaya with (Ha), and al-Maghrib with (Ba), for the precedence of understanding, and he named other books by their known names for information, sufficient without the need for the mentioned books for fatwa, and for this purpose. And he named it: Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat, the weakest of Allah's servants for crimes, and forgiveness for sins: Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Yusuf al-Sufi al-Kamaruzi, known as (Nubayra Shaykh Umar... end from the author's introduction. Then he mentioned after this introduction the signs indicating fatwa, as he mentioned a chapter on the virtue of fiqh and fuqaha', and on explaining the Sunnah and Jama'ah, and on who is permitted to give fatwa and who is not, and on the etiquettes of the mufti and mustafti, and whether it is permissible for a mujtahid to follow others in shar'i matters or not? All this he mentioned briefly. And the book has numerous manuscript copies, see al-Fihris al-Shamil(1), among them a copy in Topkapi Palace in Istanbul, in two volumes, the first (1) 81/3 [PAGE_450] 450 Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri of them in (231) folios, and the second in (274) folios. Also I found a copy in the 'Arif Hikmat Library in Medina, number (254/75) Hanafi fiqh, containing (336) folios, each page (37) lines, and its copying date on a night whose morning reveals Thursday, the 18th of Shawwal in the year 1177 AH. Allah facilitated its photography for me, and from it I transcribed the author's introduction, and learned about the nature and methodology of this commentary. And it appears from the volume of the commentary that its author expanded it, and from here comes the description of Imam al-Laknawi of him saying: It is a comprehensive commentary containing many branches, abundant in issues, I studied it (1). End. As for the author's sources from which he frequently quoted, he stated them in his introduction as previously mentioned, and he symbolized each, and what he did not quote much he mentioned by its name. He stated: Among his sources: 'al-Yanabi'', which is a commentary on al-Quduri, previously mentioned, and its full name: al-Yanabi' fi Ma'rifat al-Usul wa al-Tafari', by Imam Muhammad ibn Ramadan al-Shaybli al-Rumi, died 616 AH. And among his sources: 'al-Manafi'', by Imam al-Nasafi Abu al-Barakat 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad, died 710 AH, author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq (2), and it is a commentary (1) al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 230, and mentioned p. 30 that he studied it and benefited from it. Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction of the editor or compiler of the book, detailing the third chapter on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It begins with poetic praise of the benefits of the sources. The author of Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat, Yusuf ibn Umar al-Kamaruzi, used symbols for key works: (Ya) for al-Yanabi', (Mim) for al-Manafi', (Alif) for al-Anfa', (Ha) for al-Hidayah, (Ba) for al-Maghrib. Other books were named fully. The author then discusses the contents of his introduction: signs for fatwa, virtue of fiqh, definitions of Sunnah and Jama'ah, qualifications for mufti and mustafti, and whether a mujtahid may follow another. He notes manuscript copies: one in Topkapi in two volumes (231+274 folios), another in 'Arif Hikmat Library in Medina (336 folios, copied 1177 AH). The commentator praises the work's comprehensiveness, quoting al-Laknawi. Finally, he lists the author's main sources: al-Yanabi' by Muhammad al-Shaybli (d. 616 AH), and al-Manafi' by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi (d. 710 AH), author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. This passage is essential for understanding the methodology and abbreviations used in the commentary.

Key Terms
الينابيع (al-Yanabi'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam Muhammad ibn Ramadan al-Shaybli al-Rumi (d. 616 AH).
المنافع (al-Manafi'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi (d. 710 AH), author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
جامع المضمرات والمشكلات (Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat): The book being described, authored by Yusuf ibn Umar al-Kamaruzi, a comprehensive commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Sources and Description
Lists and describes commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri mentioned by al-Maydani and explain their methodological focus and interrelationships.

Core Idea
The Hanafi tradition is preserved through a chain of commentaries that refine and expand upon foundational texts.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by al-Maydani provides a bibliographical overview of the most important commentaries on the foundational Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding these commentaries is crucial for tracing the development of Hanafi fiqh and identifying authoritative sources for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main commentaries listed
Scan the passage and list all commentary titles and their authors mentioned. Note the author's name and death date for each.
The commentaries include al-Nafi', al-Anfa', al-Hidayah, al-Mughrib, Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat, and a gloss by al-Fanari.
2
Trace the chain of sources
Observe how al-Maydani notes that one commentary (al-Nafi') itself cites earlier works (al-Anfa', al-Hidayah, al-Mughrib). This illustrates the layered nature of Hanafi scholarship.
Al-Nafi' is a commentary that draws on earlier commentaries, creating a chain of authority.
3
Analyze the methodology of Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat
Read the description of this commentary. It presents intra-madhhab disagreements, scrutinizes narrations, and mentions views of Malikis and Shafi'is. Note that it focuses on furu' and mufta bihi, not expanding on proofs.
This commentary is valuable for understanding nuanced positions within the Hanafi school and comparative fiqh.
4
Understand the role of glosses (hashiyah)
The passage ends with al-Fanari's gloss on his own commentary. Glosses were written to clarify difficult expressions and are part of the living tradition of commentary.
Al-Fanari's work shows how later scholars refined earlier commentaries.

For the book: 'al-Nafi'' which is a blessed summary in the branches of the Hanafi school, by Imam Nasir al-Din Abi al-Qasim Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Hasani al-Madani al-Samarqandi, died 656 AH (1).
And among its sources mentioned in its introduction: 'al-Anfa'' intended, and Allah knows best, as 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il ila Tahrir al-Masa'il' by Imam Burhan al-Din Susi Ibrahim ibn Ali, died 758 AH, which is a summary of al-Tarab? Nafi' (2)
6
And among its sources: 'al-Hidayah', which is a very famous book, by Imam al-Marghinani Ali ibn Abi Bakr, died 593 AH.
6
And among its sources: 'al-Mughrib', which is on the language of Hanafi jurists, by Imam al-Mutarrizi Abi al-Fath Nasir ibn Abd al-Sayyid, died 610 AH, and he named it 'al-Mughrib fi Tartib al-Mughrib' (3).
Thus, the book 'Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat' is an extensive commentary, and it presents the disagreements of the imams of the school at length, and it scrutinizes the authenticity and provenness of narrations, transmitted from the imams of the school, as it also mentions the disagreements of the Malikis and Shafi'is.
(1) Kashf al-Zunun 2/1921.
(2) Kashf al-Zunun 1/183.
(3) See Kashf al-Zunun 2/1747, Taj al-Tarajim p. 309.

452
Chapter Three: Commentaries of
Quduri
As for evidences, it does not expand on mentioning them, but rather it is very concerned with mentioning the legal issues and subsidiary branches of fiqh, just as it is concerned with mentioning the mufta bihi in the school, and it transmits what the scholars of that school mentioned of their preponderations and their disagreements therein.
Thus, the publication of this commentary is very beneficial in knowing the rulings of these precise subsidiary branches, and the book becomes a support, indeed a foundation, for whoever wishes to attend to this aspect. And Allah knows best.
62 – Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
By the scholar Mahmud ibn Pir Muhammad al-Fanari, died 839 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
A copy of it is in the Sulaymaniyya Library, Rashid Efendi (186), in 69 folios, in the author's handwriting.
In the author's introduction it says:
'When I saw that some expressions of my commentary which I authored for the Book of Taharah of al-Quduri needed clarification at first glance, I wanted to write a gloss on it to uncover its difficulties... The book was completed by the poor servant Mahmud ibn Pir Muhammad al-Fanari, may Allah forgive both of them...' (1) end.
(1) As written to me from Istanbul by the brother, the professor Muhammad Fatih Qaya.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical section from the work 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani, here discussing the third chapter of the book which lists commentaries on the famous Hanafi text 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. The author first mentions the book 'al-Nafi'' by al-Samarqandi (d. 656 AH), a concise work on Hanafi furu'. He then notes its source 'al-Anfa'' (likely 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il') by Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Susi (d. 758 AH). Other sources include 'al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) and 'al-Mughrib' by al-Mutarrizi (d. 610 AH), the latter being a lexical work specific to Hanafi jurisprudence. The passage then describes the commentary 'Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat' as a broad commentary that presents intra-madhhab disagreements and critically examines narrations, also mentioning differences with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools. It notes that this commentary focuses on legal issues and branches (furu') rather than expanding on proofs (adillah), and gives weight to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school. Finally, the author mentions another commentary by Mahmud ibn Pir Muhammad al-Fanari (d. 839 AH), providing manuscript details and quoting its introduction where al-Fanari explains his motivation to write a gloss (hashiyah) on his own commentary on the Book of Taharah of al-Quduri. This excerpt serves as a bibliographical survey, establishing the lineage and methodology of key Hanafi commentaries on al-Quduri's foundational text.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text in the Hanafi school covering furu' al-fiqh.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A famous Hanafi legal manual by al-Marghinani, often used as a reference for fatwa.
المغرب (al-Mughrib): A lexical work focusing on the language used by Hanafi jurists, by al-Mutarrizi.
حاشية (Hashiyah): A gloss or supercommentary, written to clarify or expand upon a primary commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) al-Hidayah
C) Jami' al-Mudmarat wa al-Mushkilat
D) al-Mughrib

Key Takeaway
The commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri form a scholarly chain that preserves and nuances Hanafi fiqh rulings, with each work serving a distinct purpose in the tradition.
